
Chapter 6: The Handsome Bystander in the Comeback Novel (5)


On a weekend morning, a BMW pulled up smoothly at the entrance of the Lijiang residential complex.

Fang Chenxu rolled down the window, greeted the security guard, and drove in.

Zhang Xia sat in the passenger seat, her hands on her lap, making no particular movements, but her fingers were clenched tightly.

Fang Chenxu noticed this out of the corner of his eye, but didn't say anything. He simply took his hand off the steering wheel and gently placed it on the back of her hand. "Relax, it's not like you're going for a job interview."

"I know."

Zhang Xia responded, her tone suggesting she wasn't nervous, but a slight tension lingered on her face.

Fang Chenxu parked the car, and the two got out, walking side-by-side towards apartment building number 9.

Both were dressed smartly today. Zhang Xia wore a light-colored knitted cardigan, her hair tied up, making her look significantly younger than her actual age, like a fresh-faced teacher. Fang Chenxu, on the other hand, had changed his suit into a casual jacket, but the refined air he cultivated over the years was still undeniable; he remained composed and confident.

The two walked together, a truly handsome couple.

As they walked, they encountered the elderly folks walking their dogs in the building. Some acquaintances would ask,

"Xiaoxia! You're back to see your dad?"

Zhang Xia handled these greetings with ease and grace.

In the elevator, Zhang Xia stared blankly at the floor numbers.

Fang Chenxu leaned against the elevator wall, recalling the absurdity of the whole affair—

It was he who first had the idea.

He first heard from his father's side that his father-in-law had taken in a child. He had only casually asked how old the child was, and they said one or two months old.

One or two months old.

The thought, like a seed planted in the ground, took root and was difficult to uproot.

When they knew they could only keep one child, they considered adopting another, but Xiuxiu's health was poor, and the idea gradually faded.

But now, Xiuxiu's health has improved, and another child of similar age has appeared.

He mentioned it to Zhang Xia, expecting some persuasion, but Zhang Xia was faster than him. Before he could even finish speaking, she was already picking up her phone to call Chen Cuixia, saying she needed to talk to her mother first.

Fine.

Before he could even put in a move, his wife ran out.

Then there was his own problem—his biggest worry was his parents' reaction. He was their only son, and the child wasn't their own; he feared his parents would harbor resentment, even if they didn't say it aloud.

Then his father revealed a secret.

He said that he himself had also been adopted by his grandfather.

Fang Chenxu's expression immediately cracked. He sat at the dinner table, stunned for almost ten seconds without replying. His mother added from the side, "This isn't a joke, it's true. Your grandfather that year..."

Okay, okay, it's true, I believe you.

The family meeting lasted less than half an hour, and unanimously approved welcoming the new member.

After finishing his work at the company, he and Zhang Xia were "rushed" over. Xiuxiu was left with his mother, who said they should come here to build a relationship with the child first.

Fang Chenxu finished replying in the elevator, unable to help but sigh inwardly—he wanted to adopt, but everyone in his family was more enthusiastic than him. His parents even brought up their deepest secrets, afraid he might have reservations about the child.

Where can you reason with this?

Now he can't even say no (||●'◡'●)))

The elevator arrived.

Reaching the door, Fang Chenxu raised his hand and knocked three times.

Footsteps sounded quickly from inside, as if they had been waiting.

The door opened, and Zhang Jianguo stood there. Seeing his daughter and son-in-law, his smile was barely contained. "Coming, coming in!"

He stepped aside to make way, his voice carrying a cheerful edge he never showed when he lost a game of chess.

Fang Chenxu stepped over the threshold, greeted Zhang Jianguo, exchanged a few polite words, and Zhang Jianguo pulled him towards the living room, asking if he wanted tea or water, and briefly recounting the investigation into Fang Yuan over the past few days.

He was an abandoned baby; no one had reported it, but people at the hospital had inquired, and many expressed interest in adopting Fang Yuan, but Zhang Jianguo had turned them all down.

Zhang Xia changed her shoes faster than Fang Chenxu, and went straight inside.

Chen Cuixia was already standing by the crib. Turning around and seeing her daughter arrive, she pointed, "You're just in time. He just finished eating and fell asleep."

Zhang Xia walked over and looked down. Inside the crib, Fang Yuan slept soundly, his fists half-clenched, a hint of that indescribable contentment on his lips, his eyelashes lowered, his face round and without any sharp edges.

Zhang Xia's breathing quickened. Chen Cuixia leaned closer and whispered, "Isn't he handsome? The nurses at the hospital all said they'd never seen him before. Some even thought he was mixed race, like a little girl."

Zhang Xia didn't answer, just looked at him.

*This is my son.*

This thought popped into her head unexpectedly; her heart felt like it had been gently bumped.

Fang Yuan, on the other hand, vaguely sensed a new presence beside him.

A new scent appeared, not Chen Cuixia's baby formula, nor Zhang Jianguo's shaving cream, but something else—a faint, fresh scent with a hint of laundry detergent.

It must be her.

Fang Yuan thought to himself, but had no intention of opening his eyes and pretending to be asleep.

However, his body wouldn't cooperate. Whether he'd had enough sleep or sensed the newcomer's presence, his eyelids twitched on their own, slowly opening a crack.

Zhang Xia was standing directly above him.

The two stared at each other for two seconds.

Zhang Xia froze, not moving.

Fang Yuan opened his eyes, glanced around, his gaze returning to Zhang Xia's face. A grin spread across his face, and he reached his hand out from under the covers, waving it.

"Mom!"

Zhang Xia couldn't help herself and nudged Chen Cuixia's arm. "He's awake! Look at him!"

Zhang Xia slowly came to her senses, leaned down, and held out a finger, gently waving it in front of Fang Yuan. "Hey—"

Her voice was unusually soft, completely different from her usual tone.

Fang Yuan stared at the finger. A voice in his head told him to stay calm, to stay composed, but his hand had already acted—his chubby five fingers lunged forward and grabbed the finger.

He held on tight.

Then he put it in his mouth.

"Ha—" Chen Cuixia laughed beside him. "Look, look, he grabbed someone's hand!"

Zhang Jianguo and Fang Chenxu also came over. Fang Chenxu had just peeked over when he saw this scene, and the corners of his mouth turned up, managing to restrain himself fairly well.

Laughter from the others followed, and the living room became lively.

Only Zhang Xia remained silent.

She kept her head down, Fang Yuan's hand still gripping her fingers, the strength not great, but firm, as if he had no intention of letting go.

The thing that had been weighing on her heart ever since the car accident quietly loosened at this moment.

Her eyes welled up, but she kept her head down, not letting anyone see.

"Ugh..."

The sound wasn't completely suppressed, a soft groan, half-buried by Fang Yuan's timely "sigh."

Chen Cuixia still heard it. Turning her head, she saw her daughter with her head down, her shoulders trembling slightly. She understood. Without speaking, she gently placed her hand on her daughter's.

Zhang Xia felt the child from the car accident return to her side. For a moment, she couldn't control her emotions; her eyes instantly reddened.

"My son is back."

Her voice was soft, as if speaking to herself, and also as if speaking to Fang Yuan.



Chapter 7: The Handsome Bystander in the Comeback Story (6)


The ephemeral mushroom knows not the cycle of day and night, the cicada knows not the seasons.

Afternoon sunlight filters through the leaves, casting dappled golden light on the path in the courtyard, lined with colorful flowers and plants.

Wandering through the campus, there weren't many students.

Fang Yuan glanced at his phone; it was 2:20, ten minutes until class.

The girl with the ponytail ahead of him walked quickly, and the pink bear charm hanging from her bag fell to the ground with a thud, bounced twice, and rolled to Fang Yuan's feet.

Fang Yuan bent down to pick it up. "You dropped something."

The girl turned around and looked at Fang Yuan.

She had almond-shaped eyes, double eyelids, a high nose bridge, and skin so white it looked like it had never been in the sun; her features were strikingly defined.

The girl paused for two seconds, a blush rising to her cheeks. She reached out and took the keychain, her voice slightly trembling, "Th-thank you! I waited so long to get this, I almost lost it."

As she spoke, her gaze couldn't help but drift towards Fang Yuan's face.

The school uniform was clearly the same style, but on Fang Yuan, it somehow exuded a sense of sophistication. Broad shoulders, narrow waist, and an upright posture—clearly the kind of person who exercised regularly.

Handsome and dashing, a picture of elegance and grace—that was the epitome of that.

"Um, I don't know if you..."

The girl opened her mouth, wanting to say something more.

"Be careful next time, don't drop it again."

Fang Yuan left with those words, turning and walking away.

His steps were neither fast nor slow, his back straight, as he rounded the corner of the path and disappeared from sight a few seconds later.

The girl remained with her outstretched hand, watching his retreating figure until he was completely out of sight before she looked away.

"Oh dear, Xin Xin, come out honestly!"

Two people suddenly appeared behind her. The short-haired girl nudged her arm with her shoulder, winking mischievously. "Who was that ridiculously handsome guy just now? When did you meet him? You've been keeping it a secret for a while!"

The girl called Xin Xin blushed instantly, stubbornly replying, "It's not what you think! He's just a kind classmate!"

"A kind classmate?" The short-haired girl laughed even harder, reaching out to tickle Xin Xin's waist. "Why are you blushing? Tell me! Have you known him for a while?"

"Really, no!"

The two girls playfully wrestled on the path. Xin Xin, unable to bear the tickling, begged for mercy.

"Alright, alright, stop it."

A girl wearing glasses, who looked rather quiet, spoke up, adjusting her glasses. Her tone was calm. "That guy seemed pretty impressive."

Upon hearing this, the two girls immediately stopped playing and turned around in unison.

"What do you mean?" The short-haired girl's eyes lit up. "You know him?"

The quiet girl nodded. "I've met him a few times. His name is Fang Yuan. His family is quite wealthy, and he's very talented. He's good at painting and sports too."

"How talented?"

"I saw him at the art school I attend." The quiet girl paused. "Once, it was raining, and he arrived in a Maybach. Someone even held an umbrella for him when he got out. I was curious and asked a senior student at the school. She said that the school is owned by his family, and Fang Yuan is very skilled. He even taught her a basic course before."

"Holy crap?" The short-haired girl's eyes widened. "That amazing?"

"Not just that," another girl spoke up, lowering her voice, "I was playing in the park before, and I passed by a secluded alleyway. I saw him come out of it. I peeked inside out of curiosity, and there were seven or eight thugs lying there, their faces bruised and swollen."

The air was silent for two seconds.

"Wow..." the short-haired girl gasped, "What kind of ideal type is this? Rich, handsome, talented, and a fighter?"

"A god!"

"Xin Xin, you've hit the jackpot!"

Xin Xin blushed even more, lowering her head and waving her hands, "I really don't know him well..."

The chatter of several girls carried on the wind to Fang Yuan's ears, who was strolling leisurely not far away.

Things seem to be getting a little strange.

Fang Yuan sighed inwardly.

Isn't my identity just an ordinary high school student? How come there are so many messy settings?

Maybach, institution, fight… what does this all have to do with anything?

Fang Yuan rubbed his temples and continued walking towards the teaching building.

It's his first time being human, and he's a little unaccustomed to it. This is his first time in this kind of situation, and he doesn't know what to do.

Two difficult things happening together make it even more difficult!

More than ten years have passed since he was adopted by Fang Chenxu and his wife.

In these ten years, Fang Yuan's quality of life has improved dramatically.

Fang Chenxu and Zhang Xia truly treat Fang Yuan like their own son. Both families have kept the fact that Fang Yuan was adopted a secret. The moment Fang Chenxu received the adoption certificate, he locked it in a safe, afraid that Fang Yuan might see it and it would affect his development.

The love and pampering Fang Yuan from both families can only be described as heartfelt.

They've given him almost everything they could to help him.

Zhang Xia even considered getting Fang Yuan a Hong Kong and Macau ID card so he wouldn't have to compete with mainland students in the college entrance exam and could live a happy life.

This idea was stopped by Zhang Jianguo.

The old man said it would affect Fang Yuan's future development, so Zhang Xia gave up the idea.

To be honest, these past ten years have been quite comfortable.

Both families treat each other sincerely, and Fang Yuan isn't ungrateful. Although he's a bit slow, he calls his parents "Mom and Dad" when appropriate, and he's considerate in all social interactions.

The only problem is—

System 120 isn't always around.

Fang Yuan pushed open the classroom door and walked to his seat.

The sunlight outside the window was perfect, shining warmly on the desk.

Fang Yuan rested his chin on his hand, his mind swirling with those thoughts that had replayed in his head countless times.

System 120 had said it would ask the teacher, but that question had lasted for three years. The first time it was assigned to him in the first year made him incredibly guilty.

Fang Yuan had tried calling out to him, but each time it was like throwing a stone into the sea—no response whatsoever.

Later, whether by chance or some other reason,

after adopting him, the Fang family's company suddenly began to prosper. In just over a decade, it transformed from a small-to-medium-sized enterprise with assets of less than ten million yuan, unable to even break into the market, into a city-level leader, its reputation known throughout the industry.

Of course, with such success comes those who are desperate and prone to malpractice. The Fang family only had two children, and Fang Yuan was their only son, so the first few years were rather chaotic, with Fang Yuan's situation being quite dramatic.

Fortunately, the protective skills left by System 120 were still intact, and Fang Yuan had encountered virtually no danger in the past decade or so.

But the problem was—

Fang Yuan had absolutely no idea what kind of world this was.

Although he had undergone some training, listening and observing were never as effective as walking.

When he first transmigrated, Fang Yuan was just an infant, unable to see or understand anything, and could only barely manage with the survival manual left by System 120.

As he grew older and began to access information from the outside world, Fang Yuan discovered that this world seemed quite different from the Xiya Continent of his previous life. According to the space manual, this world was a technologically advanced society, quite developed, with mobile phones and internet access.

And then there was—

Fang Yuan looked down at his hands.

From the perspective of the people of this world, this body…

How to put it? Based on his observation, this body was quite extraordinary.

No matter what he learned, he mastered it incredibly quickly.

Painting, music, sports—if Fang Yuan wanted to learn something, there was basically nothing he couldn't learn.

Of course, what he could achieve depended on himself.

At first, Fang Yuan thought it was the protective skill left by System 120 that was working, but later he realized that wasn't right—the protective skill was only for survival, not for talent enhancement.

So, the only remaining possibility was

this body itself was not simple.

Fang Yuan frowned slightly at this thought.

Thinking back to how he was almost mistaken for an intellectually disabled person, he still felt a sense of unease.

At that time, Fang Yuan was almost three years old and hadn't spoken a word.

It wasn't that he couldn't speak, but that he was afraid to.

Fang Yuan didn't know the language habits of this world and was afraid of giving himself away if he opened his mouth, so he could only pretend to be mute, saying some simple words.

Like "drink water," "go to the toilet," "eat," etc.

This drove Zhang Xia crazy, and she took Fang Yuan directly to Peking Union Medical College Hospital for a checkup.

Given Fang Yuan's behavior at the time, he was a genius on one hand and a madman on the other, his life hanging by a thread. Giving him a diagnosis of mild intellectual disability was already being kind.

Some other families might have even put him in a mental hospital.

Just at this crucial moment, System 120 made its dazzling appearance.

System 120 helped Fang Yuan answer all the doctor's questions, ultimately earning him the assessment of being intelligent but introverted, which reassured both families.

Afterwards, System 120 taught Fang Yuan the language habits and basic common sense of this world, allowing him to officially begin living a normal life. After mentioning where he would go to high school and interacting with the protagonist, System 120 didn't appear again.

"Brother Fang."

Someone called out from beside him.

Fang Yuan snapped out of his reverie and turned to look.

His deskmate, a boy wearing glasses, pushed up his glasses and whispered, "What are you daydreaming about? Class is about to start."

"Nothing." Fang Yuan waved his hand, "Thinking about something."

"Oh." His deskmate nodded, not asking any further questions, and lowered his head to flip through his textbook.

Fang Yuan also took out his textbook and turned to the page they were going to cover today.

Physics, electromagnetic induction.

Fang Yuan glanced at the content; he knew most of it.

It wasn't that he had previewed it; he had memorized it after just one look.

He felt this was the body's innate talent; otherwise, how could an ordinary plant like him possess such abilities?

Fang Yuan closed the book and leaned back in his chair.

The current situation is that System 120 is nowhere to be found, and Fang Yuan is completely clueless about the ins and outs of this world, so he can only proceed cautiously.

According to the early plot synopsis, this world should be an ordinary one, even the protagonist's rise to power was purely by chance.

However, he only had a brief appearance in the early plot, just a single line of dialogue, and System 120 didn't give him much screen time.

Fortunately, both families are normal people, without any messy conspiracies or schemes, and Fang Yuan has lived a relatively peaceful life for the past ten years or so.

As for what those girls mentioned earlier about the Maybach, the institution, and the fight…

Fang Yuan thought about it, and it seemed there was some truth to it.

The Maybach was bought by Fang Chenxu, and the family does indeed send a driver to pick up and drop off Fang Yuan regularly.

The institution was an art institution that Zhang Xia opened with Fang Chenxu's money to help take care of their two children. Fang Yuan did study painting there as a child, and his skill level was indeed quite good. Some past memories resurfaced, allowing him to observe the world from a plant-like perspective. This novel perspective led him to win numerous awards in competitions, and his family's institution established a firm foothold in the education sector.

As for the fight—

Fang Yuan stroked his chin.

That time, he was passing by a park when he saw some thugs extorting money from students. Fang Yuan couldn't stand it and went to help.

But for some reason, those thugs were as fragile as paper. Fang Yuan just shoved them a few times, and they were all lying on the ground.

Fang Yuan was puzzled at the time, thinking it was the protective skill left by System 120 at work.

Otherwise, his body was just that of an ordinary person. Although he exercised, this level of strength was still exaggerated.

Fang Yuan sighed.

The school bell rang.

The physics teacher walked into the classroom carrying a stack of test papers, placed them on the podium, and said expressionlessly, "Last week's test papers are graded. Distribute them now."

A groan erupted in the classroom.

"I bombed the test again..."

"Oh no, my mom's going to kill me when I get home."

"Physics is so hard, I just can't learn it."

The test papers were handed out quickly.

His deskmate received his paper, glanced at the score, and his face fell.

Fang Yuan glanced at it: 72.

"Not bad," Fang Yuan comforted him.

"Not bad my foot!" his deskmate said with a bitter face. "My dad said if I get below 80 this time, I can't play games."

"That's terrible."

"What about you?" his deskmate leaned closer. "How much did you get?"

Fang Yuan opened his test paper and looked at the number in the upper right corner.

80, 80, still 80.

Fang Yuan expressionlessly slammed the test paper face down on the table.

His deskmate saw this, paused for two seconds, and said quietly, "You're so boring."

"You'll get used to it."

Fang Yuan leaned back in his chair, his gaze fixed on the window.

The sky was blue, the clouds were white, and the sun shone brightly.

Everything seemed normal.

But Fang Yuan felt that there was something he didn't know about this world.

What exactly was System 120 doing?

What kind of world was this?

Where did Fang Yuan's body's talent come from?

These questions remained unanswered.

Fang Yuan closed his eyes and took a deep breath.

Oh well, he'd just have to take it one step at a time.

Anyway, life was pretty good for now, both families genuinely loved Fang Yuan, and he didn't need to worry about survival.

As for the rest—

"System 120 will be back soon,"

...

"I'll leave today's cleaning duties to you."

A few arrogant boys spoke to a boy with long hair that reached his eyebrows.

"I, I... I didn't..."

Gu Shaoming stammered, wanting to refuse, but seeing the boys' expressions, he didn't dare to speak.

"Do your own work! Don't bother them!"

A pretty girl with a high ponytail came out from behind the door, pointing at the boys.

"Class... Class monitor."

Seeing the girl who came out to speak for him, Gu Shaoming didn't know what to say, only managing a blank utterance.

Hearing the girl with the high ponytail speak, the boys exchanged glances, looking at her with somewhat fawning eyes, and quickly said,

"The class monitor is right. Do your own thing. We were just joking around with Gu."

Seeing their disdainful looks, Gu Shaoming's anger rose. Just as he was about to say something, his phone rang.

The caller ID showed "Auntie." Gu Shaoming didn't dare delay and answered immediately, followed by a torrent of yelling:

"Gu Shaoming, you freeloader, come back right now! The toilet's broken. Remember to bring a toilet seat, and a book for your brother too!"

Before Gu Shaoming could react, the phone went dead.

Gu Shaoming put his phone back in his pocket and looked up to see the girl with the high ponytail looking at him pitifully, while the other arrogant boys' disdain deepened.

Seeing the pitying look in the girl's eyes, the anger that had just risen in Gu Shaoming vanished like a kite with a broken string.

"Thank you, class monitor. If there's nothing else, I'll head back now. My aunt is waiting for me."

After saying this, Gu Shaoming didn't look at the girl's sympathetic eyes. He simply lowered his head and left the classroom, his departing figure looking as forlorn as a homeless stray dog.



Chapter 8: The Handsome Guy Who Came From the Side in the Counterattack Novel (7)


Gu Shaoming left.

Behind him stood the proud, fiery Su Wanqiu.

Unlike her name, which contained the character "Wan," Su Wanqiu's personality was anything but gentle. Instead, it possessed the ruthless sharpness of the character "Qiu," aggressive as fire, swift as the wind. She stood there, her back as straight as a spear driven into the ground, her eyes brimming with undisguised arrogance, bright and almost scorching.

The emotions of a young man always come and go quickly. Just moments ago, he had roared like a dragon, his chest burning with a feverish intensity, feeling that the impending hell was nothing more than death. But his aunt's phone call, like a warrior's sword, pierced through all his bravado.

It shattered his sense of honor, showing him that he was neither the martial saint who calmly slew Hua Xiong, nor the Hua Xiong who challenged him at Hulao Pass; he was merely a lowly soldier by the roadside with only a wooden stick in his hand.

On the way back, even near dusk, the summer temperature still carried a hint of heat.

Watching the cars go by on the way home, he had fantasized. He imagined a cool luxury car slowly pulling up to the side of the road as he walked alone, the window rolling down to reveal two faces he'd only ever seen in photos, telling him that his family was stewing his favorite pork ribs, and that they would never leave again.

More often than not, he stared blankly out the window during class. He watched the clouds slowly drift across the rooftops of the school buildings, watched the leaves of the plane trees change from green to yellow and then back to green. Then he imagined the world suddenly changing—the sky cracking open, the earth shaking, and he being chosen. Like Shinji Ikari in *Neon Genesis Evangelion*, that cowardly, escapist boy who was forced to sit in the cockpit.

He struggled, he hesitated, but he never gave up.

But these were all just fantasies.

However, the horn of a classmate's parent's car reminded him that he needed to buy the toilet seat and novel his aunt had mentioned.

"You brat, you've been fighting again!"

"Dad, I didn't!"

A middle-aged man, pulling a boy with a slight bruise on his lip, questioned him.

The boy complained.

Amidst the scuffle, a girl walked out of the school gate. From his angle, he saw the boy's gaze drift towards her. The girl also saw the boy, and in that instant of eye contact, even Gu Ming, who had nothing, felt a silent affection between them.

He couldn't help but think of that proud and spoiled little princess.

But the boy's feelings remained unspoken, drowned by youthful inferiority after just one glance.

She came from a wealthy family, drove a Mercedes that even ordinary people knew was expensive, had a butler with white gloves holding an umbrella for her, and owned a car with a three-zero engine—she was a proud swan, living a proud and carefree life like a princess in a fairy tale.

As for him, he only wore a faded school uniform, and his meager allowance was earned by helping his aunt hold his legs. It was all absurd for a toad to dream of eating swan meat. Whenever he saw that bright and sunny princess, a warm feeling would rise in Gu Shaoming's heart, but it would be followed by feelings of inferiority. Living under someone else's roof was not easy. His life would be unbearable in the eyes of ordinary people, but for an orphan, it was already good enough to not lack food and clothing and to live under someone else's roof. He could even get into a good high school by relying on others.

Gu Ming's grades were good, but only good. His essays were particularly good. In the first-year high school monthly exam, the essay topic was "The Past." He felt that the past was like smoke—those four words were heavy. At first glance, he thought it was just another literary invention, sounding melodramatic. But upon closer examination, it was as bitter as poison. The human body has a protective mechanism; recalling the past first brings to mind sweet moments, but clinging to that sweetness, reaching out to grasp it, causes it to dissipate, revealing the stark reality, like being force-fed a cup of poison.

Whether it moved the teacher or the judge was a compassionate person, the essay received 58 points, ranking first, making him quite proud.

Frankly, he didn't like those works by famous authors that were supposedly classics. They all felt to Gu Ming like bitter, resentful things, astringent like traditional Chinese medicine. He preferred fantasy novels, those stories of flying, magical beings, and demons—like cheap, affordable soda from a convenience store.

Of course, the fact that you can buy over a million words for just a few dozen yuan is also a significant advantage.

After seeing the father and son fall silent and return to their car, Gu Changming's sharp eyes noticed that the father, while seemingly checking the road and starting the car, was actually secretly glancing in the direction of the girl who had just made eye contact with the boy.

However, this had nothing to do with him, a stranger who was relying on someone else and was going to buy a toilet seat to get something for them.

Oh well, it's not too late. I'll save some money by buying things and then go to an internet cafe later.

…

The school bell rang throughout the campus on Friday, and the gates of Shihnan Middle School slowly opened.

As a renowned private high school in the area, it attracts the best students—and, of course, the wealthiest and most influential families. The school gate was instantly filled with luxury cars of all kinds; Mercedes-Benz and BMWs were commonplace, and Rolls-Royces and Bentleys were frequently seen. The entire street seemed to have been transformed into a luxury car showroom, with parents' cars pouring in from all directions, completely blocking the once-wide road.

Fang Yuan stepped out of the school building, one of them.

But unlike those families that were simply wealthy, the Fang family now held considerable prestige in the education sector. His mother, Zhang Xia, owned the Tianxiu Training Center, a leader in the industry, and his father, Fang Chenxu, held shares in Shihnan Middle School and was one of its board members. This special status gave Fang Yuan unimaginable privileges at the school.

In fact, for Fang Yuan, Friday classes were largely unnecessary.

If he hadn't clearly remembered that this school was the one the "original protagonist's" school, he wouldn't even be here. Given his mother Zhang Xia's personality, having him enroll at Shi Nan Middle School and study at home would have been the standard procedure.

Since his paintings gained some recognition in international competitions, single-handedly supporting his mother's training center and allowing Tianxiu to establish himself, Fang Chenxu expanded his investment scope. He not only turned the institution into a chain brand but also directly invested in Shi Nan Middle School—this was Fang Yuan's suggestion; he had a "special fondness" for this school.

Without hesitation, Fang Chenxu paid for shares, became a director, and even built an art building at Shi Nan Middle School, reserving the top floor specifically for Fang Yuan's use.

Thus, Fang Yuan possessed near-absolute autonomy at the school. His unconventional behavior was seen by outsiders as the privileges and eccentricities of a genius.

After the last class, Fang Yuan walked straight out of the school gate; his family's driver was already waiting.

Just as he got into the car, Zhang Xia called: "Please stop by Tianxiu Training Center on your way and pick up your sister."

The Maybach weaved through traffic, stopping a moment later in front of the training center.

The car door slowly opened, and the first thing that caught the eye was a pair of long, straight legs.

Fang Yuan stood at the entrance of the training center, tall and slender.

He wore a black autumn jacket, sharply tailored; black trousers, the cuffs perfectly straight; and white sneakers—simple yet sophisticated. The entire outfit was understated and restrained, yet exuded an undeniable aura of coldness.

His facial features were sharp and defined, his black hair unruly, and his jawline sharply defined. He was like a blade covered in ice, silent and taciturn, radiating an innate aloofness and indifference, as if possessing an aura of "keep away."

Even in this art training center teeming with beautiful women, he remained the most dazzling focus.

"Hey! You brat, I'm here!"

Fang Xiuxiu's voice came from the crowd.

Over a decade had passed, and Fang Xiuxiu's transformation was equally astonishing. Now, she had blossomed into a graceful and poised young woman, inheriting the excellent genes of Zhang Xia and Fang Chenxu. Coupled with the long-term influence of dance and art training, she stood out remarkably in the crowd.

"Hey kid, why are you dressed so smartly?" Fang Xiuxiu looked at the girls surrounding Fang Yuan—each one dressed in a fitted dress after dance practice, their eyes burning with desire.

An ordinary boy would probably have been completely flustered. This scene could only be described as a "storm of butterflies."

But Fang Yuan simply stood there, his expression indifferent, as if all the commotion was irrelevant to him.

His expression was indifferent, his gaze level, as if all the noise and heat were blocked out by a layer of transparent ice surrounding him. He wasn't feigning composure; he was genuinely unmoved.

But he certainly had the right to be.

Surrounded by so many youthful and beautiful faces, he was the first one that caught the eye. Not because he was the only male, but because his aura was on a completely different level from everyone else. The girls around him, no matter how pretty, were merely the tangible, real-world kind of beauty.

But Fang Yuan, standing there, seemed like a character straight out of an otome game—his lines, his light and shadow, his proportions, every detail meticulously and coldly designed, separated from his surroundings by a thin, insurmountable dimensional barrier.

Seeing Fang Xiuxiu approach, Fang Yuan called out,

"Sister."



Chapter 9: The Handsome Bystander in the Counterattack Novel (8)


The setting sun cast a long shadow of Fang Yuan at the entrance of the training center.

He was surrounded by a throng of women, their fragrance intoxicating, their laughter filling the air. Some were shy, some bold, some playing hard to get, each with a predatory glint in their eyes. Fang Yuan stood in the center, a polite yet aloof smile on his handsome face.

It wasn't a confrontational atmosphere; it felt like a butterfly caught in a swarm of bees. He knew the bees wouldn't kill him, but instinct told him that getting too close to these women was no good.

Both for him and for the women around him, he had a vague feeling that getting too close was unwise.

Just then, out of the corner of his eye, Fang Yuan caught a glimpse of a familiar figure.

Fang Xiuxiu emerged from the training center, her long hair cascading down her back, her waist slender, and her long legs, honed through years of dance training, standing out in the crowd. She wore simple jeans and a white T-shirt, yet even amidst the throng of beautiful women at the entrance, she still attracted attention.

"Sister!" Fang Yuan blurted out, his voice tinged with urgency.

Hearing the voice, Fang Xiuxiu paused slightly, her gaze sweeping over the group of women before returning to her younger brother. She made a subtle movement—shifting her gaze, pretending not to hear.

But after more than ten years, Fang Yuan knew his Fang Xiuxiu all too well.

"Sister!" he raised his voice, a hint of pleading in his tone,

"Mom's home today, and Grandpa and Grandma are here too."

The effect of those words was immediate.

Fang Xiuxiu's expression instantly shifted from "I didn't hear you" to "It's time to go back." She walked gracefully and firmly in her high heels, heading straight for Fang Yuan.

The girls surrounding Fang Yuan felt a powerful aura emanating from him.

"Girls, it's time for the handsome guy to go back for dinner," Fang Xiuxiu's voice was clear and firm, carrying an undeniable tone. "Let's talk again next time."

These words were like a spell; the girls who knew her identity obediently dispersed. Before leaving, they didn't forget to blow Fang Yuan a kiss, leaving behind ambiguous smiles and a "Little brother, I'm off now, see you next time."

Among them, the most eye-catching was a girl with long, dyed blonde hair, a bright face, and a slender figure, walking confidently arm-in-arm with her companion. As she passed Fang Yuan, she glanced at him out of the corner of her eye, her eyes filled with a mixture of scrutiny and smugness.

Fang Yuan watched the girls' departing figures and secretly breathed a sigh of relief.

Although these girls posed less of a threat to him than a cat or dog, his subconscious kept warning him—it was best not to make any rash moves; if something went wrong, he'd be in for a world of trouble. Those flying kisses, flirtatious glances, and almost imperceptible touches all felt like carefully woven traps.

Fang Xiuxiu stood beside him, watching the girls walk away, then turned and nudged Fang Yuan's waist with her elbow.

"Yuan Yuan," she said, her tone a mix of teasing and curiosity, "out of all these girls, didn't you fall for any of them?"

The question seemed joking, but Fang Xiuxiu was genuinely curious.

Fang Yuan has never lacked female attention since childhood. He's genuinely handsome, exceptionally capable, and comes from a relatively well-off family—he's practically perfect in every way. As his best friend put it, "Your brother is simply unbelievable! A man among men, an elite among elites, a god!"

Fang Xiuxiu, having known him for many years, initially thought her friend's words were somewhat exaggerated, having spent more time at home. But at school, especially in high school, compared to that group of uncultured kids, her brother instantly stood out.

Especially in middle school, he won awards and helped his mother establish a foothold in the education sector with her training center. Other families were incredibly envious. Even Uncle Xu, a friend of his father, spoke of his brother with envy, while his own son was labeled an "unfilial son, a scoundrel, a good-for-nothing."

To be honest, compared to those second-generation rich kids who indulged in debauchery and ended up fleeing abroad, Xu Ge was already quite good. At least he studied diligently, even if his grades were rather mediocre.

However, Fang Xiuxiu still had some questions.

Why did her father want to groom him as the heir? Shouldn't that be her younger brother's job?

"My mother wants to live a carefree life, it's not that I really don't want to do this!"

Fang Xiuxiu matured early, and she knew all too well how miserable her father's life was. He left early and returned late every day; it wouldn't be an exaggeration to say he "got up earlier than the rooster and rested later than the ox." He squeezed in time for all the important moments in her father's life, and after her mother started her own business, she was also very busy. Fang Xiuxiu really didn't want to live that kind of life.

Besides, shouldn't this family business be inherited by Fang Yuan? What did it have to do with a weak woman like her?

Fang Xiuxiu's thoughts drifted further. She thought about how outstanding Fang Yuan was, and how he was at the age of youthful exuberance and burgeoning hormones; even if he were an old monk reincarnated, he should have developed feelings for her, right?

But no.

Not a single one.

This guy, like a hot commodity, was incredibly chaste, a true disciple of the "pure and innocent" school of martial arts. Countless girls confessed their feelings to him starting in middle school, and even more after his first year of high school, but he was never seen with any girls.

He didn't even have many close relationships.

This inevitably led her to some strange and fantastical thoughts.

Looking at Fang Yuan's outstanding appearance, his physique wasn't thin, but rather delicate and handsome, Fang Xiuxiu suddenly had a possibility—XYY chromosomes.

He doesn't like girls, but he's handsome…

Holy crap!

Brother, he… he wouldn't be gay, would he?!

Otherwise, why would Mom and Dad have raised me?!

Fang Yuan watched his older sister's expression become somewhat abstract; he didn't even need to think to know she was letting her imagination run wild again.

Zhang Xia made her study art precisely because this guy's imagination was just too rich!

She had once asked Fang Chenxu if his family's business had become so successful because his father had consulted a spiritual master.

She also asked why Fang Yuan was the younger brother and not the older brother, as she preferred an older brother.

"No, I haven't thought about that right now," Fang Yuan replied quickly, his tone somewhat stiff, trying to change the subject.

He added in his mind: I haven't even figured out what's going on yet, how can I have time to talk about this? Besides, after being a plant for so many years, and now reincarnated as a human for over a decade, his aesthetic sense hasn't changed overnight.

Many people say they know what a girl looks like, can recognize her, but is she pretty? Honestly, only his fixed standards of evaluation accumulated from life can provide feedback.

This kind of thing is more like an objective attribute to him than an emotional experience.

In layman's terms, he's face-blind (￢_￢)

Looking at Fang Xiuxiu's disbelieving face, as if to say, "You teenage boys are so fussy," Fang Yuan knew some things would become harder to explain the longer he talked, so he abruptly changed the subject.

"Alright, it's getting late, we should go back. Uncle Sun has been waiting for you in the car for ages."

Upon hearing this, Fang Xiuxiu didn't press further, only giving him a meaningful look, then excitedly got into the car, looking like she'd find him when she got home.

Fang Yuan watched his sister's retreating figure, sighing inwardly.

What she didn't know was that he wasn't just not thinking about it now, but he might never think about it that way in his life—at least, not in the way she expected.

After all, he wasn't from here; he'd probably be leaving after the mission.

"Yuan Yuan," Fang Xiuxiu called out.

"Hmm?" Fang Yuan turned around.

"You really haven't fallen for anyone?"

"No."

Fang Yuan answered decisively.

"Then why don't you find a girlfriend?"

"My time hasn't come yet."

Hearing Fang Yuan's go-to answer, Fang Xiuxiu rolled her eyes at him.

Over the years, at least seventy or eighty people had confessed to him, if not a hundred, and he still hadn't found anyone. Fang Xiuxiu thought this guy was the kind of person who, even when other people's kids were old enough to run errands, still stubbornly insisted he wouldn't settle.



Chapter 10 The Handsome Guy on the Side of a Comeback Story (9)


In the car, the two continued their monologue, one talking and the other listening. To outsiders, this might seem like a strained sibling relationship.

But once you sensed their atmosphere, you realized it was an unspoken understanding.

Having risen through several ranks in the past decade, Fang Xiuxiu, as the eldest daughter of the Fang family, naturally attracted the attention of many. There were aloof men, passionate men, cute young men, and even domineering CEOs—they had it all. Since coming of age, her life had been like an otome game.

However, there was always Fang Yuan in the family. Although her younger brother was incredibly cold, Fang Xiuxiu had to admit he was undeniably handsome. Her aesthetic sense had been honed over time, and she had absolutely no interest in her many suitors.

As for her younger brother, what's that popular term these days?

Right, the aloof type!

Fang Yuan encountered the same situation, but he was incredibly aloof. Yes, just like that innocent, pure-hearted woman on TV, as if she was afraid that getting involved with him would cause her social standing to plummet, turning her from a high-flying actress into a melodramatic soap opera.

But you have to admit, this approach actually worked quite well. At least when Fang Xiuxiu learned Fang Yuan's method, it actually drove some people away. While not as effective as Fang Yuan's approach, it still solved a lot of trouble for Fang Xiuxiu.

However, there were drawbacks. It forced Fang Xiuxiu to maintain a certain facade in her words and actions. Although nothing serious, Fang Xiuxiu's naturally outgoing personality made it a bit uncomfortable to keep things bottled up.

She could talk to close friends, but saying too much felt like sabotaging her image. She didn't have that concern with her family.

The feigned aloofness met the real blockhead, and Fang Xiuxiu's mouth never stopped the whole way. She talked about everything from minor inconveniences to the fact that she couldn't eat much during dance practice, because stopping for even a short time would ruin her health, and she didn't want to remember the painful stretching.

"Mmm, yes, yes."

Fang Yuan remained silent, only agreeing.

When Fang Xiuxiu talked about studies, she complained that universities these days were insane, requiring both art skills and exam scores, it was exhausting.

Hearing Fang Yuan's perfunctory response, Fang Xiuxiu was also annoyed. She thought about how this guy had always been quick-witted and efficient, while she, despite working herself to the bone, barely managed to be considered excellent. Sometimes she really felt they weren't even born of the same genes.

"We're born of the same mother, why is there such a big difference between us?"

Because I have a cheat code.

Hearing Fang Xiuxiu's complaints, Fang Yuan didn't say anything, just smiled, showing no reaction to Fang Xiuxiu's words. The two gave the impression of ordinary siblings complaining, but Uncle Sun, the driver in front, was sweating profusely.

The young lady truly lives up to her father's reputation as his child; her intuition is remarkably sharp!

Unlike the two others, Uncle Sun, the driver, had been by Fang Chenxu's side since their humble beginnings. He was also aware of Fang Yuan's situation.

He had practically watched Fang Yuan grow up. Like Fang Xiuxiu, he was happy for Fang Chenxu and his wife when they were doing well, especially given Fang Yuan's talent, which he had displayed since childhood. When Fang Yuan first participated in an international competition, they initially thought it was just a childish fantasy, but when the invitation and certificate actually arrived, they realized it wasn't a scam.

Fang Chenxu was initially delighted. His child was a genius. Even if their business prospered and earned enough for his two children to live a carefree life for three lifetimes without gambling or drugs, as parents, they knew their child's potential was undeniable, perhaps even leading to a famous artist.

However, Fang Chenxu and his wife were not ordinary people. After their initial elation, they realized that Fang Yuan's talent shouldn't be wasted.

But their business had no involvement in the arts. Initially, they had planned for Fang Yuan and Fang Xiuxiu to each pursue their own strengths. But now they knew their son excelled in something they lacked experience in. What to do?

Knowing their child was talented but lacking experience in the field, what could they do?

Fang Chenxu chose the simplest and quickest method: invest money!

Their thinking was simple: after they passed away, their money would be left to their children. The Fang family might be a bit materialistic, but they had the money. They were letting their child test the waters; if things went wrong, Fang Yuan could simply receive a share of the profits.

So, leveraging their substantial capital, the two ventured into the then-untapped education and training industry.

The rest is history, so I won't go into detail here (〜￣△￣)〜

This explains why, despite Fang Yuan being superior to Fang Xiuxiu in every way, he was groomed by Fang Chenxu as his successor, and why Fang Chenxu readily agreed to invest in Shi Nan Middle School when Fang Yuan suggested it.

Outsiders believe the investment in Shi Nan Middle School was due to the Fang family's ambition to enter the education sector.

What else could it be? Was it for his son's education?

Hmm… not entirely, but that's undeniable.

However, from an outsider's perspective, spending a huge sum to acquire school shares just for their child's comfortable school life? That's utterly absurd.

The Fang family's vast fortune could easily sustain them for life with just a small portion. It's far more profitable to invest more within their own group than to plunge into an unfamiliar industry.

In the end, they both couldn't escape facing the issue of their family business; at their level, their education was insignificant.

In fact, Fang Yuan hadn't expected that simply saying, "I feel very good about Shihnan Middle School, and I want to study there," would lead Fang Chenxu to invest nearly ten million and make him a director.

Yes, Fang Yuan became a director; it was a formal agreement, a coming-of-age ceremony prepared in advance.

Fang Yuan didn't understand, and Fang Mutou was utterly shocked!

Back in the car, Uncle Sun looked at the reflection in the mirror of Fang Yuan and Fang Xiuxiu chatting and laughing, quite harmonious (from an elder's perspective).

A smile involuntarily curved his lips.

The young lady and young master hadn't been this happy in a long time.

…………

Unlike the relaxed atmosphere of the two chatting in the car, Gu Changming outside was not so relaxed.



Chapter 11 The Handsome Guy on the Side in the Comeback Story 10


Shihnan Middle School, as one of the top private middle schools in the city, boasts considerable strength and a wealth of outstanding students. Especially in recent years, with rapid economic development and increased emphasis on education, not only in literature and art but also in sports, Shihnan Middle School has produced numerous students with Grade 10 piano skills and Grade 6 English proficiency. Academic performance has also been excellent, with several students each year aiming for Tsinghua and Peking Universities.

Sports achievements are also remarkable. Several students broke school records at the sports meet two years ago, and in previous years, even a student achieved the top score in the physical education exam, demonstrating well-rounded development in morality, intelligence, and physical fitness. A few years ago, the school received a significant investment from a wealthy businessman, resulting in a substantial boost.

Not only does it have a new arts building, but it's rumored that new school uniforms will be introduced this year. The school commissioned a designer, and students in the know say that several designs were created for student voting. With moral, intellectual, and physical development combined with aesthetics, it's quite impressive in this nascent city.

Logically speaking, given the size of this school, its students should come from at least middle-class families, if not the extremely wealthy. The rest are academic superstars hired specifically to maintain the school's image. Even a single student here would be considered outstanding in an ordinary school. However, there are always some who seem out of place.

Take Gu Changming, for example. He's been at the school for almost five years and has a reputation, but not a good one.

When he first started living at the school, his appearance and attire didn't reveal anything special. People initially thought he was just pretending.

One day, a sudden downpour hit the south. Other parents rushed to pick up their children in their luxury cars, completely blocking the road in front of the school. But Gu Changming? He waited in the classroom for ages, then finally threw his backpack over his head and rushed out of the school gate. Those who saw him said he looked like a stray dog, utterly dejected.

Someone relayed this to their class, thus dispelling the rumors about Gu Changming pretending to be weak while actually being strong.

Although Shihnan Middle School had a strict school discipline, there were always some petty people who would secretly mock him.

If that were the case, Gu Changming wouldn't have such a reputation at school. His only claim to fame was that, given his family's circumstances, he would either have transferred out or worked harder. How could a fifteen or sixteen-year-old boy tolerate such treatment?

But what about him? He seemed to have no temper at all. His grades were mediocre, and he spent five years at school. Some of those who mocked him transferred out, but he remained, as if nothing had happened.

To put it nicely, he was calm and collected; to put it bluntly, he was a coward.

His only redeeming quality was a slight talent for languages. His English and Chinese grades were decent, but in Shihnan, where most families were wealthy, his English was really lacking. Compared to the other academic geniuses who were just there to make a name for themselves, he wasn't even a stepping stone.

His Chinese language skills were acquired through reading some rather cold and melancholic Western literary works during club activities. According to Uncle Gu Changming, he was reading books typically read by "middle-class white women," so it's incomprehensible why someone as clueless as Gu Changming would join the literature club.

Was it for the girls? Was he smitten with the beautiful president of the literature club? Or did he genuinely want to discuss the Moon and Sixpence with someone?

No, actually, that's not the case at all.

In fact, Gu Changming initially just didn't want to go home and wanted to find a place to hide. Comparing several clubs, he finally chose the literature club after seeing the members carrying several novels.

He discovered that while reading here was fine, there was no way to slack off, because they had weekly activities that required submitting book reports.

He couldn't help it; others were submitting reports on highbrow works like *Gone with the Wind* and *War and Peace*, while he couldn't very well submit something like "The Possibility of the Novel's Male Protagonist's Cliff-Jumping Adventure" or "The Most Popular Plot Points in Wuxia Novels." So he read some himself, and by some twist of fate, he actually managed to submit more.

In a smoky, historic internet cafe, Gu Changming sat facing his computer, its screen glowing white through the thick smog, casting dappled shadows on the floor through the greasy glass windows.

Suddenly, the computer screen began to flicker violently, emitting a crackling electrical sound. Gu Changming frowned and patted the computer case.

This lousy internet cafe's equipment was long overdue for replacement. Many people complained to the manager, but the owner always said, "We'll just have to get by as long as we can."

Otherwise, how could he be the owner?

Just then, a strong electric current surged from the keyboard into his arm, instantly spreading throughout his body.

It wasn't the slight sting of static electricity; it felt like countless red-hot needles were crawling up his veins,

burning, stinging, numbing—

Gu Changming wanted to scream, but his throat felt like it was blocked, and no sound came out. His body convulsed uncontrollably, and the scene before him began to distort and spin. The sounds of tables and chairs falling over seemed to come from a great distance,

as if through a thick layer of glass.

"Quick...cut...the power!"

These were the last words he uttered before losing consciousness.

After an unknown amount of time, Gu Changming awoke with a severe headache.

He found himself lying on the cold floor of the internet cafe, surrounded by a group of people, some calling his name.

"Hey, are you alright?" A young man in an internet cafe uniform knelt in front of him. "You just got electrocuted, it scared us to death! We were just about to call an ambulance."

Gu Changming struggled to sit up and shook his head: "I...I'm fine."

"Fine? You were slumped over the table like you were dead! If we hadn't found you unconscious in the internet cafe, you..." A gamer nearby interjected, "The manager has already reported it; the boss will contact you about compensation."

If someone hadn't gone to use the internet and found Gu Changming slumped on the table, trying to get him up, and discovered he was unconscious, with a burnt smell coming from the computer...

They realized something was wrong with Gu Changming.

This was essentially an unlicensed internet cafe, and the owner didn't want the police to come. After receiving the call, he told Gu Changming to stay calm and not to call the police unless absolutely necessary.

They found that no matter how they shook him, it didn't work. His hair even smelled of rancid protein. The manager was terrified, fearing he might die there, and was about to call the police when Gu Changming woke up.

Gu Changming stood up, feeling light yet full of strength. His ankle, which he had twisted when he fell, didn't hurt at all. He looked around and suddenly froze—

Something seemed to have changed.

"Right, the time!"

"How long was I dizzy?"

Looking at the student who had just gotten up, the internet cafe manager subconsciously answered,

"About ten minutes."

He was only discovered because his machine time had expired and someone had asked him.

Gu Changming glanced at the time displayed on the computer next to him.

It was past 6:50!

Oh no!

He was so engrossed in playing that he forgot the time. If he didn't leave soon, he'd get a severe scolding.

Thinking of his aunt's angry roar, Gu Changming involuntarily shrank back.

"I'll head back now!" Gu Changming picked up his backpack and walked unsteadily out of the internet cafe.

"Brother, can I have your contact number..."

Someone behind him wanted to say something, but watching Gu Changming's retreating figure,

"Don't worry, that guy's clothes are from Shi Nan around here."

Hearing this, the internet cafe manager rolled his eyes at the speaker. Everyone around here knew Shi Nan's reputation; it didn't need anyone else to say it. Even the students at this school came from wealthy and influential families. Their boss was afraid that guy would say something. These days, things are complicated, and the boss was afraid that in the end, the shop would have to close down.

It's better to give him some money and get rid of him; at least there won't be so much trouble. Doesn't he care about his career?

Gu Changming, for some reason, ran faster and faster, feeling increasingly relaxed.

However, under the shadow of his aunt's roaring, Gu Changming didn't notice any of this.

After crossing a street intersection, he reached a side street. Gu Changming had grown up here and knew the area like the back of his hand.

Ding—

The green light turned on. Gu Changming crossed the zebra crossing and turned his head to see a row of cars waiting at the road, including several luxury cars belonging to the school.

"I'd better hurry up, or I'll get yelled at."

Seeing those cars, Gu Changming knew they were dropping people off at tutoring classes; the nearest training center was just around the corner.



Chapter 12 The Handsome Bystander in the Comeback Novel 11


Gu Changming was unaware of the changes around him; he only knew he had to hurry back, or he would face a furious tirade from his aunt.

But to those around him, Gu Changming's figure was like a fish swimming through the alleyways. People only felt someone passing by, and when they looked up, they saw Gu Changming's hurried back.

"So fast!"

"That young man must be an athlete." Two simply dressed elderly men, strolling together along the alley, remarked casually upon seeing Gu Changming.

"Probably. Don't even mention our city, that Shih-Nan Middle School, they even had a top scorer in the sports exam a few years ago."

"It's Shih-Nan, Old Zhao, your tongue's tied again. But you know what, Shih-Nan has really developed these past two years. My grandson's there too, and I heard someone broke the school record the year before last."

"Hey, don't you know where we are? This used to be the Southern Shaolin Temple, their kung fu must be amazing."

The two men chatted idly.

Gu Changming, who had sparked their conversation, wasn't in such a good mood.

Reaching the foot of his apartment building, Gu Changming suddenly remembered he hadn't brought the things his aunt had asked him to bring; he'd left them at the internet cafe.

Gu Changming looked at the setting sun, the sun dipping below the horizon.

"Oh no, oh no, oh no, what a terrible day!"

It was already dusk when he got back to his aunt's apartment building. He took out his keys, opened the door, and found his aunt sitting in the living room watching TV. Seeing Gu Changming's empty hands, she immediately frowned: "Why are you so late? Where's the toilet seat? And the books!"

Gu Changming's heart skipped a beat: "I'm sorry, Auntie, I...I forgot."

"Forgot?" His aunt's voice suddenly rose, and she stood up from the sofa. "I told you so clearly! I told you to buy a toilet seat, buy it! Are you deaf? Or are you out of your mind?"

"I got an electric shock at an internet cafe, went to the hospital for a checkup, so..."

"An electric shock? I think you've been playing games all the time!" His aunt didn't believe him at all. "All you do is play games, you don't do anything productive! We've wasted our money raising you! Xiaohui got one of the top scores in the class today, and what about you? What was your score on the midterm exam last month? Tenth from the bottom!"

"I..."

"Don't call me auntie! I'm not worthy to be your auntie!" His auntie became increasingly agitated, reaching out to pinch his arm.

Just as her fingertips were about to touch his skin, Gu Changming instinctively dodged to the side. His movement surprised even himself—he had always failed physical education, almost losing the 1000-meter race to the girls at the last sports meet, and was always the one being bullied.

"You've gone too far!" His auntie paused, then grew even angrier. "You've grown some guts, haven't you? Now you can even dodge? Stop right there!"

Gu Changming lowered his head, letting his auntie berate him. He was used to this kind of scene, but this time, for some reason, he felt unusually calm.

Not the kind of serene tranquility, but an indescribable calm.

However, looking at the middle-aged woman spewing spittle before him, a surge of anger rose within Gu Changming.

His so-called outstanding son, supposedly among the top students in his class, was just boasting. Every day he came home to either play computer games or spend money going out with his cronies. His so-called top ranking was just the top 30 out of forty students in the class.

“I…”

But before Gu Changming could finish speaking, he was silenced by the machine-gun-like barrage of words from the middle-aged woman before him.

“If I hadn’t raised you with such hardship, you wouldn’t even have the right to speak to me now! You ungrateful wretch!”

The middle-aged woman’s words became increasingly outrageous. The anger in Gu Changming’s heart felt like it had hit an iceberg, plunging into a bottomless abyss, leaving only a pool of icy water.

A sense of emptiness filled Gu Changming’s heart. He thought of many things, but only one sentence came to his lips:

“…I left something outside.”

Ignoring his so-called aunt’s ugly expression, he turned and opened the door, returning to his “home” without even sitting down to rest.

"If you're so capable, then don't come back!"

The middle-aged woman, seeing her usually submissive nephew dare to shrug at her over such a trivial matter, hurled this insult.

"Ha, impulsive."

Gu Changming, who had just come downstairs, scratched his head in regret, feeling remorse for his impulsive actions.

In his mind, even if his uncle's family hadn't treated him well, they had still raised him for twelve years. Although their attitude was harsh, they hadn't abused him, which was already quite good.

Otherwise, he, as a child, would have been sent to an orphanage. Thinking of the plight of orphanage children depicted in TV dramas, and then thinking of himself, Gu Changming's regret deepened.

He walked slowly for a while, then smelled the aroma of food and arrived at a food street. Gu Changming felt hungry.

He hadn't felt it when he came out; although he hadn't eaten, he had a lot of gas in his stomach and didn't feel hungry. But now that his emotions had calmed down, and with the metabolic rate typical of teenagers, the smell of food had instantly made him feel hungry.

Walking into a reasonably clean-looking snack stall, Gu Changming ordered a plate of fried rice and began to devour it.

"Ugh..."

He let out a burp. Walking along the snack street, Gu Changming was tempted by the dazzling array of food, even though he had just eaten. However, he stubbornly resisted the urge.

What could make a teenager in the prime of his youth suppress his desires? Was it the yearning for a good physique, or self-control?

For most people, these two answers might be sufficient, but the reason Gu Changming resisted wasn't sacrificing present enjoyment for a bright future, but the harsh reality.

In short: he was poor!

Yes, he was poor. Gu Changming longed for a big meal, stuffing his mouth with delicious, irresistibly fragrant grilled meat, followed by a refreshing drink. A simple barbecue like this in the summer heat—and if possible, a few close friends with no connections, chatting and complaining, letting out all his pent-up frustrations.

Just thinking about it made Gu Changming's expression lighten, but it quickly faded into a faint sadness.

Ah, sometimes, you really can't think too much. Thinking too much can truly lead to despair.

Gu Changming discovered that, as he had imagined, being poor was actually the least of his problems. He lacked true friends. Although he had acquaintances he could talk to, Gu Changming knew very well that these people were merely casual acquaintances, and even years later, they would have already said goodbye.

Yes, Gu Changming was just that kind of person—a dull and unapproachable person.

Gu Changming disliked quiet, at least not before bed. Quiet spaces made his mind wander, and whenever it was too quiet, he would think of that quiet morning, of himself, and of the present.

How unsightly.



Chapter 13 The Handsome Bystander in the Counterattack Novel 12


Unconsciously, Gu Changming had left the snack street and arrived at a small park, where the temperature still carried a hint of heat despite the summer evening.

In the park, a few young people were playing basketball on a court. A ball flew out of bounds, about to hit a little girl passing by—

"Watch out!"

Amidst the exclamations of onlookers, Gu Changming turned around and, almost instinctively, rushed forward, catching the ball just before it touched the girl.

Thump!

A dull thud echoed as his hand made contact with the basketball.

"Thank you, brother!" the little girl said sweetly, looking up with an innocent smile.

"You're welcome." Gu Changming looked slightly surprised, but hearing the little girl's voice, he smiled and tossed the ball back to the young people.

They stared at Gu Changming in astonishment, clearly not having seen how he had done it.

The group wanted to approach Gu Changming to ask if he was alright, but Gu Changming simply waved his hand to indicate he was fine, told the little girl to be careful, and then, amidst the admiring glances of the onlookers, vanished without a trace.

"Wow, that guy's amazing! His reflexes are incredible!"

"Judging from his clothes, he seems to be from the nearby Shih-Nan Middle School, good at both academics and sports!"

"Amazing? I don't remember him! Which school? Let's play ball sometime!"

Hearing the chatter behind him, Gu Changming struggled to suppress a smile, his earlier annoyance completely gone.

No, he couldn't laugh. Gu Changming tried hard to control the smile that was about to spread across his face like a sportswear brand's.

Even though he had walked almost fifty meters, Gu Changming could still hear the discussion behind him.

Reaching a corner, Gu Changming glanced around to make sure no one was watching.

"Hahaha, awesome!!"

His pent-up emotions exploded, and the teenager, barely a teenager, danced and gesticulated wildly in the alley.

After calming down, Gu Changming's reason returned. How had he blocked that basketball?

The ball was clearly behind him; he only turned around to see it after hearing the people behind him speak. And when he heard their praise, he was walking quickly, yet the voices were still clear.

No, no, I'm overthinking it. Gu Changming, are you going crazy from reading novels? You're just having these wild thoughts after class today.

Gu Changming lowered his head, covering his face with his hands, trying to stop his overthinking as usual. But after rubbing his hands together a couple of times, he suddenly stopped.

Something felt off…

His skin was so smooth; he couldn't feel a single blemish or pimple.

Because of puberty, he had noticed a red pimple on his face this morning while looking in the mirror.

Gu Changming seemed to have discovered some earth-shattering secret, constantly rubbing his face with his hands.

Suddenly, he stopped what he was doing, took a step, and walked along a short path, a distance of less than a hundred or two hundred meters, but in Gu Changming's mind, it felt increasingly longer, as long as his entire life.

Gu Changming had walked this road for over a decade. On holidays, his aunt and uncle would sometimes be too busy to pick him and his cousin up, leaving them to walk home. Unlike his wealthy cousin, surrounded by a bunch of sycophants, Gu Changming always chose to walk. It wasn't that he was stingy with the bustling street; he simply enjoyed the feeling of walking through it. It made his world feel less lonely. Sometimes, if he had a little money left, he'd buy a snack, watching the bustling traffic as he ate it with relish.

If, if…

A warm yellow streetlight shone on his face, making him squint for a moment.

Gu Changming took a few steps and came to a nearby stall. The warm yellow streetlight added a touch of warmth to the smoky stall, and the ingredients displayed in the glass case.

Under the light, Gu Changming stared blankly at his reflection in the glass case, which smelled of barbecue.

The gloved vendor looked at Gu Changming and asked, "Young man, what would you like? I'm not bragging, but our..."

Gu Changming didn't hear what he said. He only saw himself; his hair was a little long, covering his forehead. He swept it back, revealing his forehead beneath his bangs, revealing smooth, fair skin. Under the light, his face was as smooth as a baby's.

"It's true, it's true..."

Gu Changming covered his face with his hands, his vision blurring. He slightly raised his head, his expression hidden, only his tightly pursed lips visible.

He stood quietly in front of the stall, as silent as someone attending a funeral, but the tears in his eyes betrayed the turmoil within the young man.

"Young man, what's wrong? What would you like?"

The vendor's words pulled Gu Changming back to reality. Gu Changming lowered his head and said with a slightly nasal tone, "Next time."

His voice was very soft, like a traveler bidding farewell to their host after a ceremony, gentle and soft, yet also like comforting himself.

Leaving the bustling city street and entering a small alley, Gu Changming looked up at the sky. The night sky lacked a full moon, only a few scattered stars. He stood there, gazing blankly at the night sky he had seen since childhood, his eyes stinging and his vision blurring.

Suddenly, the countless stars in his field of vision multiplied, shining as brightly as when his mother was still alive, as if the scene had never changed.

His mind drifted to the funeral rites for his mother's passing, the chanting indistinct, drawn-out, like the gentle patter of a southern summer rain. At that time, Gu Changming was still young and confused, only knowing that a group of unfamiliar uncles and aunts had suddenly come to his house, telling him that his mother was gone, and that he was now all alone.

When he first arrived at his uncle's house, he had asked his uncle where his mother had gone, whether she didn't want him anymore.

He wanted to find his mother, but later, as he grew older, he realized that he truly was all alone.

At first, he often dreamed of his mother, dreaming that she had passed away. He would cry loudly after waking up. But as time went on, when he had the same dream, he no longer cried loudly as before. Instead, he felt both sad and joyful, and the sound of the ritual echoed in his mind.

Each time he woke from this dream, the boy's emotions were complex. If he had to find a word to describe it, "bittersweet" would be the most fitting. He was sad because his mother was gone, and Gu Changming had grown up. From a wailing child to a teenager, over a decade had proven that his mother was gone, truly gone forever.

But now, when the boy dreamt of that childhood wailing, it had a different flavor. Like the movie *Coco* says, "Death is not the end, forgetting is." Each time he dreamt it, upon waking, his tears had dried, and a sense of solace remained.

He hadn't forgotten, and she hadn't left.

Looking up at the night sky, the bright moon was already there, shining brightly, its light illuminating the darkness.



Chapter 14 The Handsome Bystander in the Counterattack Novel 13


Fang Yuan, dressed in a white T-shirt and blue-and-white jeans, looked like a clean-cut high school boy, watching the bustling crowds on the busy street.

"Hello."

Fang Xiuxiu's voice came from the other end of the line, crisp and clear, with a slight upward inflection at the end, tinged with barely concealed curiosity. She was probably curled up on the sofa, legs propped up on the coffee table, talking on the phone while flipping through channels with the remote.

Hearing this, Fang Yuan glanced at the lively street scene and replied,

"Yeah, I'm here. It's quite lively."

"Good, that's good. Don't stay out too late. We just finished dinner. Grandpa and the others wanted to talk to you, but suddenly you said you wanted to go for a walk. I really don't understand you."

Fang Xiuxiu couldn't figure out what Fang Yuan was thinking. Grandpa doted on them the most; every time he came, he'd call them his precious grandson/granddaughter!

They were treated like royalty back then. From childhood to adulthood, whenever they came, their every wish was granted. While doting on them, he also didn't forget to give them moral guidance. Of course, sometimes when they (only you, right?) angered Fang Chenxu, he wouldn't abandon them.

Sometimes Fang Xiuxiu felt like her father and grandfather were raising her, one playing the good cop, the other the bad cop, working together perfectly.

“Okay, that's all for now. I wanted to go for a walk today, nothing special, I'll be back later.”

“You…”

After saying that, Fang Yuan quickly hung up the phone, letting out a sigh of relief. He really couldn't lie; if Fang Xiuxiu kept asking, he wouldn't know what to say.

Thinking about the surge of energy he felt on the way home today, he vaguely sensed that something was off about what System 120 had left behind and his own feelings. Moreover, it kept increasing while he was taking Fang Xiuxiu home, reaching its peak just minutes after they arrived.

It felt like… like…

A revelation!

Yes, a revelation, a revelation from heaven.

Fang Yuan pressed his hand to his chest, feeling his heart pounding. He sensed the immense life force within his body; the feeling had changed.

Although he had been training to achieve physical abilities comparable to some professional athletes, a person's energy and time are finite. Unless he abandoned everything and devoted himself entirely to training, even with his current physical condition, significant progress would be difficult.

However, this evening, after reaching his peak, Fang Yuan felt as if he had entered a new world.

If he had to describe that feeling in one word, it would be:

A complete transformation!!

"It's right here..."

To figure out what was going on, Fang Yuan rushed here after dinner, searching the intersection for any clues, but to no avail. Just as he was becoming disheartened, that feeling returned, though not as strong as before, but enough for Fang Yuan.

Following the feeling, he slowly moved to the spot. Fang Yuan raised his hand, clenched it, and his knuckles cracked.

"Excuse me, is the owner here?" Gu Changming pushed open the door of the internet cafe that would change his life today.

"No..."
