You've come at the right time."

The owner became increasingly agitated, pulling a wad of cash from his drawer as he spoke: "Here, five thousand yuan! Is that enough?

I've also reimbursed the medical expenses, you can pay me later! This is settled, let's go our separate ways."

Gu Changming was stunned. He hadn't wanted any compensation, but seeing the money the owner was offering, he inexplicably accepted it.

"Take it and get out of here!" the owner waved.

Gu Changming clutched the wad of cash and walked out of the internet cafe. Five thousand yuan—an amount he had never dared to dream of before. With this money, he wouldn't have to put up with his aunt's attitude anymore, and he could even rent a place outside, completely escaping the home that had humiliated him, a home that could even be described as "domestic violence."

Gu Changming held the money, his excitement indescribable.

Now he wanted to go to the food street to grab something to eat, and maybe think about what to do next.

Passing by a newly planned construction area, he saw an intersection that wasn't usually followed. Wanting to try something new, he went in, hoping that things would be like today, that he could say goodbye to the past today.

"Damn it!"

He froze on the spot as soon as he entered, because he saw several thugs standing in a corner, extorting money from a girl about his age.

"Hey beautiful, want to borrow some money?" a thug with a buzz cut said with a grin. "We're a bit short on cash lately."

The girl leaned against the wall, her face filled with fear: "I...I don't have any money..."

"No money?" The buzz-cut thug reached out to touch the girl's face. "Then play with us..."

Gu Changming initially wanted to walk around—he couldn't and didn't dare to get involved in this kind of thing. But as he passed by, his eyes met the girl's.

At that moment, he clearly saw the despair and pleading in the girl's eyes. She didn't speak, only pleaded with him with her eyes, like a drowning person grasping at a last straw.

Gu Changming stopped in his tracks.

That look was so familiar—it was the look he saw in the mirror every time he was bullied by his aunt and cousin, hiding in the bathroom at night, secretly crying. It was exactly that look.

Powerless, desperate, only able to hope that someone would lend a helping hand—

But he never received that help.

"Damn it!!"

Gu Changming cursed himself inwardly, turning to walk towards the corner.

A few thugs turned around, saw Gu Changming's thin frame, and laughed: "Oh, here comes the hero to save the damsel in distress? Kid, who are you?"

Seeing the unfriendly expressions on his thugs' faces, Gu Changming put on a meek and submissive expression.

Before he finished speaking, Gu Changming had already quietly picked up a brick from the side and, taking advantage of the crew-cut thug's turn, smashed it hard into the back of his head.

The crew-cut thug didn't even utter a sound before collapsing to the ground.

Gu Changming didn't give them time to react, his body darting out like a leopard. His agility was now far beyond that of ordinary people; in a few movements, he circled behind one of the thugs and kicked him in the knee.

The thug fell to his knees, and Gu Changming punched him in the temple, knocking him unconscious.

Bang!

But in the world of gangsters, you're bound to get hurt sometimes. And today, he did.

But, umm (￣(エ)￣)

Fang Yuan was too naive at first.

His life had been too smooth. Although he studied, for over a decade, he had been well-protected by his family. In this city, his family was now at the top level; no one above them bothered him, they couldn't compete with those in the middle, and they couldn't touch those below.

Humans are social creatures. Over the long course of history, they have evolved a complex system.

The saying "three men can make a tiger" and "many hands make light work" perfectly describes this.

With a large population, clashes are inevitable, and clashes inevitably lead to disputes. To ensure the long-term survival of society and the community, over time, some people will step forward to establish a system and regulations for the sake of the community and life.

Within this system and regulations, East Asia, as a representative of river civilizations, especially in a populous country like China, had developed a sufficiently mature and complete system for interpersonal relationships during its evolution.

The most important matters of state are war and sacrifice. In ancient social systems, sacrifice refers to a well-established system of rituals that defined relationships between people.

In a neighboring small country with cherry blossoms, interpersonal relationships have become almost abnormal, with concepts deeply ingrained in their language system. A single sentence can have completely different meanings depending on the speaker's social standing.

A similar situation exists in China. When Fang Yuan uttered the phrase, "The heroes of today are you and me,"

the implied meaning was crystal clear to those raised with this language system.

If the speaker and the recipient are of equal status, it signifies mutual admiration—a simple social gesture. However! If the two individuals are of vastly different social standing, the meaning of that sentence will drastically change. It will become, "I admire your abilities; let's be friends."

So far, isn't this all there is to it? But this needs to be understood in context. When two people of vastly different social standing, the one with the higher status says, "I admire your abilities, let's be friends,"

the key point of the sentence is the preceding part: "I admire your abilities, let's be friends."

The person with the advantage, representing a significant difference in status, expresses admiration for the other's abilities and a desire to become friends.

If someone as naive as Gu Changming heard Fang Yuan say this, they would think he was being praised and would simply laugh it off.

However, for Gu Changming, a guy who had lived a life of dependence and subservience for many years, and who enjoyed reading miscellaneous books, these words were quite interesting.

The other person wasn't the ruthless Cao Cao, and Gu Changming wasn't the Imperial Uncle of Han. The phrase originated from when Liu Bei sought refuge with Cao Cao, during their discussion of heroes over wine. Cao Cao was the superior, and Liu Bei, who had come to him, was the inferior.

Superior to inferior, high to low.

This is a subtle way of subtly influencing and subduing him!

In a flash, Gu Changming understood: this was an attempt to tame his youthful impetuosity.

If he harbored ambitions of achieving great things, he would be terrified, but for Gu Changming, it was perfectly fine. In fact, he was quite happy about it.

The other party was undoubtedly a remarkable figure, and had even done him a favor. Gu Changming had no grand ambitions. What was wrong with having a leader looking out for him?

A person should know their own limitations. Someone who tries to be a hero and gets easily defeated—even if he wanted to, could he really turn the tide?

If he had that kind of ability, he wouldn't have been bullied at his aunt's house for so many years.

"Hey, um, senior brother, do you have anything to eat?"

Gu Changming has a good point: he knows his own limitations and is good at finding his place. After acknowledging Fang Yuan as his leader, he automatically assumed the role.

He ate at the snack street yesterday, and it's been over ten hours now. For a high school sophomore like him, this is the time of year when he eats around 11 am and gets hungry again around 2 pm. Now that he's relaxed, his stomach is rumbling with hunger.

Fang Yuan glanced at the time. Although it's the weekend, his parents went to the company early this morning. As for his maternal grandfather, Zhang Jianguo, he went to chat and play chess with his father-in-law. He figured the Fang family wouldn't be back until after midnight.

"Let's eat out."

Fang Yuan thought for a moment and decided to eat out.

"Shall we go out..."

Gu Changming, who had already acknowledged Fang Yuan as his leader, naturally had no objection to Fang Yuan's decision. He also realized that their relationship was indeed not something to discuss at home.

Boss, no, Senior Brother, you're truly farsighted!

It seems Xiu Ji has some new dishes today. Let's try them.

In his short life, Fang Yuan has experienced many novel sensations, the most fascinating of which is the variety of food!

Yes, food, not so-called high-end technology, progressive ideas, or so-called mystical classics.

It's food, food that might seem too ordinary to some high-ranking individuals.

But for Fang Yuan, who spent countless years as a plant in his previous life, his experience with food was very limited.

However, after becoming human, he experienced the incredible diversity and countless quantities of human cuisine, which is constantly being innovated every year.

In the past, he only needed to silently enjoy the sunshine and rain, the changing seasons, and remained indifferent to everything in the world.

But once he truly tasted it with his human senses,

he became completely unstoppable, transforming into a glutton.

For example, right now,

Fang Yuan's driver brought Gu Changming to a private kitchen.

"Young Master Fang, you've arrived." The head waiter greeted him respectfully, his bow perfectly measured—neither overly courteous nor obsequious. He was already used to the arrival of this young VIP, whenever he had free time.

At first, Gu Changming was astonished by the taste of the food, but gradually he became astonished by Fang Yuan's appetite.

As dish after dish was served, Gu Changming's surprise gradually turned into astonishment. Fang Yuan's appetite far exceeded his imagination. From appetizers to main courses to desserts, Fang Yuan ate each dish with relish, seemingly never satisfied.

Fang Yuan kept stuffing food into his mouth, completely disregarding his image, thoroughly enjoying himself.

There was absolutely no trace of a wealthy young master. If it weren't for the fact that the private kitchen's decor was obviously very expensive, and that Fang Yuan's clothes were also unbranded, it would be obvious to anyone with eyes that they were custom-made fitted styles. Even if ordinary people didn't know, the expensive material alone would tell that they were extraordinary.

But looking at the mountain of food piled in front of Fang Yuan and Fang Yuan's nonchalant expression, Gu Changming inwardly clicked his tongue in amazement: "Is this guy's stomach a bottomless pit?"

Fang Yuan stopped eating, turned his head to look at Gu Changming, who, although eating, kept glancing at him.

"What's wrong? Not to your liking?"

This was clearly, clearly it wasn't to his liking!

Having been human for over a decade, he understood these kinds of subtexts.

East Asians were just that tactful and reserved.

The warm light from the gilded chandelier fell on the bone china plate. Fang Yuan used his silver fork to pick up a piece of rare filet mignon, glancing up at Gu Changming across from him.

The phone suddenly vibrated under the tablecloth, the screen displaying the words "Mother." Fang Yuan frowned and pressed the answer button: "Hello, Mom."

Fang Yuan glanced at Gu Changming, who was looking up at him, and cleared his throat: "Yes, he's my junior, a good guy. As his senior, I'm taking care of him."

"Haha, I didn't know you had this junior. It's rare to have such a good friend." Fang's mother's laughter carried a deeper meaning. "We've already spoken to him about his situation."

Fang's mother's implication was that those guys who beat up Gu Changming wouldn't get away with it. Although the Fang family claimed to be law-abiding, they were still a behemoth. They wouldn't let these petty thugs off easily if they dared to say a word.

At least in this area, those petty thugs had no chance.

If they truly had that kind of background, why would they have fallen so low as to become a bunch of thugs? This isn't the way to live a carefree life.

...

After finishing their meal, the two didn't rush to call Uncle Wang over. Sitting in the private room, Gu Changming was nibbling on the restaurant's special summer dessert.

After finishing two servings of the restaurant's ice cream bars, Fang Yuan realized he hadn't brought Gu Changming out for the meal!

"What are your plans for the future?" Fang Yuan leaned back in his chair, his fingertips lightly tapping the table.

Hearing this, Gu Changming's previously languid posture instantly straightened.

Gu Changming nodded like a chick pecking at rice, but the light in his eyes didn't diminish at all. "Don't worry, I will definitely learn from you and never let you down!"

Fang Yuan rubbed his forehead. He suddenly felt like he had made a mistake. Was this protagonist really that…unconventional?

Was this still the same patient, resilient, and calculating male lead?

But now it was too late to say "give up." Saying it would only deviate from the original plan, and might even lead to enmity.

"Alright," Fang Yuan waved his hand, "Tell me, what are you planning to do in the future? You can't just keep freeloading off me, can you?"

Gu Changming pursed his lips, feigning thought.

"Hmm..."

Fang Yuan's interest was piqued by his serious demeanor; he couldn't help but wonder about the protagonist's plans.

After all, this was his first time encountering such a thing, and it wasn't mentioned in the manual.

"I think—I'll freeload off you until I die!"

Fang Yuan had expected Gu Changming to utter some earth-shattering statement, like those successful people in this world's books before they achieved great things,

but... wasn't this exactly what I just said?!

You're the protagonist, the protagonist! Understand?!

I'm not asking you to save the world or beat up villains and rich rich kids, even a business plan would be fine!

"Senior brother, think about it, living a life of ease means our living conditions are good, even luxurious. Many people can't even reach that level these days!"

That seems to make sense.

If there's no hope, Fang Yuan could stay in this world with his family. But if there is hope…

Fang Yuan thought that since contact with the male lead triggered a system reaction, according to the manual and training, the protagonist is chosen by fate—sometimes an object, sometimes a person—but ultimately, they're all roughly the same.

Since contact changes fate, then—why not make Gu Changming's fate change too!

But how?

Gu Changming is a protagonist in a revenge story, but… Fang Yuan looked at Gu Changming, who was still munching on dessert.

This guy seems to be in the early stages!

Sigh, I have a plan. It can unleash fate without harming others.

A revenge story is all about revenge, little Gu.

Chapter 21 The Handsome Bystander in the Counterattack Novel 20


Early morning.

The sun rose from the distant horizon, the summer sunlight bright and dazzling from the very first light of dawn, its golden rays streaming into the room like flowing water, piercing through the large French windows and casting dappled shadows on Gu Changming's sleeping face.

"Ring ring ring—"

The sharp sound of the alarm clock shattered the morning tranquility, dragging Gu Changming from his hazy dreams back to reality. He glanced at the time: 6:00 AM. The sky outside was already bright, the summer sun relentlessly streaming through the French windows, shining on his face.

"No, I don't want to get up!"

He mumbled, turning over and burying his face in the pillow, like an ostrich trying to avoid the sunlight.

But he still reluctantly got out of bed, not because he had any ulterior motives, but because…

Ring ring ring

The phone beside the bed rang, the caller ID displaying the bright words "Boss."

"Hello." Gu Changming answered the phone listlessly, like a dried-out salted fish. But the voice on the other end was full of energy.

"Awake? Time for breakfast."

If Gu Changming were a girl facing this person in the morning, he would probably be rolling around in bed excitedly right now. But unfortunately, this aloof male god's morning greeting was given to a sleepy, pathetic loser.

"Mmm." Gu Changming had overheard girls discussing how if Fang Yuan, this aloof male god and school heartthrob, were willing to spend even just one morning with him, she would be so happy she'd faint, willing to do anything for him.

Well, now Gu Changming was experiencing the treatment he'd imagined. Fang Yuan, this male god, was indeed impressive. His sleep schedule was as regular as a Swiss watch, he was multi-talented, young and handsome, a sure-fire future pillar of society.

Compared to Gu Changming, an orphan who was so pathetic he'd be kicked by any passing dog.

But now he's saying he wants to help him improve himself, worried he won't be able to get up, and even calls him personally every morning, speaking softly and gently. If Gu Changming were a girl, he'd probably fall in love with him by now.

But beneath this gentleness lies a devil!

"Then come down for dinner. While no one's around, go for a run."

Hearing this, Gu Changming felt like the gates of hell had opened, and the devil's whip was lashing behind him.

If he could do it all over again, he wouldn't have so easily eaten that meal. It all started with that meal.

After dinner, Fang Yuan asked Gu Changming about his ambitions. Gu Changming recited with deep feeling his ideal of following Fang Yuan around, living a life of leisure and idleness.

Fang Yuan said,

"No, your senior brother will be very sad if you waste your youth like this."

He meant that Gu Changming was exceptionally talented, and wasting his youth like this was a great loss to society. As a friend, he couldn't watch him waste his life like this.

"Summer vacation is almost here, a perfect time to enrich yourself!"

Fang Yuan said, his face expressionless yet full of enthusiasm.

"Yes, yes, senior brother is right!"

Gu Changming, who had just become a subordinate, naturally had to agree with his boss's words, even though he knew it would affect him.

But Fang Yuan was offering too much!

Not to mention the lavish meal today, which could probably cover his food expenses for many years, just the conditions Fang Yuan offered during summer vacation were unbearable.

"My family has a new apartment building that's about to open for sale during the holidays. There's a park downstairs, so you can pick a few units and stay there for now."

A new apartment building, a park downstairs, and you can pick a few units?!

"Senior brother! Fang Shen!"

Hearing this, Gu Changming, forgetting he'd just finished eating, immediately grabbed Fang Yuan's leg like a tiger leaping up.

"You're like my own brother!"

At this moment, only two words remained in Gu Changming's mind: rich guy, true big brother!

Fang Yuan, seeing Gu Changming's reaction, said somewhat embarrassedly, "Well... that might not be so quick."

"It's alright, it's alright. I can handle the trouble myself. I still have some money on me."

Gu Changming, seeing Fang Yuan's reaction, thought he was just joking and couldn't keep his promise.

Fang Yuan waved his hand, saying, "No, no, what I meant was that the floor hasn't been opened yet, the renovations aren't finished, so you can't go now. You can go, but you'll have to wait a while."

Gu Changming understood Fang Yuan's meaning. Judging by their family's wealth, he knew how big their business was; someone so big would definitely value rules. Even though the project wasn't finished, Fang Yuan, this young master, wasn't the type to be a spoiled brat.

Knowing this, Gu Changming actually breathed a sigh of relief. If he had given it to him without hesitation, despite his excited appearance, he would have panicked. Now, he felt relaxed. Thank goodness, his senior brother was still normal.

But what he said next filled Gu Changming with apprehension.

"The building project will take a while longer. If you need it in the meantime, stay in my house. I remember it's a detached house, right by Qingcui Lake, the environment is quite nice."

Fang Yuan said, taking out the keys to hand to Gu Changming.

But when Gu Changming heard "detached house," "by Qingcui Lake," and "keys," he felt a cold sweat break out.

"Is it that Qingcui Lake that was developed a few years ago?!"

Even a single ordinary room there would cost his uncle an entire year's salary, working until he was ninety, just to afford the smallest room.

One of his classmates lived there, and their homeroom teacher even invited him out for a private talk at the parent-teacher conference.

That's how it is for ordinary residents, let alone the detached villas!

Thank goodness for your help.

Too small and weak to be worthy of this!

Even a regular Imperial Guard only earned a few hundred taels of silver. How could a high school student like him possibly afford a house worth tens of thousands of gold?

Chapter 22 The Handsome Bystander in the Comeback Novel 21

Gu Changming looked at his pajamas. Fang Yuan had casually given them to him when he arrived at the villa yesterday; they were indeed comfortable. But judging from Fang Yuan's behavior, this morning was definitely not a leisurely stroll. He estimated that he could only run a kilometer in this outfit if he controlled himself well.

Fang Yuan glanced at Gu Changming and pointed to a bag on the entryway cabinet, saying, "I've prepared everything for you."

Gu Changming opened the bag and saw a pair of brand-new running shoes, the tags still attached. There was also a set of sportswear matching Fang Yuan's.

Gu Changming tried the clothes on; they fit perfectly, as did the shoes.

"Senior, how did you know my size?"

"The sales assistant asked me yesterday when I bought the clothes."

Gu Changming's clothes were all from a specialty store, as were Fang Yuan's. He brought someone to buy clothes, and the sales assistant, with her professionalism, remembered it immediately.

Tsk, no wonder he's rich.

There's a five-kilometer-long running track around Qingcui Lake. A thin mist shrouded the lake in the early morning, and several egrets foraged in the shallows—the scenery was like a tourist promotional video.

Gu Changming looked at Fang Yuan, who was wearing the same clothes but looked completely different, and pouted.

The waiter's eyes lit up immediately. "Okay, I'll arrange it for you right away."

No sooner had he finished speaking than a group of stylists swarmed around him.

"Hello, this way please—"

"Sir, are you here for a styling session?"

"What style do you prefer?"

"Do you have a favorite style?"

Gu Changming looked at the stylists who came up and sighed. "No wonder it's a high-end shop; the service is excellent." But they didn't even understand who they were serving! He glanced at Fang Yuan—"Look at that guy who could walk the runway with his face like a burlap sack, does he even need you guys to style him?!"

Gu Changming looked at the female stylist in the form-fitting uniform next to Fang Yuan and felt that if there weren't so many people around, she would have clung to him. He once again felt the world's difference in treatment compared to a truly handsome man.

"I'm not talking about me, I'm talking about him."

Fang Yuan pointed to Gu Changming behind him.

"Senior brother…"

Gu Changming was stopped by Fang Yuan's gaze before he could finish speaking.

According to Fang Yan's research, external appearance directly affects one's inner state.

A person who dresses neatly and appropriately exudes confidence, which in turn boosts their appearance.

Besides, isn't his role in this mission a comparison between himself and Gu Changming after he becomes handsome?

With Gu Changming's hair almost covering his eyes now, can he even pull that off?

(≖_≖ )

The stylists, hearing this, showed a slight hesitation, but quickly understood. After all, this customer could practically be an idol in a burlap sack; there was really no use for their skills.

Turning to look at Gu Changming, they paused for a moment. But those who could stand their ground in this kind of shop had sharp eyes; they quickly figured it out—the kid had good potential, it was just buried by that messy hair.

One of the stylists, who had been standing shyly next to Fang Yuan and his colleagues, walked up to Gu Changming first and asked softly.

"Hello, sir, do you have any requests for your hairstyle?"

Requests? What requests? For 15 yuan, you still have requests? That old man would probably throw water on you if he didn't! He used his go-to excuse for this question.

"Just cut it however you like."

The female stylist nodded obediently, indicating she understood.

She spent the most time on the bangs. She used a comb to lift the bangs, measured the position against his brow bone, and then cut them diagonally with the scissors—not a clean cut, but a series of short, uneven cuts. The finished bangs fell about half an inch above his eyebrows, varying in length and revealing a small section of his forehead.

Then she trimmed his eyebrows. Finally, she applied hair wax and styled his hair.

After finishing, she untied the cape, and stray hairs fell to the floor.

Gu Changming stared at himself in the mirror, stunned for two seconds.

He hadn't really taken care of his hair before, and thought he was just average-looking.

However, what Gu Changming didn't know was that a superior appearance is an expensive resource; maintaining it requires time and money, and while many people aspire to this, few actually achieve it.

Before, while living with his uncle and aunt, he was either at school or doing chores every day, leaving him no time for such things.

The person in the mirror now had neatly trimmed hair on both sides, with a natural, slightly voluminous curve on top. His bangs fell diagonally above his eyebrows, just revealing their neatly shaped shape.

The contours of his face were clearly defined, his skin appeared whiter than usual under the light, and his features—especially his eyes and jawline—suddenly became more pronounced.

"Wow, I can be this handsome," Gu Changming said, touching his face in the mirror.

Fang Yuan walked up from behind, stood in front of the mirror, glanced at Gu Changming, then looked at his reflection, and nodded.

"Not bad."

Gu Changming's lips were about to curl into a smile upon hearing Fang Yuan's praise, but he was startled by Fang Yuan's next words:

"More handsome than me."

After saying this, Gu Changming stopped admiring himself in the mirror, and the stylist watching Fang Yuan's expression also turned strange.

The air suddenly became heavy.

After those words, Fang Yuan also sensed the eerie atmosphere.

"What's wrong?"

Gu Changming was speechless.

Senior brother, I feel like you're messing with me!

If someone else said this, Gu Changming could shamelessly say no, no, secretly pleased. But with Fang Yuan saying it, Gu Changming couldn't respond.

Who is Fang Yuan? Wealthy, handsome, diligent, disciplined, and exceptionally talented. Putting Gu Changming in a romance novel wouldn't be an exaggeration.

Moreover, Fang Yuan had done him a great favor.

Looking at Fang Yuan's matter-of-fact expression, Gu Changming couldn't bring himself to speak.

Never mind, whatever makes you happy, senior brother.

Fang Yuan quickly paid the bill and returned to the car. Gu Changming was still admiring himself on his phone, but they didn't notice that the driver, Uncle Wang, had a strange expression.

It was as if he had discovered some earth-shattering secret.

"What's wrong?"



Chapter 25 The Handsome Guy in the Counterattack Novel 24


Upon hearing this, Uncle Wang, the driver, simply waved his hand.

"No, no."

Inwardly, a storm was raging.

By the time Uncle Wang parked the car in the Fang family's garage, it was completely dark.

He sat in the driver's seat for a long time, his fingers tapping rhythmically on the steering wheel.

He understood the Fang family's rules—don't look at what you shouldn't see, don't say what you shouldn't say. He had driven for the Fang family for over a decade, relying on following these rules.

But about today's matter, he wasn't sure.

He had been the Fang family's driver for over a decade, and he had a general understanding of Fang Yuan's character. To put it nicely, he was aloof; to put it bluntly, he was somewhat cold and unapproachable.

However, recently, that young classmate had been running errands for him, even lending him the house his boss had given him—their relationship was truly excellent. But this wouldn't happen overnight, and in all these years, he hadn't heard of or seen that young classmate.

And what he hadn't noticed before, after getting his hair done today, was something that made him shudder...

Fang Yuan and Gu Changming looked remarkably alike. While Fang Yuan's aura far surpassed Gu Changming's, their facial features, especially their face shape, eyebrows, and brow bone, were remarkably similar. Anyone with eyes could tell at a glance that the two were definitely related.

If it were just a resemblance, he wouldn't be bothered. But considering Fang Yuan's attitude towards Gu Changming...

Could this be the boss's illegitimate child?!

Shaking his head, he dismissed this absurd thought, "No, no! Mr. Fang and the boss's wife have such a good relationship, how could I think like that!"

But what if? Fang Yuan's attitude towards Gu Changming was very strange...

He hadn't heard any rumors before, yet they were so close. He even lent Fang Yuan the birthday present Mr. Fang gave him.

That wasn't just some small toy!

Thinking this, he took out his phone, then put it down. Picked it up again, then put it down again.

He tried three times.

Finally, he gritted his teeth and dialed the number.

The phone rang twice before being answered.

“Ah Xing?” Fang Chenxu’s voice came through the receiver, tinged with slight confusion at being interrupted. “What’s wrong so late?”

“Mr. Fang, there’s something… I think you should know.”

Fang Chenxu sensed the seriousness in Uncle Wang’s tone. He put down the documents in his hand and leaned back in his chair. “Go ahead.”

“This afternoon, I took the young master and his classmate Gu Changming to get their hair and makeup done.” Uncle Wang carefully chose his words. “On the way back, I noticed something.”

“What is it?”

“That Gu Changming—” Uncle Wang paused, “He looks a lot like the young master. Absolutely. His nose, his face shape, they’re practically identical. He’s just a bit thinner, and his natural features aren’t as good as the young master’s, but after some grooming… he really does look like him.”

What he didn’t say was that Fang Yuan’s attitude towards Gu Changming was strange; he lent out such valuable things so readily.

There was a few seconds of silence on the other end of the phone.

"Are you sure?" Fang Chenxu's voice deepened.

The other person didn't speak. Fang Chenxu realized he had misspoke. Well, that was fine then; he was about 80% sure.

"I understand. Don't mention this to anyone yet."

"Understood."

The call ended.

Fang Chenxu placed his phone on the table, the screen dimming. Only a desk lamp illuminated the study, its warm yellow light casting a soft glow on the documents spread out before him, but he couldn't focus on reading a single word.

From that moment on, this child became his son.

Not in a legal sense, but in every sense.

And all he could give Fang Yuan was Fang Yuan.

Because after the car accident, the doctor told him it would be difficult for him to have children again.

That was a decision he and Xiaoxia made together. Since God wouldn't give them their own child, they would give a home to a child who needed one. More than a decade had passed, and they had never regretted it.

But now, a child appeared who looked and was about the same age as Fang Yuan.

Fang Chenxu's hand unconsciously traced the edge of the phone, his fingertips brushing against the metal frame.

Coincidence?

No. This level of resemblance couldn't be a coincidence.

He picked up his phone again and dialed another number.

“Xiao Chen, help me investigate someone.” His voice regained its usual calm and decisiveness. “Gu Changming, Fang Yuan’s classmate. I need all his information—family background, parents’ information, his life from childhood to adulthood, the more detailed the better.”

“Yes, Mr. Fang.”

"Use all available connections, as quickly as possible."

After hanging up the phone, Fang Chenxu sat in his study for a long time. The night outside was thick, and the streetlights in the park shone with lonely light. He suddenly remembered the winter when Fang Yuan was five years old. It had snowed heavily, and Fang Yuan had clung to his back, his small hands clutching his collar, his warm breath brushing against the back of his neck. At that time, Fang Yuan had asked him, "Dad, what does snow become after it melts?"

He said, "It becomes spring."

Fang Yuan thought for a moment and said, "Then I want to become spring too."

That child was different from other children from a young age. Other children wanted toys and candy, but Fang Yuan didn't want anything. He would draw, sitting for an entire afternoon, as quiet as a plant that didn't need much sunlight to grow. Later, Fang Chenxu discovered his true artistic talent and invested heavily in building a training center for him, hiring the best teachers, and buying the best equipment. Fang Yuan never said "thank you," but every semester he would bring home his portfolio to show him, like a bird carrying leaves back to its nest.

If Fang Yuan really does have a family, if they come looking for him—

Fang Chenxu rubbed his temples.

He had to tell Xiaoxia.

The study door was gently pushed open. Zhang Xia walked in carrying a glass of hot milk. Seeing his expression, she paused. "What's wrong? Who called?"

"Ah Xing."

"Uncle Wang? What did he say?"

Fang Chenxu took the milk but didn't drink it. He looked up at his wife, his voice low. "Xiaoxia, there's something you need to know. Fang Yuan has a classmate named Gu Changming. Uncle Wang saw them standing together today and noticed they look very alike—very, very alike."

Zhang Xia's hand holding the tray froze.

"What do you mean?"

"I don't know." Fang Chenxu shook his head. "I've already had someone investigate. But if… if Fang Yuan really does have relatives looking for him, we need to discuss what to do."

Zhang Xia placed the tray on the table and sat down in the chair next to Fang Chenxu. Their shoulders leaned together, just like the day they decided to adopt Fang Yuan more than a decade ago.

“Back then,” Zhang Xia’s voice was a little hoarse, “the paperwork was complete. But we didn’t know anything about his biological parents.”

“No matter what,” Fang Chenxu held her hand, “Fang Yuan is our son. That won’t change.”

Zhang Xia nodded.

“But what if that child really is his brother?” she suddenly asked.

What if his family came looking for him?

Fang Chenxu didn’t answer.

Because he was thinking about that too.

————

When the Maybach stopped at the entrance of Gu Changming’s residential complex, the sky had already darkened into a gray-blue.

The car’s paint gleamed a heavy, dull light under the streetlights, contrasting sharply with the peeling paint on the surrounding apartment buildings and the potholed concrete pavement. Several elderly people taking a stroll stopped, their eyes following the car’s rear, whispering amongst themselves.

Gu Changming sat in the back seat, his fingers unconsciously digging into the leather seat beneath him, his fingertips tracing the fine texture of the leather.

Fang Yuan suddenly spoke: "Have your uncle and aunt contacted you during training these past few days?"

Gu Changming's fingers stopped.

The smug satisfaction he felt after his haircut plummeted, as if someone had dragged him back to the ground.

"No."

Two words, light and short.

He turned his head to look out the car window. The streetlights slid across his face, illuminating his suddenly pursed lips before dimming again.

Fang Yuan didn't press further. He waited a few seconds, then said, "I contacted Uncle Liu. I told him about you and his family."

Gu Changming turned his head sharply.

Fang Yuan's voice was flat, devoid of emotion, but his eyes never left Gu Changming's face.

“He said he knows about the treatment you received at home. This matter needs to be settled.”

“I…”

The car stopped.

Fang Yuan opened the car door and glanced back at Gu Changming. That look was exactly the same as when he dragged him into the barbershop this afternoon—no more talk, let’s go.

Gu Changming took a deep breath and followed.

The two walked into the apartment building, one after the other. Half of the motion-activated lights in the hallway were broken, the rest casting a dim, yellowish glow. Peeling paint revealed the mottled cement beneath, and the stair railing felt sticky to the touch. Gu Changming walked slowly, each step feeling like wading through mud. Fang Yuan walked half a step ahead, his steps steady and unhurried.

Fourth floor.

Gu Changming stood before the security door, the key in his hand, the cool metal seeping into his palm.

The door opened.

"Who is it?"

The middle-aged woman looked up and asked, but froze when she saw Gu Changming's face.

She quickly recovered and snapped,

"You still know how to come back!"

The shrill voice exploded almost the instant the door lock turned. The incandescent light bulb in the living room hummed, its light glaringly white. The smells of cooking oil, mildew, and some indescribable sour odor mingled together and wafted out from the doorway.

A middle-aged woman stood in the entryway, hands on her hips, wearing a faded floral nightgown, her hair disheveled and tied back. Her features weren't ugly, but years of a harsh expression had left deep marks on her face—nasolabial folds etched into her cheeks, her lips perpetually turned down, and two vertical furrows between her brows.

“You good-for-nothing! You ingrate! Never home for days, where have you been? You don't cook, you don't wash clothes, who do you think you are? A freeloader—”

Her speech was rapid, almost without pause, like steam hissing from a pressure cooker. Spittle flew in the harsh light.

Gu Changming stood still, his shoulders slightly hunched.

It was a tiny movement, almost imperceptible. But Fang Yuan saw it.

He took a step forward, placing himself between Gu Changming and the woman.

"This..."

Fang Yuan looked at the shrewish middle-aged woman before him, unsure how to address her. He decided to get straight to the point.

"Gu Changming has lived in your house for years," Fang Yuan said, his voice low but each word clear, "After his mother passed away, she left behind 500,000 yuan in compensation, all of which is in your hands. Not counting savings, this house you own is worth over a million yuan now."

Over a million yuan? Gu Changming looked at Fang Yuan incredulously at this figure, but Fang Yuan remained calm.

Fang Yuan had someone investigate Gu Changming's uncle and aunt's family. He realized that his initial assessment of them as parasites had been a gross underestimation.

Not only had they usurped Gu Changming's place, but they had also embezzled the compensation money after his mother's accident. His supposedly conscientious uncle, when Gu Changming's father's friend came to visit, tricked Liu Hong into letting Gu Changming go to Shinan Middle School, feigning pitifulness and using a combination of coaxing and deception to get his child admitted. Later, when his job ran into trouble, he shamelessly sought Liu Hong's help.

Calling them vampires or parasites would be an understatement; they're practically strangler figs.

"During his time in your house, his monthly living expenses were less than five hundred yuan, and he still had to cook, clean, and do laundry for you. There was no heating in winter, no air conditioning in summer, and he could only afford a fifteen-yuan quick haircut downstairs."

The woman's mouth gaped open, as if someone had suddenly grabbed her by the throat, her voice choked.

"You—" she caught her breath, her voice rising sharply again, "Who do you think you are? What right do you, an outsider, have to interfere in our family affairs? Gu Changming! Where did you find this—"

"These are materials compiled by the lawyer."

Fang Yuan placed the file folder on the shoe cabinet in the entryway. The paper bag landed on the dusty wooden surface with a soft thud.

"Child abuse, embezzlement, and negligence of guardianship—three charges. From today onwards, Gu Changming severs all ties with you. See you in court."

The last four words fell, and the room fell silent for a moment.

Then came the outburst.

The woman's face flushed crimson, turning a deep purplish-red. Her eyes widened, bloodshot, and her lips trembled violently with rage. She jerked her hand up, her long, sharp nails aimed straight for Fang Yuan's face—

Gu Changming moved.

His body reacted faster than any of Fang Yuan's trained reflexes. Perhaps it was a long-suppressed outburst, or perhaps it was an instinctive reaction.

His hand rose from his side, the edge of his palm precisely slicing across the woman's wrist—not with great force, but at a tricky angle. The woman's hand was deflected, her nails grazing his ear, creating only a gust of wind.

"Enough!"

Gu Changming's voice exploded.

He stood in front of Fang Yuan, his chest heaving violently. His face, now clean-shaven, was sharply defined in the stark white light, his eyes burning as if something was ablaze. His fingers clenched into fists, knuckles white from the force, his whole body trembling slightly—not from fear, but because something that had been suppressed for too long had finally burst forth from his chest.

"It's been six years. In these six years, I've been cooking for you ever since I was tall enough to reach the kitchen. I did your son's homework, I mopped your floor, and I washed all your clothes. All the money my mother left behind is in your hands; I haven't seen a single penny. In winter, I sleep under two coats while you use electric blankets."

His voice trembled.

"If my mother were still alive—if she knew how you treated me—she—"

He couldn't finish.

His eyes reddened, but he didn't cry.

Fang Yuan stood half a step behind him, silent and still. He simply stood there quietly, like a silent wall.

The woman clutched her wrist, her mouth opening and closing repeatedly. She looked at Gu Changming, a flicker of fear she herself didn't realize flashing in her eyes—this child she had bossed around for six years had suddenly become a stranger.

"Let's go."

Gu Changming turned and stepped out of the door first. Fang Yuan followed behind him, closing the door behind him. The metal hinges made a dull thud, shutting the room, filled with the smell of cooking oil and sour odor, behind them.

The two walked down the stairs side by side. Motion-activated lights above them flickered on and off one by one, as if something was extinguishing behind them.

As they stepped out of the building, the night wind rushed towards them. Gu Changming stood at the entrance, tilted his head back, and took a deep breath. The cool evening breeze filled his lungs, carrying the aroma of food wafting from someone's kitchen.

He exhaled.

"Senior."

"Hmm."

"Thank you."

Fang Yuan didn't reply. He took out his phone from his pocket; the screen lit up, illuminating his expressionless face. He glanced down and pressed a few buttons, then put the phone back in his pocket.

"Let's go, the car is waiting."

Gu Changming followed behind him, took a few steps, then looked back at the window with its pale, unlit window. The woman was still standing there, looking down through the glass, her face blurred.

He looked away, without turning back.

The apartment building behind them resembled an unplugged appliance, all light and sound trapped inside that door. Outside, it was night, the sound of the wind, and the two dark red dots of the Maybach's taillights in the darkness.

As the car started, Fang Yuan suddenly said,

"Starting tomorrow, extra training."

Gu Changming turned to look at him.

Fang Yuan's profile was hidden in the dim light of the car, his expression unreadable.

"...Okay."

Gu Changming leaned back in his seat, the streetlights outside the car window receding one by one. He suddenly remembered the expression on his aunt's face when her hand was slapped away—not anger, but…

fear.

He didn't dwell on it; an adult fearing a child like him.

Was he being too emotional?

The car smoothly entered the night, headlights illuminating the road ahead. In the rearview mirror, the dilapidated apartment building grew smaller and smaller, farther and farther away, finally merging into the gray skyline at the edge of the city.



Chapter 26 The Handsome Bystander in the Counterattack Novel 25


As the car crossed the bridge over the river, Gu Changming rolled down the window a crack.

A gentle evening breeze blew in through the crack, carrying the damp, fishy smell of the river and ruffling his newly cut hair. He squinted at the view outside; the river reflected the lights on the opposite bank, creating shimmering fragments across the water.

Fang Yuan sat beside him, head down, scrolling through his phone. The screen's light illuminated his expressionless face. Gu Changming glanced at him and saw he was browsing a shopping app; the screen displayed a sports wristband.

"Senior brother."

"Hmm."

“That 500,000…”

Fang Yuan’s fingers didn’t stop. “Uncle Liu checked. After your mother’s accident, the insurance payout went through your uncle’s account. Adding your father’s savings, it’s about 520,000.” He flipped his phone over and placed it face down on his lap. “The lawyer said the probability of recovering it is high, it’s just a matter of time.”

Uncle Liu here is Liu Hong, who helped Gu Changming get into Shihnan Middle School. After Fang Yuan told Liu Hong about Gu Changming’s situation, he was initially incredulous.

In Liu Hong’s understanding, Gu Changming’s uncle and his mother’s family was small; the only younger generation were his son and Gu Changming. They had grown up together, not to mention being from the same hometown, and were blood relatives.

The three of them came from the same family, and he should be okay with his nephew.

He never expected Gu Changming’s situation to be so dire. Liu Hong, from a scholarly family, and raised in the South with its strong clan atmosphere, never imagined this family could be so heartless.

After investigating Gu Changming's situation, Liu Hong angrily berated him over the phone.

"You vermin! Ignorant, despicable, all show and no substance! You're unworthy of being called a son!"

Gu Changming's father had been adopted by the Gu family and entered university with excellent grades. He and Liu Hong had formed a deep friendship at the local high school.

The two shared a dormitory room, bunk beds. Gu Cheng was two months older than Liu Hong, and Liu Hong called him "brother."

Later, during university, news came that the Gu family had fallen on hard times.

The night Gu Cheng decided to drop out and return home, Liu Hong blocked him in the dormitory all night.

"We're just commoners now, penniless, with only grand ambitions."

"No, why not study hard at school and then help the family in the future? Brother, listen to me—"

But Gu Cheng said, "I know what you mean, I understand that principle. But without my family, I, Gu Cheng, wouldn't even know where I am today, let alone study hard. Now that the family is in trouble, I... I can't just sit idly by!"

Ignoring Liu Hong's persuasion and the school teachers' attempts to persuade him to stay, Gu Cheng resolutely left.

Later, Liu Hong and Gu Cheng continued to correspond. In his letters, Gu Cheng didn't describe his own situation, saying that he was doing well and there was no need to worry about him. Instead, he asked Liu Hong how his school life was. It wasn't until later, after Liu Hong graduated, that he went to visit Gu Cheng and learned that the Gu family had long since collapsed. When Liu Hong returned, Gu Cheng's father was already terminally ill and passed away shortly after Liu Hong's return.

On his deathbed, he asked Gu Cheng to marry his daughter, who would later become Gu Changming's mother. Gu Cheng then devoted himself to saving the Gu family business, but the already struggling operations were further exacerbated by the old man's critical illness and the resulting debt. For Gu Cheng, who had been a student not long before, saving the crumbling family business was impossible. In the end, he had no choice but to sacrifice everything else, selling off everything within the Jiang family that could be sold, even kicking his brother out, while he stayed behind to shoulder the remaining debts.

Single-handedly supporting the family, he dared not have children for several years after marriage, fearing that a child would cause them hardship. Two years had passed since Liu Hong graduated from university and last met Gu Cheng. He was surprised to find that the gentle and refined Gu Cheng of his memory now had gray hair and rough skin.

However, Gu Cheng did not feel inferior or sensitive because of his situation. Instead, he smiled at Liu Hong, whose eyes reddened upon seeing Gu Cheng's current state, saying that he was now a grown man, why should he act like a woman? He said that his situation was much better now, and that Liu Hong's arrival was unfortunate; if he had come a few years later, he would have seen his son.

That night they drank heavily.

Later, Liu Hong learned that he had single-handedly paid off his debts and, to accumulate funds, had gone to sea as a sailor. As his life gradually improved, Liu Hong was happy for him. He was also busy with his work.

He even wrote Liu Hong a letter, asking him to take care of his family if anything happened to him.

Because sailors are at sea almost all year round, their contact decreased, but their affection remained unchanged.

Unfortunately, fate intervened. Liu Hong only heard news of his father, Gu Cheng, after he had perished overseas and was attending his funeral.

They encountered a shipwreck on their next voyage; a month later, only a few survived, including Gu Cheng.

Gu Cheng's decision to become a seaman was a last resort. After paying off his debts, his son, Gu Changming, was born. Gu Cheng cherished this child dearly. To provide a better life for him, his wife, and their child, Gu Cheng, using his English skills and intelligence, became a third mate on a newly commissioned ship, planning to work for two years to save money and start his own business.

However, the following year, they were shipwrecked, leaving behind only a widow and her child and some compensation. Later, Gu Changming's mother also perished in an accident, leaving only Gu Changming.

While Liu Hong was heartbroken by their deaths, upon learning of Gu Changming's academic difficulties, he stepped in. Out of consideration for Gu Cheng's upbringing, he helped his uncle's family enroll in Shinan Middle School along with Gu Changming.

Unexpectedly, despite being related, his uncle's family was involved in an extortion scheme.

Liu Hong was unwell, and upon learning of his old friend's son's plight, he was furious. Having no other choice, he asked Fang Yuan, Gu Changming's friend, to convey his apologies, blaming him for misjudging someone and causing Gu Changming so much suffering over the years.

After relaying Liu Hong's words, Fang Yuan added, "He was so angry because of you that he almost had surgery. He said he was too ashamed to tell you in person."

Gu Changming remained silent, tears streaming down his face.

So, I wasn't unwanted after all; there were people who cared for me silently.

The streetlights outside the car window slid by, illuminating his face before dimming again. He lowered his eyes, looking at his hands. Those hands, used for six years cooking and doing odd jobs at his aunt's house, were rougher than most people his age, with thin calluses on his palms.

“Is Uncle Liu feeling better now?” he asked.

Fang Yuan turned to look at him.

“I was thinking,” Gu Changming’s voice lowered, “if my mother were still alive, she would definitely go after them and fight them to the death.”

A few seconds of silence filled the car. Fang Yuan didn’t reply, but simply adjusted the air conditioning vent, preventing the air from blowing directly on Gu Changming.

After a while, Gu Changming spoke again, his voice back to normal: “Senior brother, were you deliberately asking that question on the bus just now? Asking if my uncle and aunt had contacted me?”

Fang Yuan didn’t answer.

Gu Changming didn’t need an answer. He leaned back in his seat, closed his eyes, and a slight smile curved his lips.

Three weeks later.

The final day of final exams at Shinan Middle School's Grade 11 building.

The bell pierced the sweltering afternoon air in the corridor. Exam room doors opened one after another, and students poured out like water released from a dam. Some were checking answers, some were groaning, and some took off their school uniforms and draped them over their shoulders, revealing sweat-soaked T-shirts.

When Gu Changming finished packing his stationery and walked out of the exam room, the corridor suddenly fell silent for a moment.

Not completely silent, but the kind of silence where everyone was talking, yet all eyes turned to him.

His short, neatly cut black hair revealed his forehead and brow bone. Three weeks of systematic training had completely changed his posture. Before, he walked with his chest hunched and shoulders shrunk, as if ready to hide himself at any moment. Now his back was straight, his shoulders open, his chin slightly tucked in, and his pace neither too fast nor too slow.

Most importantly, it was his eyes.

The timid, ever-observant look in those eyes was gone. In their place was a quiet, resolute light, like a deep, undercurrent.

"That's… Gu Changming?"

"Holy crap?"

"Wait, wait, wait, that Gu Changming? Gu Changming from Class Three?"

Whispers spread like ripples on the water. A few girls huddled together, their eyes following him from one end of the corridor to the other. One of them nudged the girl next to her with her elbow, whispering something, and then both of them blushed simultaneously.

Gu Changming didn't notice. Or rather, he did notice, but he didn't care.

Before, he would treat every gaze directed at him as scrutiny, mentally agonizing over whether he had done something wrong. Not anymore. The first thing Fang Yuan taught him wasn't how to punch, but how to stand up straight and not bow his head.

"Gu Changming!"

Homeroom teacher Zhou jogged down the corridor, clutching a stack of freshly printed report cards, his glasses slipping down his nose. He stopped in front of Gu Changming, took a couple of breaths, and shoved the report cards into his hand.

"Look for yourself."

Gu Changming looked down.

Chinese 128, Math 141, English 135, Science 267. Total 671. Ninth in class, thirty-first in grade.

He blinked, then flipped the report card over to make sure it wasn't printed incorrectly on either side.

Old Zhou took off his glasses, wiped them, and put them back on. He looked Gu Changming up and down, his gaze carrying a complex mix of surprise, relief, and a hint of suspicion—"Were you just putting on an act before?"

"What was your ranking in the last monthly exam?"

"Thirty-seventh in the class."

"And in the grade?"

"Not in the top two hundred."

Old Zhou paused for two seconds, then patted Gu Changming's shoulder firmly. "Keep it up. With this score, you can choose whichever comes next June."

Gu Changming folded his report card and put it in his pocket, glancing up at the window at the end of the corridor. Sunlight streamed in through the glass, casting a warm yellow hue on the corridor floor. He thought that if Fang Yuan were here, he'd probably say "Not bad," and then give him two extra sets of core exercises tomorrow.

He smiled.

On the afternoon of the third day after all the results were released, Gu Changming received a call from an unknown number.

"Little Gu, right? I'm Fang Yuan's father."

The voice on the other end of the phone was strong and confident, carrying the air of someone accustomed to giving orders. But the enthusiasm in his tone was genuine, even overly so—like someone not very good at expressing goodwill trying too hard.

"Hello, Uncle Fang."

"Oh, good, good. Are you free this afternoon? Come over for a visit. Fang Yuan hasn't returned yet; I'll have the driver pick you up."

Before Gu Changming could reply, the other end added, "Don't be shy, Fang Yuan's friends are family."

Fang Chenxu had someone investigate Gu Changming and Fang Yuan's relationship. His father had died in a shipwreck over a decade ago. Even if it was related to Fang Yuan, a dead man wasn't scary to him; at most, he could pay them off.

Besides, if they really wanted to make something of Fang Yuan…

Heh, the real estate business of Huanyu Group isn't something any kind soul could handle.

However, Fang Chenxu still intended to have Gu Changming come. Some things are better learned from books than from practice; true understanding comes from experience.

Forty minutes later, Gu Changming sat in the Fang family's living room.

It was more like an entire floor had been opened up than a living room. The city skyline stretched out through the floor-to-ceiling windows, the setting sun casting a warm glow on the greyish-white marble floor. The sofa was large enough to be used as a bed, and the coffee table held cut fruit and two cups of tea, still steaming.

Fang's father sat opposite him, a man in his early fifties, ramrod straight, wearing a dark grey polo shirt that revealed the well-defined muscles in his arms beneath the cuffs. His features resembled Fang Yuan's by about five or six points, but their demeanor was completely different—Fang Yuan was taciturn and aloof, while Gu Changming possessed a warm and approachable personality honed through years of business dealings.

"Training's been tough lately, hasn't it? That kid Fang Yuan, he's ruthless when he gets going." Fang's father picked up his teacup and took a sip. "Please bear with him. He's always been like this, just like his mother, once he sets his mind on something, he charges straight ahead."

Gu Changming shook his head. "It's not tough. The training load my senior brother arranged is just right."

"That's good, that's good." Mr. Fang put down his teacup and leaned forward slightly. "Are you settling in well? Is that apartment close to the school? If it's inconvenient, just let me know, and Fang Yuan will take you to choose one. Huanyu has plenty of other things, but plenty of apartments. You two can stay wherever you want."

He said this as casually as if he were saying, "There are drinks in the fridge, help yourself."

Gu Changming opened his mouth, unsure what to say. He had lived at his aunt's house for six years, even having to worry about using an extra kilowatt-hour of electricity. Now someone was telling him, "Plenty of apartments."

“Uncle Fang, really, there’s no need—”

“Oh, what do you mean no need?” Mr. Fang waved his hand to interrupt him. “Fang Yuan has never liked making friends. His mother and I are busy with our business, and he grew up alone, used to carrying everything on his own. We’re so happy he has a friend like you.”

He paused here, picked up his teacup, and took another sip, as if considering something. Then he looked up at Gu Changming’s eyes, his tone suddenly becoming a little cautious.

"Gu, I have a question for you."

"Go ahead."

"You know... if Fang Yuan had another brother, what do you think he'd think?"

Gu Changming paused, taken aback.

Fang's father stared at his expression for two seconds, then suddenly laughed, slapping his forehead. "Never mind, never mind, I was just talking nonsense. Don't take it to heart."

He put his teacup down on the coffee table, stood up, and his voice became loud again: "By the way, during summer vacation, you and Fang Yuan should go out and have some fun. Go wherever you want, Uncle will cover the expenses. You young people shouldn't stay cooped up at home all day, go out and see the world."

Before Gu Changming could answer, the sound of a lock turning came from the entrance hall.

Fang Yuan pushed open the door, wearing a black quick-drying T-shirt, a sports bag slung over his shoulder, and beads of sweat still clinging to his forehead. He changed his shoes and entered the living room, his gaze sweeping back and forth between Gu Changming and his father.

"Dad."

Fang's father walked over and patted his shoulder, his hand landing firmly. "You're back? I was chatting with Xiao Gu. Your friend is good, sensible."

Fang Yuan didn't reply, placing his sports bag beside the sofa and sitting down next to Gu Changming. He picked up Gu Changming's now-cold cup of tea from the coffee table and took a sip casually.

Fang's father watched this action, his eyebrows twitching almost imperceptibly, then he smiled.

That smile was different from his earlier enthusiasm—not a businessman's smile, but the smile of a father seeing his quiet only son finally have someone he can be with without speaking.

"Alright, you two chat, I have a meeting." Mr. Fang went to the entryway to change his shoes, then turned back to Gu Changming before leaving, saying, "Gu, about the summer vacation trip we were talking about, you two discuss it. Tell Fang Yuan where you want to go."

The door closed.

The living room fell silent. The sun sank a little lower, the light changing from golden to orange-red.

Fang Yuan put down his teacup. "How did the exams go?"

Gu Changming took out his report card from his pocket and handed it to him.

Fang Yuan took it and glanced at it, his expression unchanged. He folded the report card and returned it to Gu Changming, then stood up and walked towards the kitchen.

"Not bad. Starting tomorrow, add two sets of shuttle runs."

"...Got it."

Gu Changming leaned back on the sofa, listening to the sound of water being poured from the kitchen, a smile playing on his lips.

The city outside the floor-to-ceiling windows was sinking into twilight, the last rays of sunset peeking through the gaps between the buildings. He remembered that night three weeks ago, standing at his aunt's door, his fingers clenched into fists, his whole body trembling.

Back then, he thought he would be trapped forever in that house filled with the smell of cooking oil and sour odor, walking hunched over, speaking with his head down, shrinking himself smaller and smaller until no one could see him.

But no.

Someone pulled him out of that house. Someone stood in front of him. Someone taught him how to stand up straight.

The sound of water in the kitchen stopped. Fang Yuan returned with two glasses of water, handing him one and keeping the other for himself, sitting down beside him.

Fang Yuan looked at Gu Changming, sitting beside him, a completely different person from when they first met, and thought, this should be considered a comeback, right?

Gu Changming suddenly spoke.

“Can we eat something normal for training today?”

Fang Yuan: “…”

“It’s good for training.”

Gu Changming: So I need to eat more (Ｔ▽Ｔ)

Senior brother, you’re such a blockhead.

Can’t you at least consider the atmosphere and be a little more considerate of your junior brother?

Chapter 27 The Handsome Guy on the Side in the Counterattack Novel 26


"Senior brother, I cultivate immortality!"

Gu Changming's eyes lit up as he looked at Fang Yuan.

Fang Yuan: {{(°△°; "}}!

"I don't have that kind of thing!"

Fang Yuan tried his best to explain to Gu Changming.

The story takes place on an ordinary evening during summer vacation.

The western clouds were scorched a rusty color by the setting sun, like a piece of red-hot iron slowly cooling.

The two had just finished their training for the day. Fang Yuan walked ahead, the strap of his gym bag digging into his shoulder, just like any other day.

They stopped at the intersection. Fang Yuan took out his phone and glanced at the time. Gu Changming stood beside him, wiping the sweat from his neck with a towel.

It was at this moment.

When Gu Changming later tried to recall it, he found he couldn't remember anything. It wasn't that his memory was hazy; it was that the moment was too fast—so fast that all his senses couldn't keep up. He only remembered Fang Yuan's shoulder suddenly shifting to the side, as if pushed by something unseen.

Then came the sound.

It wasn't a gunshot. It was a sharp, piercing whistling sound that tore through the air. Before the sound even faded, Fang Yuan was no longer where he was.

Gu Changming had never seen such speed of movement.

It wasn't the kind of speed he used in training. The speed in training was methodical, a fluidity etched into muscle memory after thousands of repetitions.

This speed was different—it was an almost violent, whirlwind-like speed. Fang Yuan was like a fully drawn bowstring suddenly released, his body lowered to almost touching the ground, contorting at an impossible angle in the shadows of the alleyway.

A second whistling sound swept past his back, blasting a fist-sized crater in the wall behind him. Debris and cement shards flew, hitting Gu Changming's face.

His body moved before his brain.

Combat training had ingrained a kind of instinctive reaction in his mind—lowering his center of gravity, finding cover, maintaining his line of sight. Even as Fang Yuan watched him practice these movements repeatedly, he felt he could never achieve them that quickly. But now his body moved on its own, without conscious thought, as naturally as breathing.

As he rolled to the base of the wall, he saw Fang Yuan had already surged to the alley entrance. Fifteen meters, in less than two seconds. His gym bag was gone, and in his hand was a knife—not a training knife, but a real, sharpened one. Gu Changming hadn't seen where the knife had been drawn.

Two people stood at the alley entrance. Both wore dark short-sleeved shirts and black masks, their hands gleaming with a cold light.

Fang Yuan didn't give him a third chance.

The first man's wrist was struck by the back of the blade, sending the object flying out of his hand, bouncing against the wall before landing on the ground. Gu Changming later learned what it was. The second man's knee was kicked hard, and he plummeted straight down like a puppet stripped of its support. Before he hit the ground, Fang Yuan used his knee to strike his chin, producing a dull, bone-on-bone sound.

It all happened in less than ten seconds.

The two men lay on the ground, one clutching his wrist, the other curled up. Fang Yuan stood between them, blade pointing downwards, his breathing perfectly steady.

Gu Changming stood up from the base of the wall. His legs were trembling, not from fear, but from the lingering effects of the adrenaline rush. His heart was pounding like a drum, and his temples were throbbing. But he stood firm.

Fang Yuan turned to look at him.

The two exchanged a glance, confirming each other's condition.

Then Fang Yuan lowered his head, looking at the hand that held the knife.

His fingers were glowing.

It wasn't a metaphor, nor an illusion. They were truly glowing. A very faint, ethereal blue light seeped from between his fingers, like static electricity in winter, or like some bioluminescent creature in the deep sea.

The light was faint, almost invisible in the twilight, but it flowed, starting from his fingertips, spreading upwards to his wrist, to his forearm, like tiny, luminous veins beneath his skin.

Gu Changming saw it.

Fang Yuan turned his hand over, palm up. The light gathered in his palm for a moment, tried to be controlled, and then went out.

The alley was quiet except for the groans of the two people on the ground.

Fang Yuan stared at his hand for a long time. Then he looked up at Gu Changming.

"You saw it?"

Gu Changming nodded.

Fang Yuan paused for two seconds, then sheathed the knife. "Let's go back."

They called the police. The police arrived quickly, took statements, and took the two men off the ground. During the statement-taking process, Fang Yuan remained expressionless, answering questions concisely, as if stating something unrelated to himself. Gu Changming, sitting next to him, noticed that Fang Yuan's right hand was slightly clenched, his thumb pressing against his palm, as if sensing whether something was still there.

On the way back, neither of them spoke.

It wasn't that he didn't want to talk about it. It was that he didn't know where to begin. The only sounds in the carriage were the low hum of the air conditioner and the whistling of the wind outside the window. Gu Changming looked at Fang Yuan's profile, while Fang Yuan looked out the window. The streetlights slid across his face, one beam at a time, exactly the same as that night on the bridge across the river.

But something was different.

That night, Gu Changming slept very lightly. Not from insomnia, but from his body being alert. Every time he turned over, he woke up, his ears picking up every sound in the room—the hum of the air conditioner, the rustling of the trees outside the window, the faintest noise coming from the living room. He knew it was Fang Yuan; Fang Yuan wasn't asleep either.

At three in the morning, he got up to get a drink of water. Passing through the living room, he saw Fang Yuan sitting on the sofa. The lights were off, the curtains were half-drawn, and the faint morning light seeped in through the gaps, casting a pale gray outline on him. He was looking down at his right hand. His palm opened, then closed, then opened again.

Gu Changming didn't say anything, finished his water, and went back to his room.

Some things don't need to be said at three in the morning.

The next morning, Gu Changming was awakened by the aroma of porridge.

When he came out of his room, Fang Yuan was already sitting at the dining table. On the table were two bowls of white porridge, a dish of pickled vegetables, and two boiled eggs. The eggs were neatly peeled and placed on a white porcelain plate, still steaming.

It wasn't the previous nutrient solution that looked like excrement. ヾ(＠^∇^＠)ノ

Gu Changming sat down opposite Fang Yuan. The two ate their porridge facing each other, the chopsticks clinking softly against the rim of their bowls. Morning light streamed in through the window, drawing a line of light and shadow on the table.

Gu Changming looked at the hand. It was the same as always, with distinct knuckles and thin calluses on the palm. Nothing different from usual.

“Last night,” Gu Changming put down his chopsticks, “I saw light in your hand.”

Fang Yuan paused for a moment in his porridge-drinking motion.

“I felt it too,” Gu Changming said.

Fang Yuan looked up.

Gu Changming extended his right hand, placing it on the table, palm up. He looked down at his palm, as if observing a change he himself wasn't entirely sure about.

“It’s not light. It’s here.” He tapped his temple with his left hand, “Since last night, I can feel things. Not see, not hear, I feel.”

He looked at Fang Yuan.

“Like now. Is there a numb spot on your right palm?”

Fang Yuan didn’t speak.

But his pupils contracted slightly.

“Starting from last night,” Gu Changming withdrew his hand and picked up his chopsticks again. “I can sense things when I'm close to people. It's not mind reading, not that clear. It's more like… the flow of temperature. The outline of emotions. That feeling in your right palm, that's what that thing left behind last night.”

He picked up a piece of pickled vegetable and stirred it in the porridge.

“Senior brother. What did you think that light was yesterday?”

Fang Yuan remained silent for a long time. So long that the sunlight outside the window moved from one end of the table to the other, so long that the steam in the porridge thinned.

Then he spoke.

“I don’t know.”

His voice was lower than usual, as if drawn from a deep well.

This shouldn’t exist in this world.

No, it's also possible that there are things in this world I don't know about.

For example—System 120, which has been silent for so long…

“But I'm investigating.”

Gu Changming nodded. He didn't ask any more questions.

Fang Yuan said he was investigating, and he was investigating. There was no need to ask further, no need to urge him. He trusted Fang Yuan. From the moment Fang Yuan stood at his aunt's door three weeks ago and pulled him out, he had trusted this person. This trust wasn't the result of thought; it was an instinct etched into his body.

Fang Yuan finished the last mouthful of porridge and stood up to clear the dishes. The faucet rang, and the dishes clinked together crisply. Gu Changming sat at the table, motionless, looking at his right hand. He opened his palm, then closed it again. The morning light fell on his palm; it was clean, empty.

But he knew something had arrived.

Fang Yuan stood in front of the kitchen sink, his hands covered in dish soap foam.

The water was cold.

He said something to himself.

"Are you there?"

No response. The tap water was still running, foam trickling down his fingers, gathering into a drop at his fingertip before falling.

"I know you're there," he said in his mind, "Come out."

Still nothing.

Tsk, still no luck.

Fang Yuan turned off the tap. The kitchen fell silent, save for the low hum of the refrigerator and the sound of Gu Changming clearing the table from the living room.

Just then, a voice echoed in his mind.

It wasn't heard through his ears, but from within. Like a pebble thrown into water, ripples spread outwards from the center, spreading through his entire consciousness in concentric circles.

Just like the high-ranking officials he and his parents had met—equally businesslike, equally distant…

He only said those two words.

From the gratitude Fang Yuan felt when System 120 rescued him and the passion of their initial mission together, to the desolation of not seeing each other for decades, Fang Yuan's feelings for System 120...

System 120 fell silent. The silence wasn't long, about two or three seconds. But for a system whose processing speed is measured in nanoseconds, two or three seconds of silence is almost equivalent to prolonged human speechlessness.

“17 years, two months, and seven days,” 120 said. “From the time I lost contact with the host until we re-established the connection this morning, the exact time is four years, two months, and seven days, fourteen hours, and twenty-three minutes.”

He didn't want this to affect their relationship.

In the words of the novels in this world, could a mere passerby like him really have the right to seduce someone?

System 120 ignored Fang Yuan's question and continued,

"The space is actually aware of this. Later, during our first mission, the host's transformation into an infant was because the will of this world was attracted by the life force left behind in the host's previous world."

System 120's words mean that it is aware of the legacy space left behind by Fang Yuan from the previous world. Otherwise, it wouldn't have passed the host selection process so quickly. However, because when it found him, he was only a remnant soul. He had little of his original memories left, so the space treated him as an ordinary tasker.

The World Sea Space has experienced countless worlds, and the taskers come from all walks of life. They've seen all sorts of gods and monsters; in their eyes, his legacy from a major world is just ordinary, at most someone with slightly better aptitude.

A line of text appeared in Fang Yuan's vision.

There were two options below. Yes, or no.

Simultaneously, in Fang Yuan's eyes, flower petals appeared out of thin air and drifted down.

"Welcome back, 120."

A silvery-white light spread from the point he touched, like a drop of water falling into the water. The light washed over his consciousness, over his limbs, over his breath. It was very light, neither hot nor cold, as if something deep within his body had been awakened.

The morning light outside seemed to brighten for a moment. The pothos on the windowsill swayed without wind, its leaves trembling slightly. The drop of water that hadn't been turned off properly in the sink fell at that moment.

Fang Yuan opened his eyes.

"I'm glad to fight alongside you, Host."

System 120's voice became lively and vibrant, just like when they first met.

Unchanged in their initial intentions, the same old friends remain.

“The revival of spiritual energy.”

Chapter 28 Spiritual Qi Revival


The "spiritual energy revival" refers to the sudden replenishment of Earth (or another world) with a high concentration of spiritual energy after a period of "spiritual energy depletion/the end of the Dharma era."

Gu Changming wasn't unfamiliar with this concept. As someone who had read widely, from classic literature to novels, from male-oriented fantasy to female-oriented fiction, he was a man of broad interests.

This wasn't a novel concept, but he hadn't expected it to come from Fang Yuan's mouth.

He had previously encountered a strange encounter with electricity and had considered fantasy. However, at that time, he felt they hadn't yet encountered such things.

Wow, it really exists! (((ﾟДﾟ)))
