Half a day later, Fang Yuan slowly awoke in a simple farmhouse. His wounds had been carefully bandaged, and although the pain was still excruciating, the near-death weakness had subsided considerably.

He tried to move his fingers, and System 120's voice immediately rang out in his consciousness: "Host, you're finally awake! You scared me to death, waaaaah..."

"How long have I been asleep?" Fang Yuan asked in his consciousness.

"About half a day. The people who rescued you were from the Hunyuan Sect, an elder with two disciples, who happened to be passing by that forest."

Fang Yuan nodded slightly and listened intently. He could faintly hear voices outside, but his body was weak and his senses were dulled, so he couldn't hear clearly, but System 120 thoughtfully relayed the information to him in his consciousness.

"...This child is from a nearby village. He's a pitiful soul." The voice of a stranger, tinged with a sigh, spoke.

"His family had saved some money from selling mountain goods and were planning to move to town. They traveled with a caravan, but they encountered bandits on the way. His parents fought desperately to hold off the bandits, securing a path for him to escape to the city. Alas, even seasoned travelers wouldn't dare venture onto those mountain paths."

The bandits chose this mountain because of its rugged terrain, winding and twisting, making it easy to lose one's way. Even experienced travelers had to travel in groups, let alone a child.

But there was no other way. Adults wouldn't survive that situation, let alone a child. Escaping might be a near-death experience, while staying with the bandits meant certain death.

"And his parents..." came the voice of the boy named Xiao Tian.

"Gone." The merchant sighed. "Only me and one of my servants remained from the caravan. The rest are dead."

A moment of silence fell outside.

Mu Jingxing's voice rang out, deep and steady, yet carrying a barely perceptible heaviness: "This year's drought has caused widespread crop failure, leaving many destitute and forced to become bandits. The suffering... the suffering of the suffering."

He's probably staying here to collect ransom from his family. That servant was likely left to run errands, and Fang Yuan probably got lost in the mountains and couldn't endure it any longer.

They came down the mountain today to earn some money and buy some supplies. They'd only been down a short distance when they spotted a group of bandits and followed them back up.

He paused, then asked, "Does this child have any relatives?"

The merchant shook his head. "No. He doesn't have any close relatives in the village. These years are tough for everyone, that's why his family wanted to go to the city. Sigh, who would have thought..."

The atmosphere outside became tense.

Just then, Mu Chen suddenly tugged at Mu Jingxing's sleeve, as if remembering something, and whispered a few words.

Mu Jingxing's heart stirred, and he turned and went back into the house. Fang Yuan sensed someone approaching and instinctively closed his eyes, slowing his breathing.

A warm hand rested on his pulse again. This time, the hand lingered for a long time, its internal energy slowly and meticulously circulating within him, while simultaneously moving over Fang Yuan's body, checking his recovery.

After a long silence, Mu Jingxing withdrew his hand, a glint of light flashing in his eyes.

He stepped outside, nodded to Mu Chen, and said in a low voice, a hint of barely suppressed surprise in his voice, "You're right. This child... is indeed unusual."

Mu Chen's gaze sharpened: "What does Master mean?"

"He's a good prospect."

Mu Jingxing examined Fang Yuan's physical condition and found that Fang Yuan's recovery speed was astonishing. According to the survivors, the robbery had occurred five days prior.

Logically, such a young child in the mountains, even if mature, should have suffered numerous internal injuries. He was barely breathing when they found him, yet Mu Jingxing's internal energy revealed Fang Yuan's truly unusual condition.

In just half a day, without any rest, only a simple application of external medicine, his external injuries were almost completely healed, and his internal injuries were remarkably few.

This talent…

“This child is destined for our sect!”

The two walked outside, and Mu Chen said, “Master, what do you mean…”

Mu Jingxing looked at Mu Chen and smiled, “Isn’t that what you said?”

“Looks like I’ll have another junior brother.”

Mu Jingxing smiled and instructed Mu Chen, “We’ll discuss this later. Take this child to a nearby town and settle him down. Take good care of him. Once I’ve dealt with these bandits, I’ll join you.”

It’s not just Fang Yuan who’s pitiful now. Mu Jingxing couldn’t bring himself to abandon the people he’d saved for Fang Yuan’s sake.

“Yes, Master.”

Inside the room, System 120 exclaimed excitedly, “Host, host, I told you this was a super excellent prospect! Look at you, you’re already…”

But Fang Yuan didn’t answer; the only response was the sound of breathing.



Chapter 32 The Stepping Stone for the Wuxia Male Protagonist: The Holy Son 2


System 120 sighed, listening to Fang Yuan's steady breathing and the conversation between Mu Chen and Mu Jingxing outside.

Thinking of the source energy it had given Fang Yuan, a ripple of emotion stirred within it.

It controlled itself so as not to disturb Fang Yuan's rest.

"Waaah, my source energy!"

"The source energy I painstakingly accumulated!"

After Fang Yuan fainted, System 120 worried that its host and Fang Yuan would have to return home so soon after leaving for their mission, affecting their evaluation.

They weren't like before. Before, even the useless among them had a guaranteed minimum income; now they were running their own business, their income depended on themselves.

If the first job didn't go well, things would get tough for them and Fang Yuan.

There was nothing they could do; they couldn't really blame System 120 and Fang Yuan. After all, they were still newbies, never having completed a single proper mission. Becoming the world's consciousness on their first try was like starting a business after only two days of working. If it weren't for the mountain of gold Fang Yuan possessed, which System 120 found incredibly tempting...

It's a case of "as long as they dig them out, with the support of the space, they can survive until the world advances to the Great Thousand World."

This perfectly aligns with System 120's wishes; a steady, long-term approach is the key. In System 120's eyes, this is similar to passing the space mission exam with all their might.

System 120 admits that if he had a choice, he'd still think working on missions in the space with Fang Yuan wouldn't be bad. But then again, isn't being the world's will and the boss a much better option?

Furthermore, regarding the situation that Fang Yuan and they encountered the first time, did the space really not know...?

System 120 didn't dare to think about it too much. For now, it's all about fate; nothing is absolute, and human effort accounts for seven-tenths.

However, having originally planned to work with Fang Yuan this time, giving away this source of energy means he'll have to go back to work, take on side jobs, and save money.

Outside the farmhouse on the other side:

"Wandering souls, wandering souls, listen closely, may you journey east to Penglai Island, south to Zhuling Palace, west to the Vajra Ground, north to escape the bitter cold, hear the scriptures in the Northern Palace, hear the repentance in the Southern Palace. Relying on the power of the Dao, for the best cause, sincerely recite, and may you be reborn in the Heavenly Venerable's realm, with inconceivable merit."

Mu Jingxing had just finished a ritual for the deceased; the lingering sound of the copper bell still echoed in the treetops. Xiao Tian squatted to the side, tidying up the incense and ritual implements, his face even more ashen than the ashes on the offering table. Mu Chen was kneeling on the ground, changing the bandages of an old man with a severed right arm. His movements were extremely light and steady; the old man gasped in pain but gritted his teeth and remained silent.

Afterwards, Xiao Tian couldn't help but sigh, "We haven't been down the mountain for only three months." He stuffed the copper bell into his bag, his voice low, as if squeezed out between clenched teeth, "These scoundrels have harmed so many people. Damn it, it's all that dog emperor's fault—"

Before he could finish, Mu Chen's hand was already covering his mouth.

"Junior brother, be careful what you say…"

Mu Chen's expression remained unchanged, his hand pressing down. Xiao Tian struggled, whimpering, "Waaaaah, waaaah."

Seeing this, Mu Jingxing was also helpless. His fourth disciple had two older brothers who had joined the army, saying they wanted to make a name for themselves.

Xiao Taijing, the two elder brothers, joined the army twenty years ago. At that time, Prince Qian had just raised the banner of the Xuan Yu Army, proclaiming his intention to conquer foreign tribes and expand territory. Many, driven by patriotic fervor, rushed north. Eight years have passed, and not a single letter has been sent home. The Xiao family knew this, which was why they sent their youngest son, Xiao Tian, ​​to the Hunyuan Sect—at least he had martial arts talent and wouldn't be conscripted.

"I sigh deeply and wipe away my tears, lamenting the hardships of the people's lives."

"This year's harvest is even worse. Even within the Hunyuan Sect near the Hengyi Mountains, some are considering becoming bandits. Keep in mind, they're near the sea!"

"If it's like this here, what about the people elsewhere?"

"Alright, Mu Chen, release Xiao Tian."

Mu Chen released his grip as instructed. Xiao Tian rubbed his face, still somewhat unwilling, but ultimately said nothing more.

Seeing Xiao Tian's somewhat resentful expression, Mu Jingxing spoke up: "I know you harbor resentment, but the people haven't been settled yet, and we need the local Wu'an's help. We should be careful with our words and actions."

The two nodded quickly upon hearing this. Xiao Tian said, "It was my fault."

"That child we picked up earlier," Mu Jingxing changed the subject, "I examined his bones."

Xiao Tian looked over, startled: "What's wrong, Master?"

"Good bone structure, just the right weight."

Martial arts aptitude refers to one's physical constitution and meridians. These are paramount in learning martial arts techniques. Cultivation requires a combination of meticulous practice and physical exertion. Insufficient physical constitution makes it difficult to even begin learning any technique or martial art, resulting in a weak physique. Meridians are the key to mastering martial arts techniques. Cultivation emphasizes the three treasures of essence, qi, and spirit. Insufficient meridians hinder internal energy cultivation, causing techniques to progress slowly, and some martial arts become useless in one's hands.

As for comprehension, that's another matter entirely.

This is elusive and difficult to discern. While the former can be assessed through internal energy and the experience of disciples, the latter relies purely on personal observation.

Therefore, it's usually not recorded in aptitude but listed separately.

Fang Yuan's body is that of a hunter, so he naturally doesn't lack meat. The system's choice of 120 is undoubtedly the best, so his aptitude is unquestionable.

When Mu Jingxing spoke, his tone carried an unusual seriousness. "What's even more remarkable is that his external injuries have already begun to heal and scab over in just half a day. Some of the larger wounds, after my internal sutures, have already scabbed over. This kind of talent is truly rare."

Xiao Tian blinked upon hearing this, then suddenly laughed out loud: "Wouldn't little Mu Ling be overjoyed to know? She always complains about being the youngest and always getting the short end of the stick; now she finally has someone to hold her back."

Mu Chen didn't speak, but the corners of his mouth twitched slightly.

Mu Jingxing didn't respond to this, but continued, "Do you all remember the opening passage of our Hunyuan Sect's *Hunyuan Yangsheng Jing*?"

*Yangsheng Jing* is the foundational introductory martial arts of various sects in the contemporary era, encompassing all walks of life, from commoners to nobles and the lowest classes.

The difference lies mainly in the different directions of development among the various schools, but the most basic chapter is revered as the number one martial arts technique of its time, and it wouldn't be an exaggeration to call it the general outline of martial arts.

Mu Chen's expression shifted: "Master said... 'Qi arises from the innate, requiring no external seeking; the internal organs are self-sufficient, and the whole body is at peace'?"

"Indeed," Mu Jingxing nodded. "Our founder established this school because of his extraordinary physique; he was taken as a disciple by that person."

The creator of the *Nourishing Life Classic* was a renowned medical master, a scholar of both heaven and man, who broke free from intellectual constraints, personally dissecting the human body to explore the five elements within it and the transformations of various rare and exotic animals.

He created the *Nourishing Life Classic*, a text accessible to everyone and considered the foundation of later martial arts, where all techniques are based on its core principles. Later, he combined this with various intractable diseases, using the *Nourishing Life Classic* as its foundation, embracing diverse influences to create the supreme medical classic, the *Golden Chamber Prescriptions*.

He became a grandmaster, single-handedly elevating medicine to the pinnacle of his time. Those who studied medicine revered him.

He was known as the Immortal Physician.

Later, it was heard that a blond-haired, blue-eyed extraordinary person overseas, seeking to explore the mysteries of the human body, led three hundred disciples on a journey abroad.

The disciples who remained in Shenzhou began to flourish, and after a century of evolution, their influence spread throughout the Shenzhou continent.

Among them, Medicine King Valley is the largest branch.

One of the remaining disciples of the Primordial Master Hunyuan possessed a special constitution. His five internal organs were perfectly integrated, and without conscious effort, his Qi and blood flowed naturally through his meridians, resulting in a recovery speed far exceeding that of ordinary people. After becoming a disciple of the Immortal Physician, he founded the Hunyuan Sect based on the *Hunyuan Yangsheng Jing* (Classic of Nourishing Life) and his own unique understanding.

His ultimate technique, the *Hunyuan Yangsheng Jing*, is of a balanced and harmonious nature, adept at regulating the Yin and Yang and the five energies within the body, nourishing the body, and enabling practitioners to recover at a speed far exceeding that of ordinary people. Its warm and gentle internal energy is also a powerful tool for modern medicine in saving lives.

Reaching a high level of mastery in cultivation yields benefits such as longevity and immunity from all diseases, making it a masterpiece combining medicine and martial arts.

The founder of the Hunyuan Sect once said that if future generations could cultivate this technique to a high level, they could travel to Medicine King Valley to explore the supreme medical classic, *The Golden Chamber of Materia Medica*.

"When I examined this child's internal energy just now, I found that although there were no traces of cultivation within him, the flow of life force was extremely similar to what was described in the founder's notes."

Xiao Tian's eyes widened upon hearing this: "Doesn't that mean he was born to join our Hunyuan Sect?"

"Constitution is one thing, temperament is another." Mu Jingxing withdrew his gaze. "Let's settle the people first; this matter is not urgent."

The three said no more. They buried the remaining unclaimed bones on the spot, performed the ritual, and then led the rescued refugees down the mountain.

Half a day later, they arrived at Qingyu Town, where Mu Jingxing personally met with Wu An, the local resident.

The martial arts master of Qingyu Town, surnamed He, was in his forties. He practiced external martial arts, his body as strong as iron. Having served as the town's martial arts master for twelve years, he held considerable prestige. The position of martial arts master had been established since the Xia Dynasty, held by outstanding local martial artists to assist the government in managing local security, serving as a buffer between local powerful families and the imperial court.

However, this position was not hereditary—martial arts were not based on lineage, as the *Yang Sheng Jing* (a classic text on health preservation) provided a foundation for almost everyone.

One day, a young man from the mountains might have a sudden enlightenment and rise to prominence, so the turnover of martial arts masters was far more frequent than that of official positions, and thus more widely accepted.

Upon hearing Mu Jingxing's purpose, He Wu'an readily agreed, arranging for the refugees to be resettled in batches in several vacant farms outside the town, and also sending for the town's doctors. Upon arriving, the doctors immediately bowed to Mu Jingxing and his entourage, addressing them as "Teachers."

The town here isn't far from the Hunyuan Sect, and many doctors go up the mountain to study for a period of time. However, Mu Jingxing, an outer disciple of the sect, looks no more than 30 years old, but his actual age is much older. It's not that he doesn't look old because his sect's cultivation methods are excellent and his power is profound, putting him at his peak.

Although the sect is a hundred miles away from the town, its members and the local residents have countless connections. Calling them local bullies wouldn't be an exaggeration.

After all, at this age, even a minor illness or ailment can be life-threatening for ordinary people. Why wouldn't people try to cultivate a good relationship with a highly skilled, virtuous, and long-established sect?

So why did they steal their inheritance? Heh, if someone truly had that ability, the entire Hunyuan Sect would naturally welcome them with open arms.

Why do you think their founder built the mountain gate in that remote corner? Disciples without some achievement have to rely on their masters to descend the mountain.

It's simply because studying medicine is incredibly difficult!

Memorizing the human body's meridians and skeleton is just the beginning. There are also various herbs and the appearances of birds of prey to memorize. This requires diligent study and practice, taking years to master. And then, just studying isn't enough; to improve your skills and grow a year older, you have to go down the mountain for practical experience. You can't rely on family traditions or schools; you have to become a chief physician at any pharmacy down the mountain to barely pass the initial stage.

This single hurdle has stumped countless students. Now, medicine is prominent, and universities are no longer as simple as they used to be. Besides the basic internal and external medicine, countless sub-disciplines have emerged.

Pharmacy, the five internal organs, skeletal science, and so on—these subjects are still increasing.

In Tai'an in 16 years, Medicine King Valley proposed making dentistry a separate department; in Taijing 18 years, stomach diseases were separated from internal medicine and established as a separate department; in Taijing 20 years, gynecology was established; and in Taijing 21 years, improvements to herbal medicine cultivation were proposed.

Those who truly understand it know how weighty the term "prominent field" is today.

Countless talented individuals have dedicated themselves to its development, paving the way for its advancement.

Confucianism, Taoism, medicine, and Mohism stood as four pillars of society, along with Buddhism and Taoism, which had recently flowed in from the West. After four generations of capable rulers, the people of the Great Qian Dynasty recovered, and the youth of various families entered a period of rapid development.

This only covers medical skills. In martial arts, rigorous training in the coldest and hottest winters is fundamental. The Hunyuan Sect emphasizes a combination of static and dynamic exercises, requiring daily arduous practice followed by the study of medical classics and historical events.

Even so, countless people aspire to join their sect each year. Over the years, while the Hunyuan Sect has occupied two mountain peaks, its disciples have never exceeded a few hundred. However, its training of physicians has spread throughout the entire mountain range, even influencing physicians in the Great Qian Palace.

Many more often, after completing their medical training, a certificate is all that's needed to advance their ranks.

Many of the doctors in these towns came through this process, failing to pass the initial screening, and were instead sent to Nanshan to promote and develop medicine.

Mu Chen explained the prescription and precautions for the wounded soldier in detail, finally feeling relieved.

That night, the three of them booked two rooms at the Yuelai Inn in town, settled the child on the bed, and took turns watching over him until he woke up.

Fang Yuan woke up the next morning.

When he opened his eyes, he saw unfamiliar beams and a blue cloth curtain, and smelled a faint scent of herbs. The sky was just beginning to lighten outside, and he could vaguely hear the sounds of people at the morning market.

Mu Jingxing sat on a chair beside the bed, holding a cup of cold tea, having waited for an unknown amount of time.

"Awake?" He set down the teacup, his voice calm. "Do you feel unwell anywhere?"

Fang Yuan propped himself up on the bed, his mind a jumbled mess, as if stuffed with cotton wool. At the same time, a childish voice echoed deep within his consciousness—

"Host, you have amnesia. Don't acknowledge anything, don't say anything. Stay calm, do as I say."

It was System 120.

Fang Yuan remained expressionless, shaking his head blankly.

Mu Jingxing studied him for a moment, then asked, "What's your name? Where do you live?"

Fang Yuan opened his mouth, a perfectly timed look of confusion and panic flashing in his eyes, then he lowered his head and clutched the corner of the blanket. It was the reaction of someone who truly couldn't remember anything—not acting, but genuine bewilderment.

Mu Jingxing looked into his eyes; Fang Yuan's eyes revealed an innocence.

"I...I don't know."

Mu Jingxing was silent for a moment, then held out his hand: "Give me your hand."

Fang Yuan hesitated before offering his right hand. Mu Jingxing placed three fingers on his wrist pulse, a wisp of internal energy probing into his meridians like a thread. After a moment, he withdrew his hand, nodding thoughtfully.

The result was the same as his examination yesterday—no trace of cultivated internal energy, but his internal organs were vibrant, and a faint trace of the *Nourishing Life Classic*'s energy was circulating within his meridians. This wasn't surprising; yesterday, to stabilize the child's injuries, he had indeed channeled some internal energy into him, using the most basic warming method of the *Nourishing Life Classic*.

However, the child's body accepted it so naturally, as if he were born to circulate this technique.

At this moment, his belief that this child was destined for his sect grew even stronger.

Even if he lacked talent in medicine, with this innate physique alone, he was an unparalleled genius for cultivating their sect's techniques!

At the very least, he was a master of Qi and meridians! If he had some talent in medicine, innate talent was within reach!

As for amnesia, it was mostly due to the shock of a sudden event, followed by days of wandering in the mountains, leaving him mentally unstable. He had seen similar cases in medical books, especially common in children.

"Do you really remember nothing?" Mu Jingxing asked again.

Fang Yuan's fingers tightened slightly around the corner of the blanket, his knuckles turning white, and his lips pressed into a thin line. These subtle movements didn't escape Mu Jingxing's notice; it was clear he wasn't faking it.

Mu Jingxing made up his mind.

He stood up and walked to the window, the morning light falling on his thin profile. He was only in his early forties, but because the sect leader had gone into seclusion and all the affairs had fallen on his shoulders, there was already a hint of weariness between his brows.

“My name is Mu Jingxing, the acting head of the Hunyuan Sect. You, child, have been wandering alone and have lost your memory. If no one takes care of you, you probably won't survive this winter.” He turned around and looked at Fang Yuan on the bed. “Our Hunyuan Sect is founded on medicine and martial arts, and we place the utmost importance on cultivating our minds and helping others. Your constitution is quite compatible with our sect's techniques. I wish to take you as my disciple and bring you up the mountain to cultivate. Are you willing?”

Fang Yuan looked up, the confusion still lingering in his eyes. After a moment's realization, he nodded vigorously.

Mu Jingxing smiled slightly and patted Fang Yuan's head. "Good. From this day forward, you are the sixth disciple of my Hunyuan Sect."

Xiao Tian's voice came from outside the door: "Master! Is the child awake? I brought him some porridge—"

The door opened, and Xiao Tian, ​​carrying a bowl of hot porridge, poked half his body in, meeting Mu Jingxing's ambiguous smile. He paused, then, seeing Fang Yuan sitting on the bed, his eyes lit up.

"Awake? Come, come, have some porridge!" He placed the bowl on the table, leaned over the bed, and grinned as he looked Fang Yuan up and down. "Junior Brother, let me tell you, our Hunyuan Sect is great in every way, except our seniority is low. With you here, I'm no longer the youngest. You don't know, your Senior Sister Mu Ling always takes advantage of being the youngest and pushes all the chores onto me..."

Mu Chen, who had appeared at the doorway sometime earlier, coughed lightly upon hearing this.

Xiao Tian immediately shut up, giving an awkward smile.

Mu Jingxing ignored their little antics and simply said to Fang Yuan, "Eat something first, then we'll head back to the mountain."

Fang Yuan took the bowl of porridge and took a sip. The warm white porridge slid down his throat, and he heard the childish cheer of System 120 deep within his consciousness.

"It's done!" The system's voice carried a sense of relief, as if it had just escaped death. "Host, we succeeded this time! I told you this was a super outstanding candidate!"

Fang Yuan lowered his eyelashes and calmly took another sip of his porridge.

He silently gave 120 a thumbs up. "I misunderstood you before. 120, you're truly a great system."

Fang Yuan: (*＾3＾)/～☆

System 120: Ｏ(≧∇≦)Ｏ

The sky outside the window was completely bright. The outline of the Hengyi Mountain Range in the distance was faintly visible in the morning mist. Beyond the mountains lay the sea, and the sea breeze swept over the ridges into Qingyu Town, carrying a salty and warm scent.

The Hunyuan Sect was there.

And from this day forward, the name Fang Yuan would be bound together with this name, leaving a significant mark on history books.



Chapter 33 The Stepping Stone for the Wuxia Male Protagonist: The Holy Son 3


Fang Yuan finished his bowl of porridge and placed it on the table. Mu Jingxing then asked Mu Chen to pay the bill while he went to exchange medical knowledge with the town's doctor. Xiao Tian was instructed to buy some dry food and a change of clothes.

With everyone busy, Fang Yuan was left alone. At that moment, System 120's voice rang in Fang Yuan's mind.

"Host, we've struck gold! We've struck gold!"

Fang Yuan was startled by the sudden cheer and subconsciously asked, "What's so great about striking gold?"

System 120 explained that the difficulty of this mission was becoming a Holy Son, which was the biggest challenge.

What? You're asking why you can't just transmigrate into a Holy Son? System 120 replied that if it were that easy, what would be the point of having them?

It's not impossible, but that's something only wandering systems do.

If you do it without being discovered, it's fine. But once discovered, well, you'll see if the world's will punish you.

System 120 said, "I once met a guy who transmigrated into the body of a powerful family's eldest son, worked his way up to become emperor, but after less than a year, the chosen one of destiny came knocking. Five hundred thousand troops against 30,000—good heavens, without even a pretense, he unleashed a massive meteor shower, completely destroying that wandering system.

Keep in mind, that guy was a collateral descendant of a powerful family, the kind whose parents were all dead, who rose to power through sheer hard work, and yet he ended up like this."

Hearing this, Fang Yuan raised an eyebrow. Sure enough, there's no such thing as a free lunch. If you don't handle it properly, you'll regret it tenfold.

The problem lies in the fact that nobody comes to their mission: it's time-consuming, low-rewarding, and incredibly demanding.

Although their mission doesn't require becoming a "holy son" of any particular region—Confucianism, Taoism, Legalism, Medicine, or Mohism—anyone other than Taoist or Legalist is acceptable.

Subtracting the two the protagonist brings, none of those three are easy to deal with.

The remaining three are the prominent schools of thought: Confucianism, Medicine, and Mohism. None of them are easy to contend with.

"For Confucianism, you need to study the Four Books and Five Classics, the classics, the philosophical works, and the collected works. You'll be competing fiercely with those who specialize in the Six Arts. Even then, success is difficult. In this era where the *Classic of Nourishing Life* is widely known, people live longer. Those Confucian disciples who are thoroughly proficient in the Six Arts will live even longer, and they're also skilled in martial arts and have sharp minds. Standing out is extremely difficult."

"The early stages of the story are alright; if you can find a teacher, you might be able to succeed. But later, when the Great Qian Dynasty opens the imperial examinations, the competition becomes even fiercer."

As for the remaining two schools, let's not even talk about Medicine.

System 120 will focus on the Mohist school, emphasizing universal love and non-aggression. The Mohist knights-errant, renowned for their mechanical arts, have found new life in this world under the influence of internal energy.

The Mohist school is arguably the most deeply hidden force in this world. However, for those undertaking the mission, as long as they have the right temperament and ability, becoming their young master is actually the easiest path.

But the requirements are high. However, the rewards in this world are low, and the time commitment is long, so many mission takers don't value this mission.

Those with the ability don't want it because of the long time commitment; those with time find the rewards too low; those with time and who don't mind the low time commitment lack the ability and are thus trapped in the spatial dimension.

System 120 is thinking this with some excitement in its mind at this moment.

"Hehe, although there were some unexpected issues and we invested a bit more of our essence, judging by this start, this mission is practically a sure thing!"

System 120, after some calculations, realized...

"Haha, there's even a profit!"

If it were anyone else in this situation, they'd at most say it's a draw, but System 120 and the others weren't after that little bit of money; they wanted this world, their reputation, and a good start.

"Host, host, just say he's a super superior candidate! If this continues, our mission will definitely be fine!"

Fang Yuan nodded in his consciousness space.

"Yeah, the beginning was a bit bumpy, but things are definitely going well now."

System 120 also breathed a sigh of relief. If things continue as they are, Fang Yuan can continue even without him.

"That's great!"

"Junior brother, junior brother?"

Mu Chen's voice brought Fang Yuan back from his consciousness space.

The two were sitting on a donkey cart loaded with medicinal herbs and daily necessities. The eldest brother, Mu Chen, held the reins loosely, letting the old gray donkey slowly make its way up the mountain path. The path was lined with lush pines and cypresses, and the occasional bird song drifted from the depths of the forest, creating a serene and tranquil scene.

"Eldest brother."

Hearing his name called, Fang Yuan knew he was lost in thought and quickly bowed to Mu Chen.

Seeing him like this, Mu Chen waved his hand casually and smiled, "It's alright, I just saw you spacing out and was afraid you'd fall."

Fang Yuan scratched the back of his head somewhat embarrassedly, revealing the appearance of a simple-minded young boy. He looked no more than fourteen or fifteen years old, with delicate features and a touch of childishness, truly resembling a boy from a farming family.

Seeing his reaction, Mu Chen smiled and said, "Sixth Junior Brother, Master has told me about your condition. I shouldn't disturb your rest, but there are other branches on the mountain besides ours, and the world isn't very peaceful right now. There are some things I still need to tell you."

Mu Chen glanced at him, then turned his gaze back to the mountain path ahead, his tone gentle: "Sixth Junior Brother, Master has already told me about your condition. I shouldn't be going on about this at this crucial time when you're recovering, but there are other branches on the mountain besides ours, and the world isn't very peaceful right now. There are some things I still need to tell you first."

Upon hearing this, Fang Yuan quickly straightened his posture and said earnestly, "Senior Brother, please speak."

Mu Chen nodded slightly, pondering for a moment, as if organizing his thoughts.

"Junior Brother should have sensed the Qi, so you must have some understanding of martial arts."

Hearing this, Fang Yuan nodded. After waking up and experiencing Mu Jingxing taking him as a disciple, he felt something different about his body.

It wasn't the "spiritual Qi revival" that System 120 had mentioned before; it was a strange feeling he hadn't experienced much before.

It was as if... as if he had gained an extra hand.

He asked System 120, but it wouldn't say. It said that they were currently playing amnesiac farm boys, and it would definitely explain later. Even if it didn't, it would be explained to the host once they were lying on the mountain.

Therefore, Fang Yuan only had a vague understanding of the internal energy within his body, mostly based on fantasies from reading novels.

"Junior Brother, the cultivation method in your body is the 'Nourishing Life Classic,' known as the number one martial art in the world, and it's also the foundation of our sect."

"The number one martial art in the world?!"

Fang Yuan was startled upon hearing this title. Was it really that powerful? He hadn't sensed anything special about it.

Mu Chen smiled and said, "This isn't something I made up. It's universally acknowledged. Everyone can practice it; it's considered the general outline of all martial arts."

He then recounted its history.

Mu Chen pointed to his arm, then to his chest and abdomen. "Martial arts cultivation, in essence, boils down to three things: essence, qi, and spirit. No matter the school or sect, the fundamental principles remain the same."

"The methods of cultivation in the world are broadly divided into two paths," Mu Chen said, holding up two fingers. "One path is from the inside out, cultivating qi and preserving spirit, using internal energy to connect the meridians—this is internal cultivation; the other path is from the outside in, tempering muscles and bones, forging the body—this is external cultivation, also known as external training."

"In the end, both paths lead to the same destination, neither superior to the other. However, the initial investment differs greatly—internal martial arts are difficult to master, requiring calmness, cultivation of qi, and the ability to perceive its sensations, often taking several years to see initial results; external martial arts are easier to master, requiring only hard work, and can strengthen muscles and bones in three to five months. But later on, internal martial arts achieve their full potential through accumulated experience, while external martial arts become increasingly difficult."

Fang Yuan listened intently and asked, "So, which path are we taking?"

"We'll mainly focus on internal martial arts, but we'll also touch upon external training," Mu Chen smiled. "Firstly, external training is too arduous and requires extensive medicinal baths and diets, which is too costly. Even I would find it difficult to support the entire department, and a single misstep can easily damage one's foundation, which doesn't align with our medical principles."

Ordinary families couldn't afford it. Moreover, internal martial arts cultivation, once reaching a certain level, increases lifespan and brings clarity of mind and spirit, offering a significant advantage whether seeking health and longevity or advancement in martial arts.

Furthermore, while external martial arts lack specific methods, internal martial arts have the *Nourishing Life Classic*. Spending money and practicing for a long time yields far better results than those expensive and dubious techniques.

Plus, with more people choosing this method, it's constantly being improved, attracting even more practitioners.

As for external martial arts, aside from the Qian Dynasty military, very few people practice it. However, Mu Chen had heard of a sect that had entered the East and was quite skilled in external martial arts; it seemed to be called Buddhism?

He paused, then continued.

"The first level of martial arts cultivates the muscles, bones, and skin. This stage is necessary for both internal and external martial arts practitioners, honing strength and enhancing blood and qi to allow the body to withstand more advanced martial arts techniques. At its peak, a single punch or kick carries hundreds of pounds of force, making it impossible for seven or eight strong men to get close."

"The second level cultivates the internal organs. Internal energy flows from the surface inwards, nourishing the organs and eliminating impurities. At this point, one is immune to all diseases, and one's physique far surpasses that of ordinary people. Reaching this stage makes living to be over a hundred years old a certainty, and peak condition can be maintained until around seventy."

Fang Yuan silently memorized this, thinking that the widespread dissemination of the *Nourishing Life Classic* and the high development of internal martial arts made this sequence of stages very fitting.

Their medical ancestor was truly remarkable, his merits immeasurable.

Mu Chen continued the introduction...

"The third level involves the unification of essence, qi, and spirit, comprehending the will of martial arts, and condensing one's qi channels," Mu Chen's tone became more solemn. "Only upon reaching this stage can one truly transcend the mortal realm. Lifespan can reach 120 years, and some exceptionally gifted individuals possess extraordinary endurance, capable of traveling 800 li in a single day."

800 li!

Fang Yuan was also astonished upon hearing this number. This distance was beyond human capabilities; even driving a car would be exhausting, let alone running it by hand.

This was beyond the reach of ordinary people.

Mu Chen seemed to see through his surprise and added unhurriedly, "This is only the third level."

"Furthermore, there is the Innate Realm." He looked up at the distant, mist-shrouded peaks, a hint of longing in his eyes. "By circulating the inner energy to sense the outer energy, the body's qi transforms into true qi, and every move is empowered by the power of heaven and earth. At this level, one's lifespan can reach one hundred and fifty years."

"And if one follows the path of external cultivation, reaching its peak leads to the External Cultivation Realm, where the physical body is flawless, the blood and qi are like mercury, and lifespan can reach three Jiazi (60 years). However, this path is extremely difficult; only a handful of people in this world can successfully traverse it."

Mu Chen stopped his explanation here, not wanting to say anything more to avoid Fang Yuan becoming overly ambitious.

Fang Yuan couldn't help but say to System 120 in his mind, "The development of this world is too outrageous!"

System 120's childish voice immediately rang out, carrying an air of self-righteous indignation: "Host, this world isn't a novel. Even if a writer could write about a world that's feudal, how could the real world remain unchanged for over 10,000 years? That's just fantasy.

Technology develops, and martial arts certainly develop too. Ordinary farmers know to improve their tools, so don't martial artists know to summarize their experiences and innovate? Host, you see martial arts as a skill; isn't technological progress a normal thing?"

Fang Yuan was momentarily speechless, realizing there was a lot of truth to this. It was indeed the fantasy novels he'd been reading had misled him; those were just other people's fantasies. How could the real world be so one-dimensional?

“Moreover,” System 120 added, “this world has a fundamental cultivation method like the *Nourishing Life Classic* circulating throughout the land. Ordinary people can live to their sixties. It would be strange if those martial artists with talent and resources didn't make a name for themselves.”

System 120 said, sighing that this mission was truly a valuable experience. Fang Yuan and he lacked real, normal mission experience, harboring too many subjective biases about the mission world, which would inevitably lead to their downfall someday.

This mission would effectively address that.

“Junior Brother?” Mu Chen noticed Fang Yuan was somewhat lost in thought again and gently called out.

“Senior Brother, please forgive me, I was too engrossed in listening.” Fang Yuan quickly regained his composure.

Mu Chen didn't mind, instead showing an approving expression: “Having this thirst for knowledge is a good thing. You'll gradually understand what I just said in the future. You have a foundation in the *Nourishing Life Classic*, which is related to our lineage's unique skills. Although it's fundamental, it's also unpredictable, so you must diligently practice it.”

Mu Chen explained, “Almost all sects use this as their foundational technique—balanced and harmonious, harmonizing body and mind, yet with a solid foundation. Moreover, it follows the same path as our ultimate technique, the *Hun Yuan Yang Sheng Jing*.”

“Hun Yuan…Yang Sheng Jing?”

Mu Chen nodded, saying, “Our sect’s founder inherited the medical skills of the Immortal Physician, deeply studied the *Yang Sheng Jing*, and combined it with his lifelong learning to create his own ultimate technique, the *Hun Yuan Yang Sheng Jing*.

This technique requires knowledge of medical principles, practice, and herbs. Currently, we lack a foundation in geography, so we first rely on the *Yang Sheng Jing* to build a solid foundation. Subsequent solutions will also be based on this.”

Fang Yuan nodded.

Mu Chen continued, “You are still young, a perfect time to lay a solid foundation. Although our school can't compare to Confucianism or Taoism in terms of support and abundance of talent, our lineage is well-established and no less capable. You don't need to worry too much. Even if you don't achieve much in medicine in the future, with your talent and aptitude, Master will definitely accept you as a disciple.”

Fang Yuan was slightly taken aback, then quickly understood. His senior brother was trying to reassure him, fearing he might be overly anxious.

“Thank you for your guidance, Senior Brother,” Fang Yuan bowed again.

Mu Chen waved his hand, his tone becoming increasingly gentle: "Master is currently acting as sect leader, and sect affairs are numerous, so he's often too busy to attend to matters. If any of you junior brothers encounter any difficulties, feel free to come to me first. Whether it's questions about cultivation techniques or problems with pharmacology, I can offer some assistance. In the future, when you practice offensive and defensive techniques, I can also spar with you."

He added, "Yes, after you join the sect, you can come to me first. Although the *Nourishing Life Classic* is balanced and moderate, given your current memory loss and the possibility of major changes, it's unlikely to be effective. But it's better to be safe than sorry. If anything seems amiss, be sure to come to me."

His tone was calm as he spoke these words, yet they were incredibly heartwarming.

This further highlighted the senior brother's refined and reliable nature.

"Yes."

Fang Yuan gazed into the distance, his mind racing as System 120 began to explain the world's situation after Mu Chen finished speaking.

The martial arts of this world had reached a considerable level. The five prominent schools of thought—Confucianism, Taoism, Medicine, and Mohism—each had their strengths, making it extremely difficult to stand out. The Confucian school required mastering the Four Books and Five Classics and the Six Arts of the Gentleman. Its disciples were already skilled in both literature and martial arts, and enjoyed long lifespans, making them the pinnacle of their respective fields.

The Legalist school had the lowest entry requirements, but almost everyone had to become an official. While joining might be easier, the officialdom was like a battlefield, filled with intricate human relationships, making it the least suitable path for Fang Yuan.

As for the Mohist school…

Fang Yuan recalled System 120's earlier analysis. The Mohists advocated universal love and non-aggression, and their disciples were mostly wandering knights. The Mohists were the most secretive, but for those undertaking missions, as long as their temperament was suitable and their abilities sufficient, becoming their young master was actually the easiest path.

Medical secrets are never easily revealed; even entering the sect is incredibly difficult.

Confucianism is all-encompassing, Legalism is hard to climb, Mohism is as insidious as water, and medicine is not only all-encompassing but also shrouded in secrecy.

Having truly understood the difficulty of this world, despite some initial setbacks, Fang Yuan was already very satisfied to have the opportunity to become a disciple of a medical family.

"Junior brother, we've arrived."

However, Fang Yuan didn't come away empty-handed. The *Nourishing Life Classic* given to him by Mu Jingxing contained many annotations, giving Fang Yuan a clearer understanding of the specific cultivation methods in this world.

For example, internal energy cultivation is like land development; cultivators use various methods to develop their internal organs, allowing their meridians and dantian to grow.

Talent, on the other hand, is the abundance of basic resources within a cultivator's body. Some people have good talent, a large and favorable environment with abundant resources, allowing for rapid development; others have poor talent, complex terrain, and difficult paths, making development difficult and slow.

Root bone can be interpreted as terrain resources, while meridians are the channels through which foreign trade is influenced; the two complement each other.

Then, in his annotations to the *Nourishing Life Classic*, Fang Yuan recognized the depth of kung fu, or the "levels" of its techniques. This represents a practitioner's understanding of martial arts and themselves.

Its name is roughly "Martial Principles."

"Martial Principles" can be interpreted as a practitioner's ability to develop resources and modify equipment. Just as more advanced equipment allows for faster resource development, reaching a certain level of "Martial Principles" also enables the development of equipment tailored to individual needs, allowing one's development speed to catch up with so-called "geniuses."

At the end of the annotations was a line of smaller print, the ink already somewhat faded: "In the path of martial arts, the further one progresses, the more important martial principles become. Those who possess only brute force but lack understanding of principles will ultimately find only illusions."

Fang Yuan understood that the requirements for martial principles increased significantly in the later stages of martial arts training.

Seeing Fang Yuan's action, Meng Ping silently opened his own book as well.

Then he looked around.

Zhao Qiming, who sat at the back of the class, came from a well-off family and had initially entered the sect with the mindset of "just getting by for three years and making it in the system."

The Hunyuan Sect's acceptance rate was pitifully low, and for three years, he hadn't been home except for a few holidays.

Even under these circumstances, getting into the Hunyuan Sect was something many would shy away from.

But he noticed that every morning when he entered the classroom, Fang Yuan was already there; every evening when he left, Fang Yuan was still there. Fang Yuan never looked at what he was doing, and probably didn't even know his name, but Zhao Qiming felt restless.

So, Zhao Qiming was unconsciously drawn in.

Those wealthy children who chose to enter the Hunyuan Sect and truly wanted to coast wouldn't be in Class B.

Most of these students had some skills and a certain arrogance.

The atmosphere of the entire class was stirred up.

Hu Hai was happy to see this happen; how could a teacher stop the students from working hard?

Anyway, the top doctors are right here!

But word still spread.

The nickname "Study Demon" originated somewhere, but by the time it reached Fang Yuan's ears, even the cafeteria staff knew about it.

The auntie serving food would give Fang Yuan two scoops of rice every time she saw him.

You ask why she knew Fang Yuan?

The reason is simple: Fang Yuan is handsome.

After three months of recuperation, his body underwent a dramatic transformation, becoming tall, handsome, and fair-skinned.

But none of this mattered to Fang Yuan.

Fang Yuan stood still, feet shoulder-width apart, knees slightly bent, spine straight, arms wrapped as if embracing a tree—a standard starting stance.

The guiding technique began during the martial arts theory class.

It wasn't a deliberate, guided movement, but a natural flow—the breath originating from the dantian, descending along the Ren meridian to the perineum, passing the coccyx, ascending along the Du meridian, passing the Mingmen, Jiaji, and Yuzhen points, reaching the Baihui point, then descending from the forehead, crossing the Magpie Bridge, and returning to the dantian.

One circle, two circles, three circles.

Fang Yuan's breathing was as steady as a mountain breeze; with each inhale and exhale, his internal energy had completed three full cycles.

Qin Zheng paused as he approached.

Fang Yuan's body remained motionless, but Qin Zheng could sense the change in his aura. A power flowed quietly within the young man, like an underground river, silent yet inexhaustible.

The natural progression.

The Small Circulation complete!

Fang Yuan opened his eyes, sensing the changes in his body. His internal energy seemed to have become more refined and easier to control.

Furthermore, Fang Yuan discovered that even without his conscious control, his internal energy was slowly circulating…

This…

“Don’t move, stand still!”

Qin Zheng spoke first after Fang Yuan opened his eyes.

He circled Fang Yuan. He gently pressed his hand on Fang Yuan’s shoulder, a wisp of internal energy drifting into his body. He felt a weak counterforce from his palm, clearly a reaction of the internal energy protecting itself.

“More than three months… almost a month…”

Qin Zheng murmured. He remembered that Mu Chen’s quarters were only five months.

Qin Zheng withdrew his hand, his voice devoid of emotion, “Next.”

Fang Yuan opened his eyes, his aura subsided, and he bowed to Qin Zheng before stepping aside.

The surrounding classmates also stopped their cultivation, hearing Qin Zheng's words.

"A little over a month…"

"Isn't that right?"

A few who were familiar with the sect's records knew that a little over a month meant five months.

"That's not…!"

"No way?! This prodigy is in our year!"

Influenced by Fang Yuan, Meng Ping and Zhao Qiming studied diligently in the sect's books. A little over a month later, they thought of the record set by Mu Chen, who was six or seven years older than them.

"Small Heavenly Cycle Perfection!" The two stared wide-eyed. "No way! So hardworking, and with such talent too!"

"Is there no way out for us?"

…………"

"Hahaha, good, good, good! My Hunyuan Sect truly produces many heroes!"

Qin Zheng dared not hide such a genius and immediately reported it. The news had already reached Mu Jingxing's desk.

Upon hearing this news, his first reaction was surprise. His Mu Chen had already surpassed the previous generation's record of eight months in five months, and now Fang Yuan had achieved the same feat in three months.

He initially thought his subordinates were joking.

But after confirming the news's authenticity, Mu Jingxing couldn't help but feel a surge of joy.

His senior brother, Li Tianran, was preparing to break through to the Innate Realm, and his disciple, Mu Chen, had already touched the threshold of Qi Meridian four years ago, perhaps even having a chance to unlock the legendary achievement.

Now, another peerless genius, Fang Yuan, had emerged—a genius he had personally brought back.

"Excellent! Excellent!"

After confirming the news, Mu Jingxing ordered that it be kept within the sect as much as possible, not allowed to leak out.

However, when Fang Yuan broke through, under the watchful eyes of everyone, some people inevitably made connections.

Three months. Small Heavenly Circuit.

The *Nourishing Life Classic* was the founding cultivation method of the Hunyuan Sect, and all disciples were well aware of its difficulty. This cultivation method wasn't known for its rapid progress; on the contrary, it was notoriously slow—slow to enter the gate, slow to circulate Qi, slow to break through to the next realm.

A normal disciple would take at least a year to go from entering the gate to achieving the perfection of the Small Heavenly Circuit. Those with less talent might take two or three years.

Some people knew Fang Yuan's usual academic performance—he was excellent in both academics and martial arts!

A rising star of the sect!

The title "Number One of the New Generation" suddenly spread.

It started when a few outer sect disciples were chatting casually in the cafeteria, saying, "That Fang Yuan in Class B this year, he's already mastered the Small Heavenly Cycle in three months!" It was true, the speaker gave a thumbs up.

At this time, Fang Yuan was still studying late into the night in his room.

Fang Yuan: ( 。＿ 。） ✎ ＿



Chapter 37 The Stepping Stone for the Male Protagonist of a Wuxia Story: The Holy Son 7


The Hunyuan Sect wasn't large, consisting of only two peaks and a few hundred members, two hundred of whom were studying medicine. News spread extremely quickly.

Fang Yuan broke through in front of everyone, setting a new record for fastest progress, and had just begun to cultivate his fantasies about martial arts.

Now, in no time, Fang Yuan had earned the title of "Number One Newcomer," with people saying he was a rising star surpassing his predecessors.

As for who the predecessors were…

Mu Chen was happy for Fang Yuan's achievement.

It was hard.

Just as he was about to run, Xiao Tian grabbed him, leading the others with a cold laugh.

"Borrow money?" Xiao Tian interrupted mercilessly, "You're of noble birth, how can you borrow money from commoners like us? You share the same surname as the Emperor, getting money is just a matter of a word! Bring mountains of gold and silver!"

When Zhao Feixing first joined the sect, he boasted to Mu Ling, who was only five years old at the time, that his ancestors were related to the royal family but had been expelled for some offense. He promised that if she followed him, she would live a life of luxury. He managed to swindle all the dried fruit from Mu Ling's hands.

She joined him in the sect and learned that although Zhao Feixing's ancestors had some connection, his status was so vast that he could marry a princess—the only difference was their surname.

Later, after mastering his skills, he encountered a group of people suffering from toothache at a meeting in Medicine King Valley. They discussed establishing toothache as a discipline. However, they lacked a stable and reliable anesthetic, which presented an opportunity.

Upon returning, he resolved to invent an anesthetic for toothache sufferers.

That would have been fine, but for some reason, his thinking took a turn. He discovered that drinking alcohol, at a certain level, could significantly reduce pain and sensation.

Higher alcohol content results in faster reactions, but excessively strong alcohol can cause severe pain if it comes into contact with a wound.

To solve this problem, Zhao Feixing spent his own money buying alcohol every day to research, but he didn't achieve anything, only accumulating more and more bottles of liquor.

His money was practically empty; he used to be a handsome young man in Zhongnei, but now he looked like he was the same age as his master, Mu Jingxing.

Zhao Feixing was speechless after being rebuffed, saying things like, "Of course I am! My ancestor got into some trouble, didn't he?" "Once I research a miracle cure, I'll have everything!" "Consider it an investment now, you'll make a fortune later," and other incomprehensible things.

"I don't care about the money! If you don't pay me, I'll put up a banner in front of your door saying you even cheat children!"

Mu Ling didn't care about the consequences; she had been fooled by this guy years ago, even losing her snacks.

He took out his own money to pay for Zhao Feixing's expenses.

The door opened, letting in a cool mountain breeze. Fang Yuan looked up and saw a man in a blue robe standing in the doorway—tall and slender, with a calm face, standing against the last rays of twilight outside. It was Mu Chen, the one who had brought him to the Hunyuan Sect.

Fang Yuan closed his book and stood up: “Senior Brother! What brings you here?”

“Your complexion is much better than when you first arrived, and your health has improved considerably,” Mu Chen said, his voice still gentle.

Fang Yuan quickly invited Mu Chen to come in and sit down. Mu Chen waved his hand: “No need. I came to see you. I heard you’ve achieved the Small Heavenly Circuit?”

“Yes,” Fang Yuan nodded honestly.

Fang Yuan was very grateful to Mu Chen. He and Xiao Tian had talked about Mu Chen, and Xiao Tian had spoken highly of him, praising his steady character, exceptional talent, and kindness towards his junior brothers and sisters while also placing great emphasis on discipline.

"Senior Brother, speaking of which, your situation is quite similar to mine, Junior Brother," Fang Yuan asked.

He inquired about the details. Xiao Tian didn't hide anything; the entire sect knew about it.

Mu Chen, like Fang Yuan, had suffered misfortune, but even more so. Just a few months after his birth, his family was attacked and he was found by Mu Jingxing, carrying hidden injuries.

Under Mu Jingxing's care, he barely managed to grow up healthy, later displaying his talent and shouldering the responsibility of leading the sect's next generation.

After achieving success, he actively fought against thugs and villains from the surrounding area, upholding justice.

Truly a righteous young hero.

However, for some reason, he wasn't well-known outside the sect.

"Junior brother, you truly possess extraordinary talent."

Mu Chen praised, his tone calm, a sense of relief born of confirmation, devoid of any jealousy.

"Thank you for the praise, senior brother," Fang Yuan thought for a moment, then realized something was amiss.

"Just lucky, just lucky."

He then cupped his hands in a slight bow.

Mu Chen's gaze swept over the open book on the table, noticing a still-wet notebook beside Fang Yuan's hand, the handwriting neat and orderly, clearly taken while reading.

"Junior Brother's diligent study is no fluke, it's simply the natural progression of things."

Suddenly, Mu Chen abruptly added, "Recently, there have been quite a few rumors about you."

Fang Yuan's face fell slightly, as if something embarrassing had been touched upon. He gave an embarrassed smile, "Senior Brother has heard about it too? I don't know how it got like that. I just... studied step by step, nothing special."

"I know," Mu Chen said. "Your diligence is genuine; I've heard about it."

Mu Chen stepped over the threshold and sat down in the chair opposite Fang Yuan.

"Master is truly right to praise your exceptional talent and extraordinary physique. When you first entered the sect, I was worried that you were too arrogant and spoiled, but I didn't expect that you would not only be exceptionally talented but also so dedicated to your studies."

As he spoke, Mu Chen looked at Fang Yuan with satisfaction.

Fang Yuan, having seen his share of grand occasions, nodded respectfully, acknowledging his master's praise.

Seeing Fang Yuan's composure, Mu Chen admired him even more.

Young and impetuous, easily swayed by fleeting fame, but Mu Chen saw none of this in Fang Yuan.

“I’ve heard about your recent reputation,” Mu Chen’s tone became more serious. “Everyone says you might be the top student in this year’s freshmen. Master sent me to see you, not just to check on your progress—I wanted to speak with you in person.”

Mu Chen didn’t mince words; he wasn’t one for empty pleasantries:

“You have talent and are willing to work hard, which is the most valuable thing. But it’s precisely at times like these that you need to remain calm. Many talented seniors in the sect started out at their peak, but later faded into obscurity.

It wasn’t because they lacked talent, nor because they didn’t work hard enough. Quite the opposite, it was because they worked too hard, pushing themselves too hard—excessive rigidity leads to breakage; or they lost their way because of fleeting fame.”

Reputation, seemingly ethereal, is like mist, most easily influencing a Daoist.

Mu Chen paused, looking at Fang Yuan.

“Three years is a long time, long enough to wear down a person's ambition; three years is also short, if you don't give it your all, you'll be left behind. You're not the kind who works themselves to the bone, nor are you the kind who slack off half-heartedly. You have the 'steadiness' Master spoke of, and seeing it today puts my mind at ease.”

The earth is dry, and virtue carries all things.

Mu Chen knew Fang Yuan had his own sense of propriety, so he didn't say anything more.

After saying this, he turned and left, his blue robe gradually blurring in the twilight, leaving behind a bottle of medicine on the seat, finally disappearing around the corner.

"The Nourishing Essence Pill has the effect of nourishing the vital energy and strengthening the foundation. Take one pill every three days, and do not overdo it. It is best to take it before the medicinal bath."

Fang Yuan looked at the instructions in his hand, a warm feeling welling up in his heart.

Thinking of his empty reputation, he knew he had only reached this point by relying on the little essence left by System 120 and diligently cultivating according to the system's plan. What right did he have to be complacent?

Fang Yuan took a deep breath, gathering his chaotic thoughts.

His journey in this world had only just begun. System 120 was still on a mission far away, and all he could do was to establish a firm foothold at this starting point and climb up step by step. Not for fame, not for the empty title of "Number One"—those things were meaningless to him.

He came to learn the extraordinary system. This was his fundamental mission in this world.

And the path to transcendence was never a sprint, but a long marathon.

Fang Yuan picked up the book from his bedside table, turned to the page with the note tucked inside, and immersed himself once more in the densely packed meridian diagrams and pharmacological formulas.

Outside the window, the night in the Hunyuan Sect was quiet and deep, the distant sound of flowing water from the mountain stream faintly audible, like the long, drawn-out breath of the earth.

First, there was Qin Xijiao's confirmation during the martial arts class that Fang Yuan had "opened the Small Heavenly Circuit." Then, Mu Chen was seen visiting Fang Yuan's residence that evening. The strongest senior disciple of the younger generation in the Hunyuan Sect, usually reclusive and gentle, rarely initiating contact with others, had made a special trip to see a new disciple who had only been with the sect for three months. What did this mean? Everyone had their own interpretation.

But the most reasonable and intriguing interpretation was—Peak Master Mu had already accepted Fang Yuan as a disciple.

Moreover, someone discovered that Fang Yuan had returned with Elder Mu Jingxing.

Suddenly, more figures were casually passing by Fang Yuan's residence than usual.

Some wanted to see what this legendary academic demon looked like, some wondered what made him so special that the senior disciple would personally visit him, and others were simply curious—was someone who had achieved the Small Heavenly Circuit after only three months of study truly three-headed and six-armed?

"It looks like him, it's him."

"Nothing special about him. No three-headed and six-armed at all."

Some people noticed the difference in Fang Yuan's appearance.

The young man wore a simple white robe, his tall figure almost blending into the sunlight. His hair was held up by a single, simple green wooden hairpin, and his loose sleeves gave him an air of purity and untouched by worldly concerns.

His eyes held a sharp, cold glint, like distant, misty mountains, forever unattainable.

Yet, his demeanor was clear and profound, like a gentle spring rain, exuding a warm and serene gentleness.

Truly, he possessed an extraordinary bearing.

Fang Yuan was completely oblivious to these gazes. He still left home on time, stepping out into the morning mist, and returned at midnight, bathed in starlight. The school lights, as always, burned until the very end, and his figure was still present on the martial arts and theory classroom.

After that night, Fang Yuan's cultivation rhythm became more steady.

More rhythmic, balanced, and his mind more peaceful.

He consciously began to control his daily learning tasks within a manageable range—no more exceeding them, no more anxiety. Steadiness was more important than speed. This was what this plant, which had lived for countless years, excelled at.

The system detected his change in status and quietly recorded: "Host's psychological resilience rating increased. Current status: Ideal learning curve."

Fang Yuan was unaware of this. He only knew that after Mu Chen's words, the somewhat restless seed in his heart had been gently pressed deeper into the soil.

He will grow. No rush.

As Mu Chen said, one must proceed step by step, like those predecessors who have walked steadily before the gates of the Hunyuan Sect for a thousand years.

And those rumors about him, whether sincere praise or bitter criticism, are merely a passing breeze at the foot of the mountain.

The flowing water, not striving for today, but for a hundred years.

A figure dressed in white, with a gentle yet somewhat aloof demeanor, was reading a book. Beside him was an exquisite bronze model.
