Chapter 38 The Stepping Stone for the Male Protagonist of a Wuxia Story: The Holy Son 8


The young man in the room was indeed Fang Yuan. As for why he was known as a surgical genius...

Let's not dwell on his experiences over the past three years.

Fang Yuan had grown even taller than he had in three years, with broad shoulders, a narrow waist, and long, powerful limbs. He possessed a natural air of authority.

During these three years, the Hunyuan Sect had made considerable progress in its research on Miao witchcraft, attracting many Taoist masters to visit and exchange ideas. They also spread the Hunyuan Sect's theories on the natural body.

Two years ago, a Taoist master came to the Hunyuan Sect to discuss pharmacology. He happened to see Fang Yuan practicing guiding techniques by the roadside and was deeply impressed. He praised Fang Yuan's refined spirit and elegant bearing, saying he possessed the qualities of a Taoist master.

Grabbing Fang Yuan's hand, he asked if he had taken a master, claiming he was a disciple of the Zixia Temple, studying under Master Wei. He said that returning to the Zixia Temple with him would be very rewarding, completely disregarding the airs of a Taoist master or a high-level expert.

If Mu Chen hadn't happened to be searching for the Taoist master who had delivered the visiting card and hadn't intervened while Fang Yuan was struggling with him, Fang Yuan would almost have been taken back to the Zixia Temple to become a Taoist apprentice.

This matter wasn't over yet. Afterwards, rumors somehow spread that there was a handsome and ethereal young healer within the Hunyuan Sect, which somehow made Fang Yuan's name known throughout the Hengyi Mountain Range.

Fang Yuan put down his notebook, raised his head, his gaze clear as the moon, and said in a steady voice, "Have them bring him up. Tell them I'll be waiting at the medicine hut."

The person outside responded, and their footsteps quickly faded into the distance. Fang Yuan put away his notebook, took a clean white robe from the wall and put it on, then slung a wooden medicine box over his shoulder and went out.

The sunlight outside was perfect.

As Fang Yuan walked along the road to the medicine furnace, many of his fellow disciples greeted him with a bow.

Among them were several senior disciples who appeared older than Fang Yuan.

A young disciple, with a youthful face and looking no more than eleven or twelve, asked the senior disciple who had shown him around the sect with some curiosity:

"This senior brother doesn't look very old, only a few years older than me. Why do the senior brothers and sisters treat him with such respect?"

The senior disciple who had shown him around the sect smiled and explained gently, "Our sect is founded on medicine and martial arts. Those who are skilled are our teachers, so age is irrelevant."

The new disciple, still puzzled, understood. While this was true, medicine differed from martial arts. While one could hone one's skills quickly in youth, it required time to accumulate experience. Moreover, the *Nourishing Life Classic* was widely available; as long as one's medical skills were up to par, with sufficient food and clothing and proper care, one's condition wouldn't easily decline—it was the kind of skill that grew increasingly valuable.

He observed that Fang Yuan, at such a young age, had already impressed his fellow disciples. Medicine was different from other skills; theoretical knowledge was ultimately superficial, and true understanding required practice.

Without experience and achievements, it would be difficult for the others to be convinced.

Fang Yuan, walking in front, had made great progress in his internal energy over the past three years, reaching a profound level of skill. This wasn't even considering his exceptional talent and heightened senses; he had overheard the conversation of the two people behind him.

For some reason, this scene felt strangely familiar (；￣д￣).

Indeed, as the two behind him said, Fang Yuan's respect among the sect members was inextricably linked to his battle achievements.

This all started with a strange and unusual event.

Last autumn, a group of people arrived in Qingzhou City at the foot of the mountain, carrying an iron cage containing a monster that was neither human nor beast.

His bones were bent into a horrifying arc, all the joints of his limbs twisted in the opposite direction, and he was huddled in the iron cage, his hair and beard disheveled, resembling a furry, bloodthirsty beast.

But the iron cage did indeed contain a person, and a once-renowned martial arts master at that.

Han Tieshan, the sect leader of the Iron Palm Sect, had suffered a qi deviation due to the limitations of his cultivation method, forcibly attempting a breakthrough, resulting in his bones growing in bizarre, misaligned positions under the impact of his internal energy.

This former master, now reduced to a grotesque, ghostly state due to this qi deviation, had built his sect from scratch. After his incident, aside from his direct disciples and children, the sect tirelessly sought medical help for him.

They even went to Medicine King Valley. The elders there said that Han Tieshan's current condition—his bones growing in dislocations and his body deformed—required bone breaking and reshaping to restore his body to normal.

However, Han Tieshan, a master of innate cultivation, suffered a severe deformity and misalignment due to a qi deviation. The affected area was too large; if bone reshaping were attempted, the inability to circulate his internal energy would likely cause massive bleeding and death. The chances of successful treatment were extremely slim, and even if successful, the best outcome would be a wheelchair-bound person, while the worst would be complete loss of sensation below the chest.

Han Tieshan's disciples and children could not accept this outcome and had to inquire with Medicine King Valley about a better solution. However, they only stated that this was the best they could offer.

To achieve a better outcome, they either needed to obtain rare treasures, such as the Snow Heaven Divine Water from the sacred land of the Great Snow Mountain of the alien race, to enhance Han Tieshan's recovery during treatment and increase the chances of success. Alternatively, Han Tieshan's cultivation would advance further, taking another step forward in his path, becoming a grandmaster and drawing in the spiritual energy of heaven and earth to rebuild his body.

Faced with these solutions, Han Tieshan's disciples and relatives were all utterly devastated. The Snow Heaven Divine Water of the Great Snow Mountain Holy Land was priceless, a true treasure, revered as a supreme artifact by the northern barbarians. The current Emperor Qian, after decades of campaigning in the north, had only acquired three bottles of this treasure. One was given to General Wei Huo, who was assassinated and on the verge of death; the remaining two were kept in the imperial treasury.

As for the other, to advance further and attain the Grandmaster level, not to mention that Han Tieshan himself had suffered a qi deviation in his pursuit of that further advancement, Han Tieshan, who practiced external martial arts, could barely stand. How could someone on the path of indestructibility possibly advance any further?

Just as everyone was losing hope, an elder from Medicine King Valley mentioned the Hunyuan Sect of the Hengyi Mountains, saying that his master had studied the *Nourishing Life Classic* of the Medical Immortal lineage and had researched the human body for a century, which might be helpful to Han Tieshan's condition.

Overjoyed, the group rushed to the Hunyuan Sect. Han Tieshan's third direct disciple and two sons knelt before Mu Jingxing, begging him to save their master/father.

At that time, Fang Yuan had already made some progress in herbalism and surgery.

His achievements in herbalism were particularly outstanding.

Speaking of which, this was all thanks to Zhao Feixing.

Three years ago, Zhao Feixing was a drunkard who refused to pay his debts, spending his days using sect funds to research his twisted theories of "drinking to numb the body." Until one day, Fang Yuan passed by his herbalist's hut, smelled a strong odor of alcohol, and out of curiosity, pushed open the door, just in time to see Zhao Feixing drinking a jar of strong liquor.

"Senior Brother Zhao, what are you doing?"

"Research!" Zhao Feixing burped confidently. "This is legitimate medical research! What do you know?"

Fang Yuan was silent for a moment, then asked a question that stunned Zhao Feixing: "Why don't you just extract the essence of the wine? High-concentration alcohol itself has antibacterial and anesthetic properties. You don't need to drink it; applying it directly to the affected area avoids irritating the wound."

Zhao Feixing's eyes widened.

That night, the two talked until dawn.

Fang Yuan's knowledge from his previous life and the pharmacological system of this world collided that night, creating a wonderful chemical reaction. Zhao Feixing contributed his extensive experimental data and practical experience accumulated over three years regarding alcohol anesthetics.

The two hit it off immediately. Over the next three months, they continuously experimented with different wines, tested the purity of the distilled alcohol, and repeatedly blended them with various anesthetic herbs.

Fang Yuan proposed combining peppermint, asarum, and datura pollen with alcohol to enhance the analgesic effect. Zhao Feixing, leveraging his connections in Medicine King Valley, obtained a batch of high-purity distillation equipment. After repeated adjustments to the proportions following initial failures, the two finally developed a topical analgesic called "Ice Numbness Powder."

Its efficacy was remarkable. Zhao Feixing quickly became a sensation in the newly established dental clinic thanks to this medicine, and Fang Yuan's already considerable reputation grew even further.

At that time, the Han family came seeking medical help. Mu Jing, a compassionate healer, summoned the elders still within the sect to discuss treatment options. Fang Yuan and Zhao Feixing were also called in because their analgesic was helpful in surgery.

After learning about their situation at the meeting, Fang Yuan offered his opinion.

Since conventional bone-setting and reshaping methods were ineffective, a corrective method should be used.

Through anterior/posterior incisions, pedicle screws were implanted, and connected with devices to open, lift, and rotate the curved spine for correction.

This method was unheard of in the medical field at the time—implanting foreign objects into the body to correct and assist skeletal structures.

It was unprecedented, even within the then-advanced Hunyuan Sect, and considered groundbreaking.

The elders present all looked grim, as this method was simply too far-fetched.

However, upon closer examination, they found some feasibility. Following Fang Yuan's method would require less reshaping, less bleeding, and a shorter recovery time—a good choice from a medical perspective.

But since this was the first time such a plan had been proposed, and by a disciple with only two or three years of medical training, the elders exchanged hesitant glances, unsure of its success.

In the end, Elder Mu Jingxing decided to shelve the plan, setting it aside for now, and to explore other, better options.

Finally, the group discussed and came up with a method consistent with that of Medicine King Valley, and then informed the Han family.

Upon hearing Fang Yuan's proposed method, Han Tieshan and his group were furious, accusing the Hunyuan Sect and others of deceiving them and using a disciple's conjecture to fool their master.

The situation quickly spiraled out of control, but Han Tieshan eventually regained his senses and decided to use Fang Yuan's method.

He expressed that he didn't want to live like this, insane and inhuman; even in death, he wanted to be buried humanely.

Finally, Fang Yuan and the sect agreed on a treatment plan, with Fang Yuan as the primary surgeon, Elder Li Mo, the sect's most knowledgeable expert on bones and meridians, as his assistant, Zhao Feixing as the anesthesiologist, and Mu Jingxing and Mu Chen assisting by observing Han Tieshan's condition.

The Hunyuan Sect commissioned a master craftsman from the Mo family to forge a set of specialized surgical instruments according to their blueprints—forged from the finest iron: a bone saw as fine as a hair, a graduated bone chisel, bone forceps with precise angle adjustment, and a bone grinder to smooth out deformed bones.

After the instruments were completed, the Mo family master even asked the Hunyuan Sect why they had gone to all that trouble to have him forge these woodworking materials. Any blacksmith could have done it; why did they insist on having him?

The surgery lasted a full day and night.

Fang Yuan precisely sealed all of Han Tieshan's meridians with his internal energy, minimizing interference from his true qi. Li Mo assisted, using acupuncture to determine the depth and angle of each bone misalignment.

Although the surgery was somewhat complicated, after two months of recuperation at the Hunyuan Sect, Han Tieshan's bones were indeed successfully repositioned, and he seemed to have returned to normal.

This successful surgery can be said to have pioneered a new surgical approach to bone treatment, a feat worthy of being recorded in medical history.

In Zhao Feixing's words, it was thanks to Fang Yuan that he and Fang Yuan could truly be remembered in history.

The impact of this surgery didn't stop there. After confirming Han Tieshan's condition, the Han family hired a troupe of musicians to present the Hunyuan Sect with a plaque inscribed with "Skill in Restoring Life."

The elders of the Medicine King Valley specializing in orthopedics, upon learning of this, frequently visited the mountain to exchange ideas.

After this battle, Fang Yuan's reputation in Fang Yuan's area soared. Everyone knew that the Hunyuan Sect had a miracle-working surgeon, Doctor Fang.

People flocked to him for treatment.

Fang Yuan's hands were steady and swift. First, he cleaned the wound, then used his internal energy to protect the tendons and blood vessels at the broken points. With a push and a pull, the three broken bones were expertly put back in place in his hands.

He wrapped layers of hemp cloth around the old man's calf, each layer with just the right amount of pressure—tight but not suffocating, loose but not falling apart.

Finally, he reinforced it with several specially made bamboo splints. The whole process was fluid and seamless, without any unnecessary movements.

"Alright." Fang Yuan stood up and washed his hands in the basin. "Stay in the next room for three days for observation. If there are no problems, you can go home to recuperate. The medical expenses will be settled by the accountant later; it's not expensive."

The fees at Hunyuan Sect were actually similar to many large medical clinics, which was quite good for ordinary people, and among the highest in the surrounding area. The problem was that Hunyuan Sect said the terrain on the mountain was rugged and complex, and getting up the mountain would be a problem, so unless it was a particularly difficult case, they wouldn't go up the mountain.

Of course, this applies to ordinary people. It's different for wealthy families. They don't need to leave the mountain; they can go to the pharmacies set up by the sect's disciples and send messengers up the mountain to request treatment from the mountain dwellers. However, the cost is...

extremely high, especially for some difficult and complicated illnesses. The Hunyuan Sect directly pledges a quarter of its wealth to guarantee a full-scale treatment, but success is not guaranteed.

Even common illnesses are quite expensive, as the mountain dwellers' food and horses are also costly.

The Hunyuan Sect's income comes from selecting intelligent children from ordinary or impoverished families to come to the mountain to learn martial arts. If they are exceptionally talented, they stay in the Hunyuan Sect after three years. If their talent is limited, they receive a certificate to leave the mountain and work as doctors in the clinics and pharmacies of the sect's senior elders. Half of their income for five years goes to the sect.

They also generate revenue by selling prescriptions and elixirs.

The biggest profit in recent years has likely come from the boiling water ice-making technique that Fang Yuan and Zhao Feixing developed while creating anesthetics for dental extractions.

Thanks to this technology, many merchants flocked to the mountain to purchase it, significantly increasing the sect's revenue.

The anesthetic powder was especially popular, and Zhao Feixing heard that recently, members of the sect had come to inquire about the family's secret recipe.

…………

When Fang Yuan stepped into Mu Jingxing's study, the sun was already setting, and the slanting sunlight streamed through the window, bathing the room in a warm golden light.

Mu Jingxing was sitting behind his desk, flipping through a yellowed book. Hearing footsteps, he looked up, his gaze lingering on Fang Yuan for a moment before he nodded slightly. Three years had passed, and the boy he had found on the mountain path had grown into this handsome and composed young man.

He nodded in satisfaction and said gently,

"You've arrived. Find a place to sit."

Fang Yuan sat down in the chair opposite the desk, his back straight, his hands resting naturally on his knees. Mu Jingxing observed him for a moment before speaking, "I called you here because there's something I need to tell you."

"Please speak, Sect Leader."

Mu Jingxing waved his hand, "Just call me Grand Elder. I don't feel comfortable wearing the title of Sect Master." He paused, then continued, "In three days, the sect will hold an apprenticeship ceremony to formally accept disciples who have completed their three-year probationary period. Among these disciples, you are undoubtedly the chief."

Fang Yuan remained calm, his eyes slightly lowered. If others knew this, even if they had expected it, they would be overjoyed at his age. However, Fang Yuan remained composed and, after hearing the explanation, simply bowed to Mu Chen.

He expressed his determination not to disappoint his master's expectations.

Seeing his composure, Mu Jingxing's eyes showed even greater approval. He continued, "At that time, as the representative of the disciples, you will formally become my disciple. I personally brought you up the mountain three years ago, and it's only now that I'm officially informing you of your entry; it's been a difficult time for you."

That's what he said, but during these three years, while holding the position of sect leader, Fang Yuan performed a groundbreaking surgery. Many people in need came to the sect seeking Fang Yuan, many of whom had ill intentions. Mu Jingxing was the one who dealt with them.

He also held the positions of bodyguard and supervisor, handling both duties. In these three years, not only did he neglect Fang Yuan, but many of his disciples and daughters were also cared for by his eldest disciple.

"Sigh, it's his own fault for not wanting to be the sect leader, wanting to leave it to some unknown guy out there."

Mu Jingxing gestured for him to sit down again. Then he picked up a thick book from the table. The cover was made of special leather, with the four large characters "Hun Yuan Yang Sheng Jing" (Primordial Chaos Nourishing Life Classic) written in ancient seal script. The edges were worn smooth, clearly indicating it had been frequently read.

Mu Jingxing pushed the book towards Fang Yuan. "This contains annotations and analyses of the cultivation method by generations of sect predecessors. From beginner to advanced levels, the insights and taboos of each realm are recorded inside. It also includes the theories and insights from the founder's conversations with the Immortal Physician. Take this back and study it; it will greatly benefit your future cultivation."

Usually, only those recognized as core disciples of the sect are qualified to access the original cultivation method with annotations from previous generations.

Ordinary disciples only study the transcribed text, which contains only the original text of the cultivation method. There are annotations and insights, but more importantly, there are taboos to be observed during cultivation. Within three years, they will only offer a few words of advice on these new techniques at crucial moments.

This is also the practice of major sects: they only reveal the taboos, and guidance is only given at crucial moments. Martial arts cultivation comes later, increasingly relying on comprehension. Too much guidance from others in the early stages can easily backfire, hindering growth.

Therefore, all major sects uniformly stipulate that only the taboos are revealed in the initial training manuals, and masters only offer guidance in certain areas. Only after one has mastered the skills do they release the annotations and insights of their predecessors.

Fang Yuan remained silent for a moment, then solemnly put the book into his robes. He stood up and bowed deeply to Mu Jingxing. This bow was sincere.

Mu Jingxing accepted the bow, his gaze towards Fang Yuan filled with satisfaction. Three years ago, when he brought this young man back, he only felt that the boy had rare talent and a calm temperament, a promising prospect. He never expected that in just three years, this handsome young man would bring him so many surprises.

Just as Fang Yuan was about to take his leave, Mu Jingxing suddenly spoke up: "Fang Yuan."

Fang Yuan stopped and turned around.

Mu Jingxing leaned back in his chair, his gaze deepening, his tone becoming more meaningful: "These past few years, everyone has been discussing your medical achievements, but rarely mentioning your martial arts cultivation.

But I know your martial arts talent is equally astonishing."

Mu Jingxing paused, his voice softening slightly: "Could you tell me the truth? What level have you reached now?"

Fang Yuan remained calm upon hearing this.

The room fell silent for a moment.

Then, Fang Yuan didn't speak, but simply bowed to Mu Jingxing again. He straightened up, slowly raising his right hand, his finger pointing to the ornamental bonsai on Mu Jingxing's table.

It was an elegantly pruned gnarled pine bonsai, its branches vigorous, its needles verdant. It was early autumn, and a few old leaves were slightly yellowed, hanging precariously from the branches.

Fang Yuan's finger lightly tapped the air.

There was no sound, no obvious movement, but Mu Jingxing sensed it—an invisible, intangible energy flowed lightly from Fang Yuan's fingertips, traversing a distance of three zhang (approximately 10 meters), and landing on the gnarled pine tree.

*Snap.*

A very soft, crisp sound.

The few yellowed old leaves, as if gently brushed by an invisible hand, detached themselves from the branch and drifted onto the soil in the pot.

Then, something even more astonishing happened.

At the very instant the old leaves fell, three or four tiny buds, no bigger than grains of rice, trembled violently on the bare branches of the gnarled pine, as if infused with some vibrant life force. Those buds began to unfurl and grow at a visible speed, swelling from the size of a grain of rice to the size of a bean, then unfurling again to sprout two tender green leaves covered in fine down.

The whole process took only a blink of an eye.

On the edge of the flowerpot, the few withered old leaves lay quietly, while the newly sprouted leaves on the branch trembled slightly, gleaming with a warm luster in the slanting sunlight. The alternation of withering and flourishing seemed to encapsulate the essence of spring and autumn.

Mu Jingxing's eyes widened.

The room was silent.

"This..." Mu Jingxing abruptly stood up from his chair, his hands gripping the table, staring intently at the tender new leaves sprouting from the gnarled pine tree. With his keen eyesight, he could naturally tell it wasn't an illusion, nor some kind of magic trick.

The old leaves weren't broken by internal force. If it were merely a matter of breaking leaves from a distance, that would only be a manifestation of internal energy cultivation reaching a certain level, of condensing qi into power—something anyone at the Great Perfection of the Qi Meridian Realm could do. But the growth of those tender shoots—that was something that simply channeling internal force couldn't achieve.

"Intent."

Fang Yuan had already grasped his own "intent," this threshold that had trapped many martial artists, he had crossed in just three short years.

Everyone's intent is different; some's intent is sharp as a knife, some's is majestic as a mountain, some's is vast as the sea. But Fang Yuan's intent—he couldn't see through it.

"Within three zhang of the air, the force is concentrated and does not dissipate, reaching the Qi Meridian level." Mu Jingxing's voice was filled with barely suppressed joy.

To have achieved this level of cultivation in three years is already astonishing.

This intent can stimulate vitality and drive the growth of plants—this martial arts essence is truly extraordinary.

Truly, a hidden dragon lies dormant in the abyss; it remains silent until it roars, and then it astounds the world!



Chapter 39 The Stepping Stone for the Male Protagonist in a Wuxia Story: The Holy Son 9 (6k)


"Truly, Heaven blesses our sect!"

This thought popped into Mu Jingxing's mind after learning about Fang Yuan's situation.

Mu Jingxing slowly sat back in his chair, took a deep breath, and looked at the young man before him with a complex expression.

Three years had passed. In these three years, as the acting sect leader and Grand Elder, he had personally instructed every martial arts disciple in the sect.

How long does it take to enter the Qi Meridian Realm? For those with exceptional talent, twenty years. For ordinary geniuses, thirty years or more. The vast majority of people spend their entire lives without even touching the threshold of the Qi Meridian Realm.

And entering the Qi Meridian Realm is already the threshold for first-rate masters in the martial arts world, enough to become an elder in any sect!

Yet, their Hunyuan Sect has produced two geniuses in this generation.

The last one was Mu Chen, who at sixteen years old comprehended the essence, stunning countless people!

Now, only three years later, another one has emerged: Fang Yuan.

How old is Fang Yuan this year?

Fifteen years old!

She's even a year younger than Mu Chen!

More importantly, internal energy can be accumulated over time, but "intention" is different. "Intention" is the most profound thing in martial arts cultivation. Some people are trapped in the Qi Meridian Realm their entire lives without ever grasping a trace of intention, while others achieve sudden enlightenment in a life-or-death situation. This kind of thing cannot be taught or learned; it can only be acquired through one's own efforts.

Mu Chen had grown up under Mu Jingxing's careful guidance and nurturing since childhood, but what about Fang Yuan?

Fang Yuan had only been in the Hunyuan Sect for three short years. In three years, from a boy with no foundation, he had broken through all realms, reaching the Qi Meridian Realm, and even comprehending his own martial arts true intention?

Who would believe it?

Those so-called geniuses in the martial world, those prodigies hailed as "once-in-a-century" talents, were simply a joke compared to Fang Yuan before them.

"Three years," Mu Jingxing murmured to himself.

"Truly...truly, Heaven blesses our sect!"

Upon uttering these words, Mu Jingxing could no longer suppress the surging emotions within him. He suddenly threw his head back and burst into laughter. His laughter, like a booming bell, echoed throughout the study, rattling the windowpanes and causing dewdrops to roll down from the gnarled pine tree.

"Good lad, good lad, a hidden dragon in the abyss!"

Upon hearing this, Fang Yuan smiled and bowed to Mu Jingxing again, saying, "This disciple was merely lucky."

After smiling, Mu Jingxing leaned back in his chair, letting out a long sigh, his voice tinged with an unspeakable melancholy: "What a masterful concealment, what a skillful way of keeping a low profile. In three years, others only saw your surgical prowess and your acupuncture skills, but they were unaware that your martial arts cultivation was equally astonishing. You've truly hidden it well."

Mu Jingxing knew that Fang Yuan was hiding his cultivation level. He knew that this surgical master, already renowned within a hundred miles, possessed extraordinary abilities. The people in the Scripture Pavilion had told Mu Jingxing that Fang Yuan had exchanged his skills for the *Hun Yuan Yang Sheng Jing* (Primordial Chaos Nourishing Life Scripture) three months after entering the sect.

At that time, Fang Yuan had just broken the sect's record for the Small Heavenly Circuit Perfection. Knowing Fang Yuan's exceptional talent, he had intended to cultivate him in the direction of martial arts, but Mu Chen stopped him, saying that Fang Yuan was very diligent in his studies in medicine, and it would be better to observe him for a while before making any decisions.

Mu Jingxing also thought it was quite good at the time, and decided to observe for a while longer. After all, the Hunyuan Sect was founded on medicine and martial arts, with medicine preceding martial arts. It had only been three months, and it was too early to predict Fang Yuan's future. However, as his master, he couldn't do nothing. He had Mu Chen send Fang Yuan a pill that would help with his internal energy, and also instructed his own disciple to interact with Fang Yuan more.

And guess what? After interacting with Fang Yuan, Zhao Feixing completely turned things around. His anesthetic drug was a huge credit to the Hunyuan Sect at the Medicine King Valley Conference in the twenty-first year of Tai'an.

Later, he displayed astonishing talent in the Han Tieshan incident; that surgery was groundbreaking.

What did Mu Jingxing do to deserve such an outstanding disciple?

"I'll wait for your performance in three months."

Three months later, the medical lineage would lead the team to the Medicine King Valley Conference to take the "Apricot Grove Manual" exam—a grand feast for the entire medical lineage.

Every profession needs young people, even a profession like medicine where experience is highly valued.

Upon hearing this, Fang Yuan was about to bow again.

Mu Jingxing waved his hand, sat back down at his desk, picked up a brush, and began writing with flowing strokes, saying,

"Alright, we doctors aren't Confucianists, why all this formality?"

After finishing, he stamped the sect leader's seal, flicked it, and tossed it to Fang Yuan.

"For the past three years, I, as your master, haven't done much, just given you some odd jobs. Now that you've formally become my disciple, I can't leave without showing some appreciation."

Fang Yuan caught the scroll steadily, his robe billowing. He looked down and saw the characters were vigorous and powerful, seemingly penetrating the paper, but more importantly, the content.

"Judging from this child's exceptional talent, extraordinary comprehension, and remarkable character, he is a prodigy rarely seen in a century.

Today, we specially open the sect's treasury, granting him special permission to enter and freely choose three treasures, as a sign of our special favor and to nurture this talented individual. We hope he will diligently cultivate and live up to the sect's expectations."

Fang Yuan was also surprised after reading it. Although the Hunyuan Sect wasn't one of the top sects in the world, it had a well-established lineage and a vast history. This favor was undeniably significant.

Mu Jingxing's voice came from behind: "At the apprenticeship ceremony three days later, I will personally inscribe your name into the sect's genealogy."

Fang Yuan paused slightly, then stepped out the door. His clear voice came from outside:

"This disciple will certainly not disappoint Master."

Mu Jingxing remained silent, only looking out the window.

The study door closed softly behind him. Fang Yuan stood on the veranda, looking up. The evening glow bathed the entire Hunyuan Sect in a golden-red light. A mountain breeze stirred, fluttering the hem of his white outer robe.

Fang Yuan reached out and touched the *Hunyuan Yangsheng Jing* (a classic text on health and longevity) in his robes. The handprints left by the sages on the cover rippled slightly beneath his fingertips.

For three years, Fang Yuan had been unaware of his progress until one morning, watching a seed sprout from the soil, its accumulated energy finally bursting forth. He was deeply moved and sat alone for five hours, even missing his morning lessons.

When he first arrived, Fang Yuan noticed Zhao Feixing beside him. Zhao Feixing told him he had comprehended "Intent," and Fang Yuan realized he had obtained the "Intent" that countless martial artists yearned for but could not attain.

After examining Fang Yuan, Zhao Feixing confirmed that Fang Yuan had indeed grasped the "intention" that many martial artists at the Five Organs Realm sought but could not achieve.

Afterwards, Zhao Feixing asked Fang Yuan if he had consumed any rare treasures, otherwise his progress in the first two realms wouldn't have been so rapid. While the first two realms were simple, they still demanded a high level of skill from the cultivator.

Hearing Zhao Feixing's words, Fang Yuan thought of the source energy that System 120 had given him.

Seeing Fang Yuan's expression, Zhao Feixing knew he was right and said he would report this matter to Mu Jingxing.

Fang Yuan didn't say anything, but the system in his mind did remind him to suppress the matter. It said that if Fang Yuan wanted to become the young master of the medical family as set, it was best to suppress this matter and wait for an opportunity that would allow him to become famous.

One year later, at the Medicine King Valley Conference!

Fang Yuan descended the steps and walked back along the mountain path. Several disciples patrolling the mountain greeted him with bows. He nodded in return, his expression calm and his steps unhurried.

The system's view was that, based on data collected within the sect, if Fang Yuan wanted to achieve his goals, he would inevitably face a formidable enemy standing in his way.

A friend he didn't want to hurt, a man who could be considered an elder brother to Fang Yuan.

The number one young talent of the Hunyuan Sect, first place in the previous Medicine King Valley Martial Arts Tournament, third place in the Xinglin Tie competition, an unparalleled genius with a Qi Meridian of eighteen, Mu Jingxing's eldest disciple, the sect's senior brother…

Mu Chen!

Fang Yuan was outstanding, truly outstanding. In the current Hunyuan Sect, even considering martial arts cultivation, Fang Yuan's achievements were the most dazzling new star.

But he was also unfortunate, because a similar genius had already emerged in the previous generation.

There cannot be two suns in the sky, nor two masters on a mountain.

At eighteen, a Qi Meridian Realm expert is enough to make him stand out among his peers throughout the Nine Provinces. Whether in reputation or character, cultivation or medical skills, Mu Chen is virtually impeccable. If the Hunyuan Sect were to nominate someone to compete for the title of heir to the Yao family, Mu Chen would be the best candidate.

In terms of cultivation, achievements, and fame, Mu Chen consistently crushes the next generation and the generation after that.

If Fang Yuan wants to achieve his goal, Mu Chen is a formidable obstacle he must overcome.

System data analysis shows that if Fang Yuan wants to win, Mu Chen is the key figure he must defeat honorably. Perhaps Mu Chen's talent is inferior to his, but the ten years he started earlier have given Mu Chen an overwhelming advantage over Fang Yuan in cultivation, reputation, status, and connections.

Therefore, to defeat Mu Chen, Fang Yuan must lie low. He must conceal his brilliance and wait for an opportunity—an opportunity that will allow the world to see and even be forced to submit.

And the Medicine King Valley Conference a year from now will be Fang Yuan's best battlefield.

Therefore, he must keep the news of his enlightenment today a closely guarded secret, and not let a single word of it leak out.

After hearing this explanation, Fang Yuan fell into a deep silence. The auxiliary system left by System 120 only coldly analyzed data, devoid of human emotion or compassion. But from Fang Yuan's perspective, these words were undeniably true. Every word struck a nerve, every cut piercing his heart.

Keep the news hidden, continue to lie low. Wait until the Medicine King Valley Conference, then make a stunning debut, overwhelm Mu Chen with a resounding victory, seize the opportunity to overtake him, and make everyone in the Hunyuan Sect see and acknowledge him.

Complete the leapfrog development.

Zhao Feixing collaborated with him; Fang Yuan helped him make the anesthetic he needed. If Fang Yuan asked, he would agree…

Fang Yuan looked at Zhao Feixing, who was beaming with excitement, saying, "Junior Brother is truly amazing! Our Hunyuan Sect will have a much higher opinion of us now!"

He felt a strange, heavy feeling in his heart.

Zhao Feixing couldn't remember what that patient looked like, but he remembered the agonizing expression on his face when he described the toothache.

Senior Brother Mu Chen, Second Senior Sister Li Huaisu, Third Senior Brother Xiao Tian, ​​Fifth Senior Brother Mu Ling.

If a ruler treats his subjects like brothers, then the subjects will treat the ruler like their own heart and soul; if a ruler treats his subjects like dogs and horses, then the subjects will treat the ruler like a stranger; if a ruler treats his subjects like dirt and weeds, then the subjects will treat the ruler like an enemy.

Mu Chen treated his junior brothers and sisters with utmost care, like an elder brother and father, and regarded Fang Yuan as his own younger brother.

"If a ruler treats his subjects like brothers, then the subjects will treat the ruler like their heart and soul."

"Hahaha, I knew you had something to say to me today, Junior Brother. I didn't expect it to be just this?"

Fang Yuan was stunned. What, just?

Zhao Feixing, standing to the side, was also stunned. What did Mu Chen mean by that?

Mu Chen explained that he had heard Xiao Tian mention this idea before, and he was very happy that Fang Yuan had such ambition.

He implied that if Fang Yuan had this idea, there was no need to mince words; he should just say it directly. As the senior brother, he was overjoyed that his junior brothers and sisters could surpass him!

Fang Yuan was also somewhat taken aback and hurriedly asked, "Senior brother, aren't you angry?"

He gestured with his hand to indicate the size of a little.

"But it's not because you want to surpass me that I'm angry; it's because you want to keep your breakthrough a secret."

"I cancelled it after you told me your plan."

Zhao Feixing, standing beside him, was dumbfounded. He knew his senior brother was magnanimous, but this was too magnanimous!

Although Zhao Feixing's family was small, they still had three children. He was the second oldest, and the family's affection went to the youngest, while the eldest received all the attention. Years ago, when he defiantly declared he would surpass his eldest brother, no one else even had to lift a finger; his youngest brother and a group of cousins ​​could have easily beaten him to a pulp, teaching him the meaning of respect for elders.

Zhao Feixing suddenly remembered the bet with Xiao Tian and Mu Ling.

Sigh, he didn't lose unjustly.

Mu Chen continued, saying that Fang Yuan's breakthrough was a good thing, but upon reflection, he realized his junior brother was still too young. Early fame, especially with a powerful weapon, wasn't necessarily a good thing.

Therefore, he thought it best to suppress the matter, indicating that he would help Fang Yuan resolve things with their master.

After listening, Fang Yuan's expression remained calm, but his heart began to pound inexplicably. He felt no pain, but rather a warm current flowing through him.

Chen then said to Fang Yuan, "Junior brother, your plan is quite good, but I think it can be improved a bit."

Zhao Feixing stared dumbfounded as the two discussed how to defeat Mu Chen, as if they were discussing a third person.

By the time they saw Fang Yuan off, it was already dark. Mu Chen stood at the corner of the mountain path, hands behind his back, watching Fang Yuan's figure gradually disappear into the twilight.

"Junior brother," he called out.

Fang Yuan stopped and turned around.

Mu Chen smiled slightly, a smile that seemed particularly gentle in the mountain breeze.

"A year from now, your senior brother will be waiting for you to become famous throughout the world, surpassing your master."

Fang Yuan nodded heavily.

Mu Chen waved goodbye, everything understood without words.

"Junior Brother, may your sword strike astound the world, your loyal heart illuminate the clear blade."

...

In the distance behind him, the light in Mu Jingxing's study flickered on, a solitary lamp, like a bean or a star in the vast twilight.

Mu Jingxing sat alone behind his desk, the gnarled pine tree before him. He reached out and touched the newly sprouted leaf once more, feeling the real, vibrant touch on his fingertips. He remained silent for a long time.

Remembering Mu Chen's earlier revelation of Fang Yuan's extraordinary talent, and with the ceremony approaching, Mu Jingxing wanted to probe further.

Unexpectedly, their Hunyuan Sect had secretly nurtured two dragons.

Was this a good thing or a bad thing?

Thinking back to when Mu Chen had stood up against all opposition to support Fang Yuan's treatment method, Mu Chen had been so confident, even vouching for Fang Yuan.

Mu Jingxing smiled, thinking of that bastard who said he wanted to seek a breakthrough and would pass the sect leader position to him.

So much like them back then.

Then, he muttered something to himself, his voice so low it was carried away by the mountain breeze outside the window.

"Li Tianran, Li Tianran, if you knew there was such a monster hidden in the sect, you probably wouldn't have gone out to travel even if you were beaten to death."

The setting sun finally sank behind the mountain ridge, night fell, and everything was renewed.

The new leaves on the gnarled pine branches swayed gently in the night breeze, awaiting dawn.

It was as if another season of growth had begun.

Three days later, the sky was bright.

On the martial arts arena of the Hunyuan Sect, over a hundred disciples stood solemnly, arranged according to seniority and dressed in uniform gray-blue sect robes. A high platform had been erected to the north of the arena, incense smoke curling from the burner, creating a solemn and dignified atmosphere.

The sect elders sat on either side of the platform, with Mu Jingxing in the center. Today, he wore a formal black robe, his expression serene.

The triennial apprenticeship ceremony is one of the most solemn rituals of the Hunyuan Sect.

The triennial apprenticeship ceremony is one of the most solemn rituals of the Hunyuan Sect.

Disciples who rushed back from branch schools and pharmacies across the land filled the training ground, all eyes fixed on the open space in front of the high platform—where stood seventy-seven disciples who had passed the three-year test and were about to officially join the sect.

Among them were Fang Mengping and Zhao Qiming, classmates of Fang Yuan.

Looking at Fang Yuan, Zhao Qiming sighed inwardly. Some people are just born extraordinary. Not only are they talented, but they also work hard and are handsome.

In the past three days, Zhao Qiming had truly admired Fang Yuan. Breaking the sect record in just three months, his martial arts talent was the best of the contemporary generation. Most people would be arrogant in the face of such achievements, but Fang Yuan acted as if he couldn't bear it, arriving first every day without fail, maintaining this attitude for three years.

What was even more infuriating was that in those three years, Fang Yuan had grown taller and more handsome.

This completely extinguished Zhao Qiming's competitive spirit.

Meng Ping glanced at his friend Zhao Qiming's expression and knew the guy was lost in thought again. Turning to Fang Yuan, he thought, "People say you become like those you associate with, and over the past three years, as Fang Yuan's right-hand men, Meng Ping and Zhao Qiming had forged a strong friendship."

At first, thinking he couldn't compete in martial arts, he decided to challenge Fang Yuan in pharmacology, studying diligently like a man hanging from a beam. Seeing this, Meng Ping, wanting to save face, also gritted his teeth and began studying hard.

Later, when Zhao Qiming realized he couldn't beat Fang Yuan and was starting to feel discouraged, he turned to see Meng Ping studying hard beside him, and his motivation returned.

"If I can't beat a prodigy, I can beat you!"

Thus, over the three years, the two competed fiercely, forging a deep friendship.

"The auspicious hour has arrived—" the master of ceremonies drew out, "The apprenticeship ceremony, begin!"

The disciples below, who had been conversing with their fellow disciples, fell silent, watching the young men on the platform.

The young men were in the prime of their lives.

The drums thundered, echoing through the mountains.

First, there was a collective worship of the ancestral master, followed by instructions from the elders. The complex ritual was completed, and the sun had risen considerably. Finally, the most crucial part arrived—the disciples' apprenticeship ceremony.

Seventy-seven disciples stepped forward one by one to perform the three kneelings and nine kowtows ceremony before their chosen masters, offering tea, receiving instruction, and exchanging tokens. Every step was meticulously executed, and the disciples watching below held their breath in utter silence.

This action drew glances from several elders present. While the other disciples had performed their kowtows, Mu Jingxing had been seated. This gesture by Mu Jingxing was itself a declaration of commitment.

He kowtowed once.

The child of yesteryear had grown into a handsome young man, now ready to spread his wings.

He is of upright character, possesses exceptional medical skills, and pioneered the art of bone correction, bringing honor to our Hunyuan Sect. Now, after deliberation by all the elders, Fang Yuan is hereby recorded in the sect's lineage, becoming a personal disciple of Mu Jingxing."

A slight murmur rippled through the audience. A personal disciple and an ordinary inner disciple are two different concepts; personal instruction means Mu Jingxing will impart all his knowledge, and Fang Yuan is the heir to Mu Jingxing's lineage.

After performing the three kneelings and nine kowtows, Fang Yuan offered the apprenticeship tea, his voice calm and even: "Disciple Fang Yuan greets Master."

Mu Jingxing took the teacup, took a sip, and then took out a jade token from his robes, handing it to Fang Yuan. The jade token was entirely blue-green, with the characters "Hun Yuan" engraved on the front and a leaf vein pattern on the back. Upon seeing this jade token, the elders present all paled—this was the inheritance token of the Hun Yuan Sect; possessing this token allowed one to access any of the sect's scriptures and resources.

Three years ago at the Apricot Grove Gathering, the Hunyuan Sect suffered a crushing defeat, failing to even crack the top five, a stark contrast to the unparalleled success of Mu Chen's generation.

The Apricot Grove Gathering of Medicine King Valley is meant to test the young. Mu Chen has already participated once with outstanding results. Even if he wanted to return, the sect wouldn't allow him.

To beat up a child?

The gathering is for members of the medical lineage; calling them fellow disciples wouldn't be an exaggeration. To do this is shameless; the Hunyuan Sect would never do such a thing.

Chapter 41 The Stepping Stone for the Wuxia Male Protagonist, the Holy Son 11


On the day of departure, just as dawn broke, several figures already stood before the gates of the Hunyuan Sect.

Morning mist rose from the valley, shrouding the stone steps and the gate tower in a thin veil. Distant peaks appeared like dark eyebrows, while nearby pine needles glistened with dew; the entire sect was still immersed in a tranquil, half-awake stillness.

Mu Chen arrived first.

He stood on the stone steps before the gate, hands clasped behind his back, his grey robes billowing slightly in the morning breeze. He didn't speak, simply waiting quietly, his gaze fixed on the gradually brightening horizon at the end of the mountain path.

Beside him were Zhao Feixing and Xiao Tian.

Zhao Feixing carried a heavy medicine chest on his back, several cloth bags of varying sizes hanging from his waist, jingling as he walked. He didn't exchange pleasantries with Mu Chen, only nodded, and stood quietly to the side, his gaze calm and serious.

Thinking of Fang Yuan's achievements,

"Haha, didn't expect that, did you! My junior brother is even more amazing!"

"I don't believe it, I don't believe it! I have to maintain a good image and let my junior brothers and sisters know that the inventor of this great drug, anesthetic, is such a noble and upright senior brother."

Mu Chen was appointed as the team leader.

In their youth, they harbored lofty ambitions, considering themselves among the best.

Before the imperial examinations were invented in the Great Qian Dynasty, the best way for ordinary people to succeed was to gain fame, and events like the Apricot Grove Conference, held every three years and of great significance, were their best opportunities.

According to the rules of the medical community, passing this conference and obtaining the Apricot Grove Certificate would be enough to prove that one had entered the ranks of pharmacists.

With this certificate, you can go to any pharmacy or clinic in the world. The government highly values ​​doctors who obtain this certificate, and anyone literate with a bit of money knows its significance.

Obtaining the "Medicine Doctor's Certificate" signifies you have a lineage and are capable.

Furthermore, in the martial arts world, you're less likely to be bullied.

They're all incredibly healthy, with their internal organs, meridians, and bones memorized perfectly. Do you think they can't fight?

The area next to Medicine King Valley used to be the territory of a group of barbarian tribes. Why do you think they're still there?

In short, obtaining this certificate guarantees a comfortable life, as long as you're alive and have the skills, you'll always have a place to make a living, and you'll be in high demand wherever you go.

Of course, obtaining the certificate doesn't mean everything is settled. Since the late Xia Dynasty, when medical schools began holding regular conferences, medical techniques have entered a period of rapid development, revealing many flaws and errors in existing theories.

So they set a standard: the guarantee of the Xinglin Post would be in 10-year increments, increasing sequentially thereafter.

The group marched for a full day, setting up camp in an open valley at dusk.

Traveling a group of over eighty people was no small feat, especially since most of them were only fifteen or sixteen years old—the prime of their youth and full of youthful vigor. A moment's mismanagement could easily lead to problems.

Fortunately, however, this grand gathering had been held for many years, and the local officials were aware of it; Mu Chen had also reported it to the authorities.

Mu Chen was currently directing the disciples, assigning tasks—some gathered firewood to start a fire, some fetched water to cook, and some pitched tents and laid out bedding. The work was busy but orderly and efficient.

What's going on?

Zhao Sanshi was a bandit, a moderately successful one.

At this moment, he was drinking fine wine in the main hall of his mountain stronghold, watching the woman he had abducted from the foot of the mountain dance for him.

On one side were his group of crooked-looking brothers, whose appearance, upon closer inspection, revealed a lewd quality.

Zhao Sanshi, seeing this, clapped his hands and laughed loudly,

"This is good, this is good!" With that, he arrogantly stood up from his seat, pulling the woman into his arms and teasing her.

"Little beauty, if you follow me, I guarantee you'll have mountains of gold and delicacies to eat and mountains of silver to spend."

The woman, forcibly taken into his arms, could only resign herself to reconciliation.

Seeing the woman's submissive face in his arms, who knows what Zhao San was really thinking? It only added a peculiar charm to him.

"Chief, have you been raiding again lately?"

Zhao Sanshi replied casually, "Oh, strategist, it's just that the winter solstice is approaching and I happened to find some fat sheep; I just got the urge to plunder."

The scholar, hearing this, questioned angrily, "Chief, how can you do this? Didn't I tell you not to raid during this time? You'll get us killed!"

Upon hearing this, the atmosphere in the hall changed drastically. Zhao Sanshi's playful expression vanished, and he casually tossed the woman in his arms to the ground, saying with a dangerous look:

"Strategist, you're overthinking it. With so many brothers under my command, who would come up the mountain to kill me?"

Zhao Sanshi was somewhat displeased. Bandits raiding was commonplace, especially with autumn ending and winter approaching. How could they have a good New Year if they didn't take advantage of the situation to rob as many people as possible?

The scholar was even more furious. "Chief, you'll ruin all the brothers in the village this way! You know what's going on!"

The scholar, Xu Qi, had previously warned Chief Zhao Sanshi not to go down the mountain this month. They had already made a few good deals, and going down now would easily lead to trouble.

The Medicine King Valley Gathering had been held for decades, and the residents south of the Hengli Mountains knew about it. Sects from all over would travel to Medicine King Valley.

The number of disciples from each sect was considerable. Even though it was held every three years, the expenses for food and supplies were substantial. Therefore, someone came up with the idea of ​​providing free medical consultations along the way, charging only three coins for a consultation and a meal. This way, they could heal and save lives while reducing their own expenses.

But this wasn't enough. So, these sect disciples also developed another project:

a fixed tradition among martial arts practitioners!

Fighting bandits, hunting mountain thieves, and capturing thieves.

There are dozens of routes to Medicine King Valley, even if the number is small, and these are all trained by their sects, with regular group training and teamwork. Their combat strength is nowhere near that of the scattered bandits on the road.

What? You ask what if they can't win?

Are you kidding? Isn't it normal for a group of doctors to be outmatched? They'll just use their traditional skills.

You know, the process of refining medicine always produces some strange byproducts: powders that cause diarrhea; powders that cause fainting if certain herbs are not available; powders that taste delicious but easily lead to coma.

Disciples of various sects start refining and mixing medicines at a certain level. Who hasn't produced some strange things in the process?

These things are difficult to deal with. Throwing them away seems wasteful; these medicinal herbs are hard-earned, accumulated by their sects bit by bit. But keeping them might lead to trouble if a junior disciple steals them one day.

Hey, guess what? A brilliant idea came up.

They're all doctors, it's not good for them to be fighting and killing all the time. Why don't we put some drugs in their hands?

Let's poison them!

Everyone: Σ( ° △ °|||)︴

But after thinking about it, they realized it actually made sense! It's not good for us to be fighting and killing doctors all the time. If we poison those bandits, we might be able to sell them for some money. It's a win-win situation, and we can clear out our stock.

A triple win, isn't it?

So ever since someone discovered this method, during the annual Medicine King Valley Assembly, the sect disciples treated those bandit gangs like easy targets, grinding them down like experience points.

They left no trace.

An unnamed elder surnamed Mu commented, "Out of ten of these guys, eight will get poisoned and suffer the consequences; the other two are just lucky to escape. Most of them deserve what they got."

They could gain fame, make money, and practice their martial arts all at the same time.

Moreover, most of the bandits and thugs couldn't beat the disciples, and with the help of highly skilled elders, they couldn't cause any real trouble.

Especially after discovering that using drugs was more effective than direct combat, many disciples would send someone with superior disguise skills to add drugs to their food, and then raid their old residences a couple of days later.

Along the way, the bandits and thugs all kept their tails between their legs.

However, the scholar Xu Qi seemed somewhat heavy-hearted. Over the years, they had roughly estimated when the Hunyuan Sect would set off for their grand assembly, and would specifically avoid those two months.

According to the scholar's calculations, it should be within those two months, so he repeatedly told their chieftain Zhao Sanshi not to go down the mountain to plunder for the next two months, but to wait until things calmed down.

Seeing Xu Qi's troubled expression, Zhao Sanshi realized he had hurt his feelings and comforted him,

"It's alright, strategist. I only robbed that one. I took the remaining wood from the cart up the mountain, and I fed the people to the bears. I swept everything clean; those sect disciples won't find out."

"But..."

"This..."

Zhao Sanshi laughed heartily, picked up the wine barrel, poured a cup, and shoved it into his arms. "Nothing's wrong, is it? Come on, brothers, keep the music playing, keep dancing!"

"Hahaha!"

Then he burst into loud laughter, and even the bandits drinking and eating nearby joined in.

The scholar, watching this scene, resigned himself to the situation, a sliver of hope lingering in his heart.

Yes, it's almost the end of October, and nothing's come of it. He figured the sect disciples really hadn't noticed anything.

Thinking this, Xu Qi picked up his wine bowl and took a sip. It was sweet and smooth, and a warm sensation rose in his stomach. In this increasingly wintery weather, such a sip was truly wonderful.

Maybe I was just overthinking it.

Zhao Sanshi was still laughing wildly, and his men joined in.

"Hahaha, hahaha!"

"Hahahaha!"

Seeing this, the scholar thought to himself, "Since our chieftain is laughing so happily, I won't spoil the fun."

He downed another bowl of wine.

The laughter of his brothers from the surrounding stronghold filled the room, echoing as if they had witnessed some great joy.

Suddenly, the scholar realized something.

No, something's wrong!

"Chief, there's..."

Before he could finish speaking, the scholar felt someone put their arm around his shoulder, a hearty smile spreading across their face.

"Strategist, let's have a drink!"

Before he could even speak, Xu Qi suddenly felt a chill on his shoulder, a wave of dizziness washing over him.

"You...you..."

He collapsed onto the table with a thud.

Zhao Sanshi looked over. "Hahaha, Strategist's drunk? Is your alcohol tolerance that low?"

"Hahahaha."

Zhao Sanshi laughed for a while. Years of surviving life-or-death situations told him something was wrong!

Haha, why can't I stop?

Zhao Sanshi tried to cover his mouth with his hand, but found his throat involuntarily opening wide in laughter.

"Fake medicine seller, your medicine's no good!"

"You scoundrel, what are you saying?!"

Two arguing voices rang out, a clear, crisp voice breaking in.

"Alright, alright, Senior Brother, this guy seems to have realized something."

It turned out that Xiao Tian had found a skeleton not far from where they were. Upon closer inspection, he discovered a worm-eaten growth on the skeleton.

They estimated the body had been dead for no more than a month.

Suspecting bandits lurking nearby, they told Zhao Feixing this information. After observing it, Zhao Feixing confirmed his assessment; the owner of the skeleton had died no more than a month ago.

They found the scattered bones.

Piecing them together, based on development and bone and joint wear, they deduced that it was the remains of a thirteen or fourteen-year-old child who had suffered severe injuries above the waist, but whose hand bones showed no signs of disease and normal development.

It was an accidental death.

Their verbal sparring was pre-arranged. The group explained the situation to Mu Chen, essentially testing the area to see if anyone was nearby. If so, they would follow the trail up the mountain.

This was an old sect rule: during trials, bandits and outlaws encountered would be used as practice targets for the disciples.

A little bloodshed was necessary. While it wasn't exactly a time of war and chaos, it was still quite dangerous outside.

For one thing, even though everyone would be unarmed at the grand competition, there was a huge difference between having seen blood and not.

If they couldn't bring themselves to fight on the stage, they'd be at a huge disadvantage. At that time, the strongest healers in the entire Great Qian Dynasty were all gathered there.

Unless it was a fatal injury to a vital part of the body, ordinary injuries there could almost always be revived on the spot.

Decades ago, a disciple who won a martial arts competition didn't want the prize; he only asked the seniors present to help him. That disciple had suffered a family accident that left him paralyzed, only able to move his right hand.

Seeing his filial piety, the Valley Master of Medicine King Valley used the "Marrow Cleansing Pill," the reward for first place in the martial arts competition, as collateral to gather the best physicians of the time.

The assembled medical masters discovered that the patient had been paralyzed for many years, with stiff meridians. The surgical expert Xu Yi used his "Dislocating Tendons and Bones Technique" to realign the meridians, restoring their function. The Valley Master of Medicine King Valley, a master of the Innate Realm, channeled true energy into the injured man's body. Then, a renowned surgeon pinpointed the blocked acupoints, and a master of internal medicine guided the patient's mind.

This group of people, working together, brought back to life a man who had been bedridden for nearly ten years.

The entire process took a full day. Not counting the cost of hiring the experts, the medicinal herbs alone amounted to ten years' income for a wealthy family.

Back to the main point, Zhao Sanshi, a roadside bandit, had no idea that in the eyes of these doctors, corpses were often easier to extract information from than living people.

Upon hearing this, Zhao Sanshi's fleshy face twitched, and he suddenly let out a hoarse, bitter laugh.

“So…so it was that little skeleton…”

His body swayed twice; the drug had fully taken effect. His legs gave way, and he collapsed to his knees with a thud, his hands digging into the mud, his nails carving into his flesh, supporting his last vestiges of sanity.

“If only I had known…if only I had burned it…” he gritted his teeth, the voice forced out, “Chop it into pieces, throw it in the fire, scatter the ashes…you doctors, you don’t even spare the bones! You’re more ruthless than us murderers!”

“Ruthless?” Xiao Tian crouched down, looking Zhao Sanshi straight in the eye, his tone as calm as if he were commenting on the weather. “When you chopped that child up, did you even think about what ‘ruthless’ meant?”

Zhao Sanshi’s pupils constricted sharply.

"Severe injuries above the waist, with repeated slashing marks on the bones, the force diagonally from the upper right to the lower left, a total of seven fatal wounds. There's a defensive fracture at the end of the hand bone, indicating he used his hand to block the blows before death."

Xiao Tian counted on his fingers, one by one, "Also, the degree of pelvic closure and the state of tooth eruption in the skeleton indicate an age between thirteen and fourteen years old."

Zhao Sanshi's face turned completely pale.

Zhao Feixing suddenly reached out to stop Zhao Sanshi, squatted down in front of him, and pulled a small silver knife from his leather pouch, waving it in front of him.

"I'm asking you, how many people are left in the stronghold? Tell the truth, and I'll give you a quick death. Don't tell the truth, and this knife will keep you in agony for three days and three nights. You just saw it yourself, we may not have many other skills, but we have plenty of ways to keep you alive."

Zhao Sanshi's Adam's apple bobbed several times, and he finally deflated completely: "That's it… just these people. Several groups left two months ago to start their own strongholds, and the rest you took down."

Zhao Sanshi wasn't lying. Unlike the years when he was forced to go up the mountain, the situation at the front had improved, things weren't so tense, and life at home was much better.

Zhao Feixing stared into his eyes for three breaths, confirming he wasn't lying, before standing up and putting the small silver knife away.

Zhao Sanshi's already drowsy body collapsed, ending his life.

The first day went well. Fang Yuan and his group easily dealt with Zhao Sanshi and his bandits, even finding a batch of medicinal herbs in their warehouse and discovering their connections with other bandits. This should have been a good thing, but…

After that, things started to get a little…

Strange.

The problem began on the second day when they entered the city. Although the Hunyuan Sect and Medicine King Valley weren't far apart as the crow flies, the Hunyuan Sect area was rugged, and they would have to take a long detour to get to Medicine King Valley, which would take at least ten days, and if they were delayed, it could be a month.

The next day, they entered the city. Fang Yuan and Zhao Feixing found an inn to book rooms for their junior brothers.

Leaving aside their own expenses, the money they had found at Zhao Sanshi's place—just the money from selling the medicinal herbs they had processed in their warehouse—was enough to rent an inn for several days.

However, upon arriving at the inn, they encountered the landlady's husband's passing. A large group of his relatives wanted to exploit the deceased. Fang Yuan and Zhao Feixing initially didn't want to get involved, but the group, attracted by Fang Yuan's handsome appearance and the timing of his arrival, impulsively accused him of being the landlady's lover.

Before Fang Yuan could react, Zhao Feixing couldn't hold back any longer. This group's exploitation of the deceased was already despicable; they had only come to watch the spectacle and were about to leave. Why were they dragging their junior brothers into it?

In this day and age, reputation is crucial for advancement, especially for professionals like doctors. The difference between a good and a bad reputation is vast. Take their ancestor, for example. Before achieving prominence, he was unknown, yet despite his extraordinary medical skills and ambition to break new ground, he was slandered as a heretic and his ancestor's corpse was desecrated.

It was only after their medical master silenced those people that they began to take medicine seriously.

Now, their most promising and valued junior brother, Fang Yuan, is being slandered by a group of opportunistic individuals as the adulterer of a village woman. Putting aside everything else, Zhao Feixing cannot tolerate such slander, especially considering Fang Yuan's help to him.

He immediately confronted them.

But the outcome was obvious. How could someone who diligently studies medical texts and pharmacology within the sect possibly win against a group of unreasonable, foul-mouthed individuals who dared to prey on a woman's unborn child while her husband's body was still warm?

After several rounds, Zhao Feixing was flushed with anger.

There was nothing they could do; he wouldn't reason with them. He started talking about his mother all the time, one after the other, and before long, Zhao Feixing's house was practically a scene of chaos.

It was only because Zhao Feixing was there; if Xiao Tian had been there, they would have been knocked to the ground the moment they uttered their first word.

Xiao Tian wasn't going to argue with them. With them around, even if they got hurt, a few doses of medicine would make them bouncing back to life, no medical bills needed.

Finally, Xiao Tian came to check on them and found his junior brother being bullied by a group of people.

Xiao Tian: (▽д▽)

Are they messing with my junior brother?

He went in and swept through the group, knocking them down one punch at a time. Fang Yuan and Zhao Feixing joined the fray.

In no time, the three of them had taken down the group. Fang Yuan even caught one trying to escape, only to discover that this guy actually possessed cultivation and was ruthless.

However, against Fang Yuan, absolute numerical superiority was nothing but paper; he was easily broken. The guy could only retaliate because he was afraid of hitting him too hard.

Then Xiao Tian realized that this guy's martial arts style was the same as the bandits they had captured on the mountain.

Upon questioning, it turned out this guy was a bandit from the mountains who wanted to make a quick buck. He'd gone up the mountain, only to find that the situation at the front lines of the Great Qian Dynasty hadn't been so dire in recent years, allowing the Emperor to focus on cleaning up the rear.

He'd become a bandit, but after realizing the situation was unfavorable, he came down. However, he refused to work honestly. He discovered his wealthy relatives in the city were seriously ill and childless, and those closer to him wanted to exploit the family's infertility. Although he had some connections, they were superficial. So he devised a plan.

"What plan?" Xiao Tian asked curiously.

The guy didn't answer, but his gaze drifted towards the still-attractive landlady.

Seeing this, Zhao Feixing and Fang Yuan instantly understood what was going on.

This kid wanted to take it all for himself!

He realized that even if he went to exploit the family's infertility, he'd be lucky to even get a sip of soup, let alone meat. He found out that the family that wanted to exploit the family had spread rumors that the landlady was responsible for Sun Li's death; she was having an affair.

Sun Chang scoffed at this claim. Sun Li's wealth came from hooking up with his boss's wife while working in the city. If she had a gigolo, what business was it of his?

However, this claim gave Sun Chang an idea. If Sun Li could get rich by hooking up with his boss's wife, why couldn't he?

Sun Chang knew his brother-in-law's family were cowards who only dared to bully a woman.

So Sun Chang put his plan into action: spreading rumors about a gigolo, intending to stage a "hero saves the damsel in distress" when they came to take advantage of him.

He would take both the woman and the money.

He had been watching from the sidelines, when Fang Yuan suddenly appeared.

Looking at Sun Chang kneeling on the ground, Zhao Feixing felt a chill run down his spine. The plan had a high probability of success. If someone hadn't insulted Fang Yuan, and he hadn't retaliated, or if Xiao Tian hadn't intervened, he might have succeeded.

Not to mention Zhao Feixing, even Xiao Tian, ​​listening from the sidelines, was dumbfounded.

The relatives who had come along were also stunned. What did they mean by "going up the mountain to become bandits and coming down"?

Won't we be considered colluding with bandits?

Some of the more level-headed people realized this and quietly led their families away.

They were just there to lend a hand; this kind of deadly work was none of their concern. Sun Li's brother-in-law's family was the fastest to run.

They didn't dare mention compensation, fearing these thugs would stab them.

Upon hearing this, the landlady was extremely grateful to Fang Yuan and said that he could stay in any room at the inn without paying. After learning that Zhao Feixing and the others were from the Hunyuan Sect, she even gave them a treasured item from her own collection as a thank-you gift.

Then they insisted that they stay a few more days.

They were told to accept the gift, not only as a token of gratitude but also as a sign of respect for the Hunyuan Sect's relief efforts for the poor.

She even mentioned that her daughter would be studying medicine at the Hunyuan Sect in the future, and this was considered advance payment.

Having no other choice, Zhao Feixing had to accept it, given her "I'll kneel down if you don't accept" attitude.

She also returned two bottles of her own anesthetic.

Afterwards, back in his inn room, he marveled at how much he had learned.

But he didn't realize this was just the beginning.

At the second inn, they encountered a young lady being chased. After she escaped to the city, they escorted her to her uncle's house. On the way, Fang Yuan and Mu Chen encountered an assassin and fought him. The details are roughly as follows:

Fang Yuan noticed someone and searched.

Fang Yuan found the assassin, who unleashed a hidden weapon attack.

Fang Yuan defended successfully.

Fang Yuan counterattacked, and the assassin attempted to escape.

The assassin died.

Then, amidst the other party's profuse thanks, they escorted them to their destination and gave Fang Yuan and his companions a considerable sum of money, enough for about five more trips.

They insisted they stay a few more days.

The third time at the inn, there were no wandering rich girls or scoundrels taking advantage of their families. They simply randomly chose an inn and happened to witness two young men from two families who had a long-standing feud arguing over a woman. A disagreement escalated into a fight, drawing swords and prompting the intervention of their parents. The situation escalated, and the deep-seated grudges between the two families erupted, leading to a duel between their elders.

The bad news was that no one brought them gifts anymore.

But the good news was that they could earn more than just gifts.

Although the two families had a duel, low-level squabbles and clashes occurred frequently. No one was named, but there were many large, bleeding wounds, and some even had severed limbs.

Knowing the reputation of the Hunyuan Sect's surgeons, the two families went directly to their residence seeking medical help. They couldn't just stand by and watch someone die.

Well, thankfully there were many people this time, otherwise they would have been working non-stop. The external injury medicine that Hunyuan Sect originally planned to sell gradually along the way was completely sold out by two families. Later, they said their wound medicine was no different in effect from the local ones, but people still insisted on their medicine, each offering a higher price than the last.

Finally, Mu Chen couldn't persuade them otherwise and set a maximum price, a 10% premium over the market price, but it was still sold out. Not only two families, but also some local doctors, who heard their medicine was effective and came specifically to buy it to study, regardless of how Fang Yuan explained, they were convinced their medicine was the best. At the same time, both families liked to come to them for any injuries or illnesses.

They were delayed for several more days.

The money they earned was enough for eight more round trips.

But honestly, this money wasn't very enjoyable. Fang Yuan and the others were witnessing the cruelty of the martial world for the first time; a quarrel, a moment of hot-bloodedness, resulted in two families shedding blood.

Although this was a result of long-standing animosity between the two families, it was still remarkable that someone who could be chatting casually with you yesterday was now lying on the ground bruised and battered, some even with broken legs. If the Hunyuan Sect group hadn't arrived in this city, given the local medical standards, at least 30% more would have died, and half more would have suffered long-term health problems.

It wasn't that the local doctors were incompetent; quite the opposite, their surgical skills, especially in orthopedics, surprised both Xiao Tian and Fang Yuan.

Both were highly skilled surgeons, and it was clear the doctors here were exceptionally skilled. They learned that the two families had a long-standing feud. Martial artists, in their prime, were prone to injuries, and the local doctors were experienced in orthopedics.

This also demonstrated the deep-seated and irreconcilable animosity between the two families. The exact origins of their feud were unknown, but this resentment had indeed been passed down, leading to the deaths of both family heads in a final battle in the rain.

Fang Yuan and the others witnessed the cruelty and helplessness of this martial world.

Zhao Feixing watched as both sides carried the two bodies back, sighing, "In the martial world, one is often powerless."

"Senior brother, is there really no way?" Fang Yuan watched this scene. It had nothing to do with him, yet these two sides, who didn't even know the cause of their grudge, had dragged their juniors into hatred, creating future trouble.

Zhao Feixing looked at Fang Yuan, opened his mouth, but couldn't say anything.

And then, was he supposed to tell his junior brother there was no way, to let this fledgling junior brother see the cruelty of the world?

Zhao Feixing didn't want to, he really didn't want to. Zhao Feixing hoped his junior brother would always be so kind, but in this martial world filled with scheming and cruelty, this kindness, along with his talent, dragged Fang Yuan into one vortex after another.

He wanted to tell Fang Yuan that this had always been the way, and what could they do?

"There is a way."

A weary voice rang out. Xiao Tian walked to their side and continued,

“There is a way, but it’s too difficult.”

“What way?” Zhao Feixing asked, a mixture of curiosity and longing.

Xiao Tian’s weary face uttered a name that was both logical and unexpected.

“Martial power.”

“Unparalleled martial power.”

Zhao Feixing was taken aback by this answer, scratching his head, and said,

“Well…”

This answer was correct; with the unparalleled martial power Mu Chen mentioned, many such incidents could indeed be suppressed. However, it was also a wrong answer.
