Unparalleled martial power was powerful enough, but it would also bring an absolute, unquestionable authority, causing countless people to cling to him, using him in the shadows, drinking his blood, and standing on others again, exploiting them to the bone.

But it is indeed a solution. If someone could achieve such unparalleled martial prowess, in literature there is no first place, but in martial arts there is no second. Whatever that person wants to do, as long as he desires it, his fists, his strength, and his subordinates will pave the way for him.

However…

“It’s easier said than done, and some things cannot be solved simply by force.”

A voice rang out, and Mu Chen stepped out. Listening to his junior brothers' conversation, he couldn't help but say a few words.

Martial arts can indeed solve ninety percent of problems in the martial world, but the remaining ten percent is the most crucial.

Like the springs of the Mo family, even if you compress it with immense force until it's reduced to a mere stub, the slightest loosening will cause it to spring back with lightning speed.

Regarding the conflict between the two families, if martial arts could resolve it, with Mu Chen present, their family heads wouldn't have died in the competition, and so many people wouldn't have suffered serious injuries.

May the world be free of illness, even if it means letting the medicine cabinet gather dust.

Mu Chen had tried to mediate the conflict between the two families, and both family heads clearly told him that the current situation was beyond their control. Having reached this point, the two families needed to reach a resolution.

Even if Mu Chen could kill them both with a single palm strike, could he kill both families? Even if he could, he didn't want to.

In the end, Mu Chen only received enough money for their group to make eight more trips, and the corpses of the two dead family heads.

This brought an imperfect end to the feud between the two families.

“Force is important, but not everything. Sometimes, what's needed isn't force, but…”

“Something that makes people stop and think about the pros and cons.”

Something that makes people stop thinking… about the pros and cons…

Fang Yuan pondered this sentence.

Why were the disputes among the common people in the previous world, though existing, not on a large scale?

In this world, even though the two families had almost forgotten the reason for their feud, they were still drawing swords against each other, breaking bones and bleeding.

Fang Yuan kept thinking about this question, from the time they finished chatting, to eating and sleeping, he looked at the bright full moon outside.

Fang Yuan seemed to float between heaven and earth, becoming a drifting cloud. The affairs of the world were merely a leaf obscuring his view, easily swept away. Just as he was about to choose to drift between heaven and earth…

One by one, figures appeared: Fang Chenxu, Fang Xiuxiu, Gu Changming, Mu Chen, and Mu Jingxing. Each name, each event, surfaced.

This pulled Fang Yuan back to the ground, allowing him to connect with the past of these people.

The threads of emotion, like a net, wove into a mountain, heavy as a thousand burdens.

So that's how it is…

I was mistaken.

But I've also come to understand.



Chapter 44 The Stepping Stone for the Male Protagonist in a Wuxia Story: The Holy Son 14


Fang Yuan sat up, repeatedly pondering that flash of inspiration, finding it increasingly clear.

Force is a fundamental necessity. Without unparalleled martial prowess, even the best reasoning is just empty words, unable to control the swords or stop the bleeding. But force alone is not enough—something else is needed to halt the boiling blood before it reaches the breaking point, to allow the head clouded by passion to consider the pros and cons.

Rules.

Rules supported by sufficient force. Even in the moment before drawing swords, both sides must weigh the pros and cons: is this strike truly worthwhile?

Early the next morning, Fang Yuan found Mu Chen and explained his thoughts to him.

Mu Chen listened intently. Sunlight streamed through the window, falling beside him. He remained silent for a long time, so long that Fang Yuan thought he was about to say, "A pipe dream."

But Mu Chen neither denied it nor affirmed it.

He simply raised his eyes and calmly asked, "Do you know how the Xia Dynasty fell?"

Fang Yuan was taken aback and shook his head.

History wasn't untaught within the sect. Physicians needed to be familiar with medical cases throughout history, so naturally they had to read history books. But when it came to the reasons for the Xia Dynasty's downfall, the teachers were always vague. He and his fellow disciples had discussed it privately—some said it was due to a lack of virtue, others said it was due to insufficient martial prowess, but every explanation couldn't withstand scrutiny, and no answer could convince everyone.

Seeing him shake his head, Mu Chen slowly spoke.

"The fall of the previous dynasty wasn't due to insufficient martial prowess, nor was it due to a lack of virtue." His voice was soft, yet carried a weight of experience. "On the contrary, the previous dynasty excelled in both."

Fang Yuan was stunned.

"From its founding, the Xia Dynasty revered Legalist thought, and its national strength far surpassed what modern people can imagine. Later, a ruler, seeing the long-standing chaos and deep-seated blood feuds in the martial world, resolved to restore order and bring the entire martial world under the court's control. He implemented military law, using military discipline to restrain warriors and regulate all affairs within the martial world."

Mu Chen paused, his gaze drifting into the distance, as if looking at a long-forgotten past.

"The idea wasn't wrong. But there was a problem—a huge problem."

As Fang Yuan listened, a strange sense of familiarity suddenly welled up within him.

Isn't this… the conflict between the individual and the collective, the individual will and the unified order? He had seen similar stories in history books in his previous life, over and over again.

Mu Chen continued, “Knights-errant use their martial arts to break the law. The Xia Dynasty implemented harsh laws, with each level adding to the burden, inevitably leading to loopholes for corrupt officials. Those who were oppressed, possessing martial prowess and harboring resentment, would inevitably clash with the court. This was commonplace; which dynasty didn't? But the last emperor didn't see it that way.”

“He felt his nation was powerful, that all under heaven belonged to the king, and all people within the realm were his subjects. Therefore, he issued a series of coercive decrees, incorporating the previously scattered martial arts factions into the imperial system, forcibly managing local sects and families, ordering local powers to obey officials appointed by the court, and even mandating that sects recruit disciples and family martial arts competitions follow imperial rules.”

Fang Yuan's eyelids twitched. How similar these methods were—examples from his previous life of hasty centralization of power backfiring flashed through his mind.

The last Xia emperor's combined approach was like a cascade of Yang Guang's ambition, Hu Hai's harsh laws, and Li Longji's stubbornness in his later years.

Imperial power took over his mind; self-importance replaced critical thinking, and he didn't consider whether he could sustain the regime.

"Thus, resistance erupted across the land," Mu Chen's tone remained calm, but beneath that calm lay a turbulent undercurrent. "And the officials dispatched by the court to the provinces were themselves from powerful local families. The military commanders, even more so, had countless ties to various factions. The laws severed their roots from them; how could they possibly wield their swords?"

"The Xia Dynasty, after five generations of rulers, finally collapsed."

After a moment of silence, Mu Chen looked out the window; the sky was just beginning to brighten.

"Afterwards, the world descended into chaos, with numerous warlords vying for power. One faction sought to restore the ancient feudal system, reshaping the land into numerous vassal states. Ultimately, however, the one who seized power was the current emperor. He continued the Xia Dynasty's system, maintaining imperial dominance and preventing the general from succeeding."

Indeed, once the concept of unification was instilled, no wise person would become the eternal villain.

River civilizations relied on river plains and agriculture for survival, while maritime civilizations were different. Without major rivers to obstruct their path, when the first ruler proclaimed unification, the seed of unification was planted in the hearts of every ambitious individual.

Unlike the previous world's dynasty, which perished after only two generations, the Xia Dynasty in this world enjoyed a long reign, lasting 120 years. Aside from the relatively short lifespans of its emperors, given the nation's strength at the time, it could have lasted at least another 80 years without resorting to extreme policies.

Fang Yuan's mind stirred. Mu Chen's deliberate mention of this must have a purpose.

"After the founding emperor ascended the throne, he also realized that while the Xia emperor's measures were too radical, they weren't entirely without merit. The martial world couldn't remain a chaotic mess of disarray, where swords spoke forever; there had to be a thread connecting it. But at that time, the empire was newly established, with a ravaged land within and foreign tribes lurking outside. The founding emperor wanted to reform, but lacked the power to implement it. He could only make some compromises—stipulating that martial arts garrisons in various regions had the authority to monitor local forces, while strictly prohibiting martial arts forces from interfering with the daily livelihoods of ordinary people."

Mu Chen turned to look at Fang Yuan, his gaze filled with a complex understanding.

"That's why those two families fought to the death, while you, along your journey, rarely saw ordinary people caught in the crossfire. That thread, though thin, still exists."

Fang Yuan suddenly understood. Then his heart sank—that thread was merely a fragile balance, a stopgap measure left behind when the founding emperor was unable to thoroughly reform. If they wanted to go any further, the bloodstains of the previous dynasty were still fresh; who dared to touch them lightly?

Mu Chen looked at him, her gaze softening slightly: "Fang Yuan, it's good that you have this intention. But this isn't something we should be considering right now. The upcoming conference is what you should be focusing on."

Fang Yuan nodded, remaining silent.

Fang Yuan thought to himself: My thinking is correct.

This path is the right one. The martial world cannot be governed solely by swords and spears, nor by empty promises from the government. It must be based on rules, using force as its sword, giving the rules teeth and the force reins.

And to pave this path, only one thing can clear the way:

Unparalleled martial prowess.

Fang Yuan lowered his eyes, burying those words deep within his heart, like planting a seed in newly awakened soil.

………………

“No, we can't go on like this.”

Xiao Tian groaned to the others.

After several unexpected events, the group realized something was wrong.

Given their stamina, even on their first trip, after navigating a few rough terrains, the rest was flat road. Reaching Medicine King Valley in 20 days would be ample time. Yet, they had set off a full month early.

However, after several unexpected events, they discovered they had already traveled for 15 days. Logically, they should be close to their destination by now, but they were only halfway there. If they continued this stop-and-go pace, with one trivial matter every three days and another adventure every five, they wouldn't even make it to the conference. They might even run into acquaintances halfway through the journey.

Xiao Tian and Mu Chen discussed it for a moment, then pointed to the map and said to everyone, "We'll reach open plains soon, the road will be easier. We need to hurry and catch up."

How could they explain to their sect if they couldn't make it?

The other disciples had no objections. Traveling the martial world, what journey doesn't involve hardship? Besides, although they had been delayed for quite some time, upon reflection—they had dealt with the wicked relatives who had wiped out their families, rescued the young lady being chased, and witnessed the blood feud between two clans. Each of these was an extraordinary event; an ordinary person could talk about one of these for two or three years, and they had encountered them all.

Just seeing wasn't enough; the gains they had made along the way were enough for their sect to make a dozen more round trips.

But the journey still had to be taken; otherwise, if all the other sects arrived while they were the only ones missing, their sect would suffer a great loss of face.

Strangely enough, for the first twenty days or so, one strange thing after another happened, as if they had stumbled upon some kind of luck. But once they focused on their journey, the martial world became quiet.

The young lady wandering the streets was gone, and they hadn't encountered the descendant of a loyal official being hunted down. However, their junior brothers, while scouting in the wilderness, unexpectedly stumbled upon two extremely rare and beautiful medicinal herbs.

Zhao Feixing was truly amazed by this luck.

Why didn't they have this kind of luck when they left before?

Zhao Qiming squatted down, examining the two medicinal herbs, clicking his tongue in amazement. "These things, if sold in the market, would probably be enough for another round trip." Before he could finish speaking, Xiao Tian grabbed him by the back of the collar and lifted him up. "Take them and go, enough talk."

Zhao Feixing muttered, "Coming with Junior Brother this time was really a steal. Ah, why didn't we have this luck back then?"

"Alright, alright, we still have a long way to go. Take it easy."

Xiao Tian scolded irritably.

And so, after a hurried journey, five days before the start of the conference, the Hunyuan Sect group finally entered the territory of Medicine King Valley. Medicine King Valley, though called a valley, felt like a blessed land hidden deep in the mountains. Surrounded by green mountains like a screen, the valley itself was open and flat, with a stream flowing through it. Along the banks were bamboo houses and wooden pavilions with upturned eaves, exuding an atmosphere completely different from the Central Plains.

The valley has a mild climate, and even in late autumn, unnamed wildflowers are still blooming profusely, with a faint herbal fragrance floating in the air.

Arriving five days early wasn't exactly early, but the inns throughout the valley were already packed with guests from all walks of life: young talents attending the conference, disciples from various sects escorting their followers, wandering martial artists drawn by the news, and even family members of patients suffering from rare illnesses.

From the beginning until now, it had been quite a lively event in the martial arts world.

Mu Chen had intended to arrange accommodations for his fellow disciples, but found that although they hadn't arrived late, the inns were already full of people from all over.

Well, it seemed there was nowhere to spend money.

Finally, the people of Medicine King Valley stepped in and led them to the guesthouses prepared specifically for the participating sects. The rooms weren't spacious, but they were clean and tidy, and at least the disciples had somewhere to stay.

Fang Yuan placed his bundle on the bed, found a room to wash up, and changed into a clean white outfit, making him appear handsome and dashing—a truly spirited young swordsman.

Standing by the window, Fang Yuan felt the gentle breeze and sensed the changes in his body.

Since his conversation with Mu Chen that day, a vague idea had begun to take root in Fang Yuan's mind.

What is the role of the protagonist? To ride the wave of fate and destiny, a trendsetter of the times.

What is the role of the protagonist in this world?

After that day's contemplation, Fang Yuan had vaguely grasped a glimmer of understanding, but it wasn't entirely clear.

During his journey afterward, Fang Yuan noticed subtle changes in his body.

At that moment, he felt as if he were merging with the outer world, as if the heavens and he were one with the infinite, yet he also seemed to be pulled back.

Xiao Tian pushed open the door and came in. Seeing Fang Yuan standing by the window, lost in thought, he patted him on the shoulder: "What are you doing cooped up inside? Come on, let's go out for a walk. It's your first time in Medicine King Valley, you should at least see the local customs and culture."

Fang Yuan responded and followed Xiao Tian out the door.

The valley was more lively than he had imagined. Stalls selling medicinal herbs lined both sides of the streets. Almost every kind of herb from all over the country could be found here. Some Fang Yuan had only seen illustrations in medical books; seeing the real thing for the first time, he couldn't help but squat down to examine them closely.

The stall owner, seeing that they were two young men, greeted them with a smile: "Young brothers, are you here for the event? Want to buy a couple of herbs to practice with?"

Fang Yuan smiled and shook his head. While the herbs on the stall were decent, they seemed a bit expensive compared to the prices the stall owner quoted.

With such large events, it was inevitable that the locals would try to squeeze some money out of outsiders.

However, most of the people here were physicians; surely they knew these medicinal herbs well?

The closer they went to the center of the valley, the more people there were. Fang Yuan unknowingly found himself ahead, with Xiao Tian leisurely following behind, not urging him on. The valley had a mild climate, and the locals' clothing differed from that of the Central Plains. The women mostly wore brightly colored dresses and silver bracelets on their wrists, which jingled melodiously as they moved, creating a unique and exotic atmosphere.

Fang Yuan was so engrossed in admiring the scenery that he didn't realize he had become part of the scenery himself.

A tall, slender young man, dressed in the simple, moon-white robe of the Hunyuan Sect, stood there with a handsome and refined air, exuding youthful vigor and charm.

Women thronged the valley, their gazes falling on him. Some whispered amongst themselves, others tugged at their companions' sleeves, and some, bolder enough, stared directly at him. Some glanced at him repeatedly, their eyes darting back and forth – the typical girlish infatuation.

Xiao Tian, ​​watching all this from behind, grinned and quickened his pace to catch up, nudging Fang Yuan with his shoulder: "You little rascal, with such a striking face, when you stand on the stage during the competition, you probably won't even need to compete; your looks alone could win over half the hearts of the martial world."

Fang Yuan was taken aback, then shook his head helplessly, knowing his senior brother was teasing him again.

Xiao Tian, ​​however, didn't give up. He draped his hand over the man's shoulder and gestured with his chin towards the flower hairpin stall nearby: "Seriously, with your looks and the skills of our Hunyuan Sect, even if you don't win first place, just walking around and showing off would make countless noble ladies and senior sisters from various sects scheming to marry you off."

Yes, marry.

Due to the flourishing of the *Nourishing Life Classic* martial arts, unlike in the ordinary world, women in this world have more autonomy. Some highly skilled women even have a life filled with romantic escapades that rival those of men.

For noble families, daughters are sometimes even more valuable than sons. This has led to numerous cases of women marrying into wealthy families.

Xiao Tian paused, then winked and said, "So, how about it? Want your senior brother to keep an eye out for you?"

Fang Yuan was both amused and exasperated, pushing the arm off his shoulder. "Senior brother, stop teasing me."

"Hey, how is this teasing?" Xiao Tian laughed heartily. "I'm just worried our junior brother's standards are too high. He'll look down on everyone, and when we get back to the sect, Master will have to worry about his marriage."

He was only fifteen or sixteen years old, still a budding talent in their medical family. As long as his marriage didn't cross any lines, the elders would naturally let him be.

Of course, his senior brothers and sisters would also help with the selection process.

Fang Yuan didn't reply, only looking at the bustling crowd ahead, a helpless smile on his lips.

Five days passed quickly, yet slowly.

During these days, Fang Yuan hardly left the guest house.

At dawn, the bell rang in the valley.

The bell tolled from the Hundred Herbs Pavilion, the highest point in Medicine King Valley, striking nine times in total. Deep and resonant, it seemed to emanate from the depths of the mountain, echoing against the surrounding green hills before returning, its lingering resonance filling the entire valley.

The triennial Medicine King Valley Assembly officially opened.

Hearing the sound, Fang Yuan exhaled a breath of stale air.

Is it finally here?

My first step



Chapter 45 The Stepping Stone for the Wuxia Male Protagonist: The Holy Son 15


Nine chimes echoed through the valley, their lingering sound still reverberating against the mountainside. On the highest viewing platform in the center of the hall, a figure slowly stepped forward.

The man was slender, his hair and beard as white as the first snow of winter. His green robe fluttered slightly in the valley breeze. It was none other than Sun Sixian, the current master of Medicine King Valley and a renowned healer.

Sun Sixian didn't use his inner strength to amplify his voice. Simply standing before the platform, without further ado, he began:

"The 137th Medicine King Valley Conference begins—"

His voice wasn't loud, but it reached the ears of everyone present clearly.

As soon as these words were spoken, waiting disciples began to call out:

"Disciples of all sects, please enter."

As soon as the words fell, the ceremonial officials, who had been waiting on both sides of the hall, struck gongs. Disciples from the valley led their respective groups, filing in single file from the east and west ends of the plaza.

First to enter was the Thousand Gold Pavilion. Located in the prosperous Jiangnan region, the disciples of the Thousand Gold Pavilion wore brocade robes and jade pendants, their movements composed and their every gesture exuding the air of wealth and power.

The wealthier one is, the more afraid of death one becomes. With the flourishing commerce of Jiangnan, the wealthy merchants were especially afraid of death and had a particular pursuit of medical and health preservation methods. Therefore, a group of people pooled their money to invest in a successor and established the Thousand Gold Pavilion.

With the financial support of various wealthy merchants, the Thousand Gold Pavilion possessed substantial wealth, especially in a country that had revived under the rule of several generations of Qian Dynasty emperors, making it a formidable force.

Leading the procession was a young man in his early twenties, with a handsome face and a perfectly measured smile. He passed the viewing area without glancing to either side, heading straight for the center of the arena.

From a nearby bamboo pavilion, someone whispered, "That's Ji Mingzhao, the young master of the Thousand Gold Pavilion. I heard he's mastered the 'Golden Needle Acupuncture Technique'."

Next came the Hundred Flowers Valley. All the disciples of Hundred Flowers Valley were women, dressed in simple silk skirts, adorned with flowers and herbs. They emerged from the passageway. The leading female disciple was beautiful and slender, with a long, emerald-green sword hanging at her waist, its scabbard adorned with unknown dried flowers. She was none other than Su Wantang, the rising star of the Hundred Flowers Valley.

As she passed the Hunyuan Sect's procession, her gaze seemed to sweep over them almost imperceptibly, as if she were looking at something.

Next came the Shennong Sect, the Qingyun Medical Clinic, the Lingshu Sect… medical sects from all corners of the land entered in turn, each group displaying its own unique character—some dignified and composed, some sharp and assertive, some understated and reserved. Colorful flags fluttered in the wind above the venue.

When it was the Hunyuan Sect's turn to enter, the master of ceremonies announced loudly, “Hunyuan Sect—”

Fang Yuan took a deep breath and walked alongside Mu Chen at the head of the procession. Behind them were Xiao Tian and Zhao Feixing, followed by Zhao Qiming, Meng Ming, and their fellow disciples.

The group marched in perfect unison, their robes simple and clean, the mountain-patterned emblems on their lapels faintly visible in the morning light, illuminating the excited faces of those behind them.

However, it was irrelevant to the Hunyuan Sect's imposing presence, for the aura of the two at the forefront was enough to draw everyone's attention.

Mu Chen and Fang Yuan walked side by side, the two most outstanding disciples of the Hunyuan Sect in the last hundred years.

Mu Chen is naturally beautiful, and with his excellent physique from diligently practicing martial arts and the refined temperament cultivated from reading medical books and pharmacology, he is truly as gentle and refined as jade.

Beside him, Fang Yuan was no less impressive. Although still young, his mastery of martial arts had given him a height comparable to many young men. His physique was already tall and slender, with broad shoulders, a narrow waist, and a well-defined, streamlined frame. His appearance was also exceptional.

Unlike Mu Chen's gentle and refined demeanor, Fang Yuan possessed a cool and composed air. His sword-like eyebrows slanted sharply towards his temples, and his phoenix eyes were long, narrow, and deep, devoid of any youthful naiveté, subtly revealing a distant and aloof demeanor.

The moment Fang Yuan appeared, many of the young girls in Hundred Flowers Valley seemed glued to him.

Many of the more seasoned members, seeing their positions, suddenly shifted their conversation to them.

An elderly man sitting in a bamboo shed on the left stroked his long beard, bowed slightly, and said to his companion, "Did you see clearly the young man leading the Hunyuan Sect this year?"

His companion squinted. "So young, yet he's standing next to Mu Chen?"

The old man smiled. "You don't know. That young man is Fang Yuan."

"Fang Yuan? That Fang Yuan?" His companion was taken aback, then realized, "The one who invented the anesthetic and that bone-setting technique?"

The old man nodded. "That's him. The Hunyuan Sect has truly encountered good fortune this generation. First there was Mu Chen, and now Fang Yuan has emerged."

The old man couldn't help but sigh. Could the Hengyi Mountains really be some kind of auspicious place?

In just over a decade, two prodigies, Mu Chen and Fang Yuan, have emerged one after another.

Similar conversations were taking place elsewhere in the viewing area. Some disciples who were previously unaware of the situation couldn't hide their surprise when they saw that the leader of the Hunyuan Sect was a fifteen or sixteen-year-old boy.

The line was full of young men in their twenties, so why was a teenager standing at the front? Those in the know whispered amongst themselves, their surprise quickly turning to understanding—it was him.

The prodigy who supposedly improved anesthesia and pioneered a new surgical procedure for bone surgery last year.

Once they understood, their thoughts diverged.

Some wore expressions of admiration, some seemed thoughtful, and others let out a soft snort.

A disciple sitting at the back of the Qianjin Pavilion line glanced sideways at Fang Yuan and whispered to the person beside him, "Impressive pharmacology doesn't equate to superior martial arts. The Medical Tournament isn't just about writing prescriptions; when it comes to actually treating patients and improvising, who knows what he'll do…"

Before he could finish, a calm glance from the leading youth silenced him.

Didn't he consider the circumstances surrounding the Han Tieshan incident that had made Fang Yuan famous?

Thinking this, the young man secretly shook his head.

In his opinion, he was destined to be number one on the pharmacology list this year.

Fang Yuan, however, paid no heed to these discussions. He walked where the morning light met countless gazes, his steps unhurried, his posture upright and dignified. His junior brothers behind him were infected by his composure, their previously tense shoulders gradually relaxing.

After all the factions had entered, Sun Sixian spoke again. This time, he spoke of the competition schedule.

"Gentlemen, you have come from afar; I thank you in advance. This conference, following the wisdom of our predecessors, will consist of two parts," he said, holding up two fingers. "The first is a written examination on pharmacology. The examination will assess your basic pharmacological knowledge, prescription compatibility, and case analysis. The papers will be divided into three grades: A, B, and C, each further subdivided into upper, middle, and lower levels. Rankings will be based on your scores."

A slight murmur rippled through the audience. The written pharmacology examination was a tradition of the Medicine King Valley Conference, so it wasn't unexpected. However, the rule of grading and ranking was something they had never heard of before.

Sun Sixian ignored the uproar below and continued, "Secondly, the practical test. After the written exam, an examination hall will be set up in the valley where disciples from each school will conduct on-site diagnosis, acupuncture, medicine preparation, and bone setting, using real patients as subjects to test their clinical skills. This will last for five days, one subject per day. After five days, the total scores will be tallied to determine the top four."

He paused, his gaze sweeping over the hundreds of young faces below, his tone softening slightly: "The path of medicine is about benefiting the world. Ranking is secondary; mutual learning is paramount. I hope that you will all demonstrate your skills over the next five days, so that this old man and my fellow practitioners can witness the potential of today's rising medical talents."

As soon as he finished speaking, the master of ceremonies struck a gong, announcing the end of today's ceremony. The disciples could disperse and gather at the square at Chenshi (7-9 AM) tomorrow for the formal pharmacology written exam.

The crowd dispersed in twos and threes. Fang Yuan walked out with the flow of people, suddenly feeling a tap on his shoulder.

Turning around, he saw Xiao Tian, ​​followed by Zhao Feixing and Zhao Qiming. Several junior brothers huddled behind Zhao Meng, chattering excitedly about the scene that had just unfolded.

Zhao Qiming was still counting on his fingers: "Grade A, upper-middle-lower; Grade B, upper-middle-lower; Grade C, upper-middle-lower—once the scores are posted on the list, won't it be immediately clear who's high and who's low?

Tsk, this isn't a friendly competition, it's clearly a public execution."

Meng Ping rolled his eyes at him: "You should first think about whether you can even get into Grade B." Zhao Qiming was speechless, scratching his head and remaining silent.

Fang Yuan listened to his junior brothers' chatter, a slight smile playing on his lips, but his gaze swept past the crowd, fixed on the square where the examination papers would be laid out the next day. The morning light was bright, illuminating the entire area.

Tomorrow.

His first step.

The next day, before dawn, the guest quarters where the Hunyuan Sect was staying were already brightly lit.

When Fang Yuan opened his eyes, a layer of bluish-gray still shrouded the outside world. He dressed, straightened his belt, and pushed open the door. A cool valley breeze, carrying the scent of herbs, brushed against his face, finally waking him completely.

"Senior Brother."

Zhao Qiming and the others were already waiting in the courtyard, clutching their writing implements, their expressions increasingly tense, as if they, not Fang Yuan, were the ones taking the exam.

Mu Chen strolled over from the corridor. Their eyes met, and Mu Chen smiled slightly, "Good luck! Senior Brother is waiting for you to become famous throughout the land."

The examination hall was set up on the flat bluestone plaza at the foot of the main peak of Medicine King Valley. The place, which had been empty yesterday, had been transformed overnight into nearly two hundred low tables, arranged in rows and columns, each covered with plain silk, ink sticks, and vermilion brushes.

The morning mist had not yet dissipated, and the candles were still lit, casting the entire scene in a dim, flickering light, like a giant chessboard spread across the valley.

Fang Yuan found his seat, lifted his robe, and sat down. He carefully arranged his brush and ink, then closed his eyes and sat motionless, like a mountain. People gradually took their seats around him, the sounds of turning pages, clinking inkstones, and hushed whispers rising and falling, but his corner remained eerily quiet, as if encased in a veil.

Ji Mingzhao, the young master of Qianjin Pavilion, sat two rows to the left. He held a brush in his hand, his fingertips slowly caressing the handle, glancing sideways at Fang Yuan—the boy hadn't even opened his eyes.

The sound of a gong echoed across the square.

Sun Sixian's voice drifted from afar: "Pharmacology written exam, one and a half hours. Open the book."

The ink on the silk was neat and orderly, containing twelve major questions. The first six tested prescription compatibility and drug properties analysis, the next four were medical case analysis, and the last two were the most challenging, the questions densely packed, almost filling half the silk.

Fang Yuan opened his eyes, quickly scanning the entire scroll, then picked up his brush, dipped it in ink, and began answering the questions.

Under the guidance of the auxiliary system left by System 120, Fang Yuan hadn't dared to stop for a moment these past few years. He faced a daily schedule meticulously planned down to the minute, which he had gritted his teeth and persevered through. It could be said that he had memorized the sect's pharmacological texts perfectly.

He answered the first six prescription questions almost without pause. For each herb, he could instantly grasp the properties, channels, and combinations of the herbs, their processing methods, and the appropriate contraindications. To avoid mistakes, he would still review the questions a couple of times.

An elder from Medicine King Valley, responsible for patrolling, passed by him, paused, said nothing, and walked away with his hands behind his back, continuing his patrol on the other side. When he returned after completing his round, the young man had already turned over the scroll and begun answering the medical questions.

The seventh case: The patient, aged fifty, suffered from chest pain and palpitations. His tongue was purplish-dark with ecchymosis, and his pulse was irregular and knotted. Fang Yuan pondered briefly and wrote down "a modified version of Peach Kernel and Safflower Decoction." He carefully adjusted the dosages of Red Peony Root, Sichuan Lovage Rhizome, and Corydalis Rhizome, and noted at the end, "If there is concurrent phlegm, add Trichosanthes Fruit and Allium Macrostrum; if qi deficiency is significant, reduce the amount of Peach Kernel and increase Astragalus Root."

The eighth, ninth, and tenth cases followed. He wrote each case with a clear diagnostic approach, the basis for the prescription, and modifications, every word a gem.

Just over an hour later, he had completed all twelve major questions.

Fang Yuan did not rush to submit his paper. He meticulously checked the entire paper twice, confirming that the dosage of every herb was correct and that every modification was reasonable, before finally putting down his pen and handing in his paper.

The official in charge of collecting the papers glanced at him as he took the exam paper, his lips moved as if to speak, but he ultimately said nothing, simply placing the paper in a sealed box and affixing the seal.

As he left the examination hall, the sun had just climbed over the eastern mountains. A large crowd had already gathered outside the square, mostly accompanying elders from their sects and disciples who had submitted their papers early. The moment Fang Yuan appeared, at least a dozen pairs of eyes fell upon him simultaneously.

Someone recognized him and whispered, "That Fang Yuan from the Hunyuan Sect, that's him."

"Out so early? Did he hand in a blank paper?" a young disciple from some unknown sect muttered under his breath. Someone next to him scoffed, "What are you thinking? Someone who can improve anesthetic and bone surgery, would hand in a blank paper for a pharmacology exam?"

"That's him! He looks only about my age, yet he's achieved so much."

Fang Yuan seemed oblivious to the discussions. He found a stone bench under the shade of a tree, sat down, took a sip of water from his water pouch, closed his eyes to rest, and remained calm as if nothing had happened.

One by one, some disciples of the Hunyuan Sect also emerged. Meng Ping's expression was relatively composed, while Zhao Qiming appeared completely lost in thought, being helped out by Meng Ping.

"It's all over, all over, all over!" Zhao Qiming plopped down on the ground. "That last medical case—what illness was it? It looked like a stroke or a phlegm syncope to me! I didn't dare put pen to paper; I spent the last half hour on that question."

Meng Ping gloated beside him: "So what did you write in the end?"

Zhao Qiming looked at him blankly: "...A modified version of the Life-Sustaining Decoction."

Meng Ping was taken aback: "Life-extending soup?"

"Because I feel like I'm about to die."

Everyone burst into laughter, attracting the attention of people from several nearby sects. Zhao Qiming, embarrassed by the laughter, changed the subject, asking Fang Yuan, "Senior Brother Fang, um... how did you answer that question?"

Fang Yuan thought for a moment and said, "The differentiation between a true stroke and a stroke-like condition."

Zhao Qiming blinked, then suddenly stood up: "I'll go for a walk over there." After taking a few steps, he turned back, "No, I'm not going anymore. Anyway, the results will be released in two days."

The written exam lasted two days, both in the morning, and the results would be released two days later.

A grade of C or above is the limiting condition. This may be slightly changed each year, but it generally stays within this timeframe. Only those who achieve this grade can proceed to the next practical exam.

Otherwise, where would Medicine King Valley find so many patients for them to treat?

This pharmacology exam alone filters out disciples who make it into the fourth level. Each Medicine King Valley Grand Meeting has about three to four hundred participants, from five to six sects. Each sect brings an average of about 40 to 50 disciples, and about 100 are selected each year to receive the "Apricot Grove Inscription."

Each sect usually only brings about ten to twenty disciples who actually receive it; most are brought to broaden their horizons and make friends with fellow disciples.

Fang Yuan didn't say anything more. He stood up, brushed the grass clippings off his robes, and walked back side-by-side with Mu Chen. Behind them, Zhao Qiming was still chasing Meng Ping, asking for details, while Xiao Tian followed with a smile, his hands in his sleeves. The group walked back to the guest courtyard in the afterglow of the setting sun.

Two days later

Three large wooden plaques, each taller than a person, stood before the square. The top-ranked list was in the center, the second-ranked list on the left, and the third-ranked list on the right. The viewing area and bamboo pavilions were packed with elders and disciples from various sects. The elders of Medicine King Valley stood in a row, holding gilded scrolls in their hands.

Zhao Qiming was the one who had come to run the errand. He had gone to the square early in the morning to offer to guard the list, arriving at 5:45 AM. Zhao Feixing and Meng Ping tried to persuade him to come back and have breakfast, but he didn't turn around, tossing out, "I can't wait any longer," and disappeared into the morning mist.

When the Hunyuan Sect members arrived at the square, the list had just been posted. The crowd was immense, with those at the front craning their necks and those behind standing on tiptoe. Zhao Qiming stood on the outermost edge of the crowd, his eyes fixed on the top-ranked list, his mouth agape, as if he had seen something unbelievable.

"Qiming?" Xiao Tian called out to him.

Zhao Qiming turned around, his knuckles white as he pointed to a spot on the list: "Senior Brother Fang, he..."

Everyone looked in the direction he was pointing.

At the very top of the list of top-tier students, several large, vividly written characters read: Top Tier 1: Fang Yuan of the Hunyuan Sect.

Next were the leading disciples of each family, about nine in total. Disciples from all families were on the list, though their rankings varied.

Moreover, unlike the paper scrolls and silk scrolls used at the Medicine King Valley Assembly, these were woven from the silk spun by the unique spirit cicadas found around Hunyuan Medicine Mountain, specifically used to record the top tier. Now, after a full thirty-one sessions, Medicine King Valley was adding new silk.

Most eye-catching was Ji Mingzhao, the young master of the Thousand Gold Pavilion, ranked second in the top tier, firmly seated in second place. Third was Su Wantang of the Hundred Flowers Valley, ranked third in the top tier.

Only these three names were listed in the top tier.

At first glance, Fang Yuan's name stood out prominently at the top.

A murmur of surprise and excitement erupted from the crowd.

"Fang Yuan! The same Hunyuan Sect disciple who handed in his paper early yesterday?"

"Ji Mingzhao is actually ranked below him."

"What a prodigy! What makes the Hunyuan Sect so capable? Producing such geniuses one after another!"

"I told you all before." A junior brother from the Hunyuan Sect puffed out his chest, trying to sound nonchalant, but his slightly trembling voice betrayed him.

Standing in the Qianjin Pavilion line, Ji Mingzhao looked at the list, remained silent for a moment, then nodded slightly, as if he had expected this result. The junior brother beside him, who had questioned Fang Yuan yesterday, didn't dare to breathe loudly now.

Su Wantang from Baihua Valley didn't show any particular expression. She simply looked at Fang Yuan's name, gave a soft "Oh," and whispered to her junior sisters beside her, "I thought it was an exaggeration, but it turns out it's true."

And Fang Yuan?

Throughout, Fang Yuan stood slightly off to the side of the crowd, arms crossed, his expression as calm and aloof as ever, revealing little joy. He seemed indifferent to the whispers around him, only becoming more amiable when facing his fellow disciples.

The entire afternoon, Fang Yuan's name resounded throughout Medicine King Valley.

However, Fang Yuan maintained his own pace, refusing visitors and focusing intently on preparing for the upcoming experimental exams.

On-the-spot diagnosis, acupuncture, medicine preparation, and bone setting—all based on unconventional thinking, and with the Han Tieshan incident pioneering new methods in orthopedics, Fang Yuan excelled in these areas with unstoppable momentum.

First-class, first-class, and still first-class!!

Fang Yuan crushed his contemporaries with overwhelming force; in this Medicine King Valley conference, his pharmacology was undisputed the best!

Like a blazing sun, he shone brightly, obscuring the brilliance of his peers.

It was foreseeable that, provided he progressed smoothly, he would become another medical master in a decade or so.

However, the excitement belonged to others; Fang Yuan paid no heed.

The pharmacology exam was over; he needed to prepare for the upcoming martial arts exam.

On the way back, the setting sun bathed the bluestone path in a deep gold light as Fang Yuan and his fellow disciples walked back along the mountain path. A summer breeze rustled through the bamboo forest of Medicine King Valley, the bamboo leaves rustling softly.



Chapter 46 The Stepping Stone for the Male Protagonist in a Wuxia Story: The Holy Son (16)


At dawn, the sound of gongs echoed through the valley.

On the training ground behind Medicine King Valley, sixteen blue stone arenas rose from the ground, each ten zhang (approximately 33 meters) long and wide. The arenas were constructed from whole slabs of blue stone, polished and filled with glutinous rice mortar.

Medicine King Valley had specially commissioned a master of the Mo family's mechanical arts to build these arenas. The master confidently asserted that even if dozens of Innate Realm cultivators attacked simultaneously, the arena could withstand them.

Medicine King Valley also trusted the opponents' abilities. Whether they could defeat them was uncertain, but they were certainly more than capable of dealing with these young upstarts.

What? What if some of these people possessed Innate Realm cultivators?

Haha, how could a group of twenty- or thirty-year-old lads possess Innate Realm cultivators?

Our patriarchs all attained Innate Realm at the age of 20. Impossible, absolutely impossible.

A morning breeze swept through, causing the flags above the arenas to flutter in the wind.

The martial arts competition rules stipulated that sixteen flags of different colors represented the ownership of sixteen arenas—whoever could stand on one for half an hour, or defeat eight opponents in a row, would own that flag.

Unlike the intricate rules of pharmacology, the martial arts competition's rules were simple: sixteen arenas, and according to the rules, whoever defended their position advanced directly to the next round; there were three rounds in total.

The winner was first, and could choose to rest in between.

The spectator stands were packed. Elders from various sects, disciples from the valley, and independent cultivators who had traveled from afar—over a thousand people sat there. Sun Sixian sat on the high platform in the center, flanked by several elders of Medicine King Valley and leaders from various sects.

Today he wore a dark brown robe, the collar buttoned up meticulously. He held a cup of tea in his hand, its aroma wafting, but his gaze was sharp as an eagle, scanning the arena beyond the rim of the teacup.

The rules for the first round were simple to the point of being brutal… Go on stage, fight, win or lose.

There was no drawing of lots, no grouping, no ranking system of A, B, C, or D; only sixteen arenas and one ironclad rule: those who stand remain, those who fall are eliminated.

This primitive rule was established from the very beginning of the Medicine King Valley Tournament, and successive Valley Masters have never changed it in the slightest. The reason is simple:

Healers save lives through their medical skills, but the path of medicine requires not only defying fate but also interacting with people.

If you can't cure people, they call you a quack; if you can cure them well, some will try to steal your prescriptions, ruin your reputation, and cut off your lineage. Can you stand up and protect them? When Fang Yuan set Han Tieshan's bones, was it just by writing a prescription? What kept those forces coveting the prescriptions at bay?

The fists of the Hunyuan Sect, and the influence behind Han Tieshan.

Therefore, the martial arts test doesn't examine fancy techniques, but the purest form of martial prowess—strength, speed, reaction time, and courage—detached from the labels imposed by later generations.

To tell future generations that martial arts are not only for physical fitness, but also to let those scoundrels know

what they can and cannot mess with.

On the first day of the preliminary rounds, sixteen arenas opened simultaneously. Winners advanced, losers were eliminated—simple and direct. Disciples from all sects were eager to fight below the stage.

When Fang Yuan arrived, he was accompanied by Mu Chen, Xiao Tian, ​​and a few others. Zhao Qiming, as usual, peeked out from the back of the group. Today, Fang Yuan was wearing the standard uniform of the Hunyuan Sect: a dark blue short-sleeved shirt with tightly cinched cuffs, a two-finger-wide leather belt around his waist, and thin-soled boots.

This attire was extremely simple; there was no armor, no wrist guards, and not even any weapons—on the arena, it was all bare-handed, a contest of fists and feet.

Fang Yuan walked at a moderate pace, his gaze fixed straight ahead, yet many eyes followed his retreating figure.

"Fang Yuan's here," someone whispered from the Thousand Gold Pavilion.

Ji Mingzhao, sitting under a tea stall by the arena, put down his cup and looked up.

Beside him sat the junior brother who had been politely refused Fang Yuan's invitation yesterday, now scoffing, "Not even wearing armor, how arrogant!"

Ji Mingzhao ignored him, simply watching Fang Yuan's progress.

Fang Yuan stopped before the central arena.

The first arena battle wasn't a one-on-one fight; victory required considering one's stamina. Those present were all well-versed in medical texts, and faced with this situation, they chose to observe for the time being.

Some seasoned veterans also understood the importance of practicality and waited for this impetuous young man to step forward first.

Watching Fang Yuan reach the arena, everyone wondered what this medical genius intended to do.

"Won't I be the first one to go up?"

Fang Yuan didn't rush onto the stage. Instead, he first looked up at the blue flag on the flagpole. The flag fluttered in the wind, empty—meaning the arena was still unclaimed.

Then he went up.

His movements were extremely ordinary. There was no effortless lightness of footsteps, no flamboyant leaps of several feet. He simply lifted his foot and stepped onto the stairs, one step at a time.

Many people around stared wide-eyed as Fang Yuan climbed the steps.

With each step he took, the murmurs below subsided. When he stood in the center of the arena and turned to face the crowd, an eerie silence fell over the surrounding area.

He really went up?!

Sunlight streamed in from behind him, casting a long shadow across the blue platform.

Fang Yuan's hands hung naturally at his sides, his gaze calmly sweeping over the dense crowd below, before he spoke.

"Come on up together."

His voice wasn't loud, he didn't amplify it with internal force, yet, like Sun Sixian's at the opening ceremony, it reached the ears of everyone present clearly.

It wasn't a suggestion, not a provocation, much less a declaration of war; it was a matter-of-fact statement, a tone of habit.

Arrogant!

That was the first reaction of everyone present upon hearing this.

That nonchalant arrogance was more piercing than any desperate roar.

A moment of silence fell over the audience, then a clamor erupted like a burst dam. Disciples from various sects exchanged bewildered glances, a murmur of discussion rising and falling.

"What did he say? Attack together? Is he crazy?" Hu Xi from the Shennong Sect exclaimed, eyes wide.

Several hot-tempered disciples from Qianjinguan's side had already taken a half-step forward, only to be stopped by their senior brothers.

The disciples of the Lingshu Sect remained quiet, though their eyes held a hint of amusement. The girls from Baihua Valley reacted most directly—a junior sister with her hair in double buns covered her mouth and gasped, turning to Su Wantang: "Senior Sister, what is he doing?"

Su Wantang, sitting in the front row of the audience, her hands folded on her knees, merely smiled slightly, saying nothing.

The strangest reactions came from the top disciples of each sect.

When Ji Mingzhao of Qianjin Pavilion's gaze fell upon Fang Yuan, his brows twitched slightly. He then slowly put down his teacup, a faint smile playing on his lips.

Fang Yuanren's composure wasn't feigned; that calmness couldn't be acted out. He was either extremely arrogant and conceited, or genuinely confident.

This top pharmacologist didn't seem like the arrogant type.

Ji Mingzhao wanted to see how much real skill this pharmacologist truly possessed on the stage.

Xue Shaoyan of Qingyun Medical Hall shook his head, said "Interesting" to his junior brother beside him, then leaned back in his chair with his arms crossed, adopting a leisurely posture.

Liu Chuanping of Shennong Sect silently watched the young man on the stage for a long time, finally uttering only two words: "Impressive."

Su Wantang of Baihua Valley didn't speak, but her almond-shaped eyes never left Fang Yuan. A junior sister leaned over to say something, but she gently waved her hand to stop her.

This wasn't an ordinary provocation. All six branches of the current Yao family were present, along with several smaller sects.

Some might exaggerate and say that by the time this conference concludes, news of today's events will have spread throughout half of the Great Qian Dynasty.

None of these people showed anger.

Not because they were magnanimous, but because every top disciple present understood the same principle:

Both medicine and martial arts are paths that become increasingly difficult with each step. Mastering even one is already a remarkable achievement; to excel in both simultaneously is akin to walking a tightrope, a single misstep wasting precious years.

Fang Yuan's medical talent is already astonishing, but in martial arts, while talent is important, honing skills and time are even more indispensable.

In their eyes, the young man's appearance on the stage and uttering those three words was more a display of youthful arrogance than genuine ability.

Before the Grand Competition of Pharmacology and Talent, various sects investigated Fang Yuan's background overnight. The news brought back by their agents left every leader and elder silent.

Fang Yuan, sixteen years old, was brought to the Hunyuan Sect at the age of twelve, and has only been cultivating for four years. In those four years, his achievements in medicine are already undeniable—anesthesia powder, bone-setting techniques, medical case analysis—any one of these skills would be enough for an ordinary person to study for ten years.

But what about martial arts? He's cultivated for four years, invincible among his peers—how much truth is there in that claim? Four years is a time when even the initial stages of cultivation might not be completed. How much skill could he possibly possess?

Were those peers he defeated truly martial arts masters, or were they deliberately placed there by the Hunyuan Sect to hone his skills? These questions churned in everyone's minds, yet no one could provide a definitive answer.

But the young disciples from each family, suppressed by their masters, clearly didn't think that way.

Over at the Thousand Gold Pavilion, a tall young man suddenly stood up, quickly pushing through the crowd and striding off the stage. He was extremely robust, with broad shoulders and bulging muscles in his arms, standing like half an iron tower.

His name was Tang Zhongyu, twenty-one years old. His family owned thirteen shops in Jiangnan. His talent had been evident since childhood, and his father, with connections, had placed him in the Thousand Gold Pavilion. His martial arts talent was indeed remarkable; his cultivation had already reached the Five Organs Realm.

The martial arts technique he practiced made those with discerning eyes present nod in approval—"Iron Shirt" was not the kind of common, widely circulated version found in the martial arts world, but a secret manual personally improved by the medical patriarch, the Immortal Physician, making it an absolutely superior martial art.

The Iron Shirt technique commonly practiced in martial arts circles is harmful to the body and damages one's very essence. In later stages, it causes problems in various areas. However, the technique Tang Zhongyu practices is a rewritten version by the Immortal Physician.

The first two stages advance rapidly. Combined with a unique medicinal bath body-tempering method, it not only doesn't harm the body but also regulates the internal organs and strengthens muscles and bones.

The only drawback is the exorbitant cost—the medicinal bath requires century-old He Shou Wu (Polygonum multiflorum), sea pangolin scales, and tribute-grade dragon's blood. The cost of just one month's medicinal bath is enough to feed an ordinary family for five years.

This is the epitome of "the poor study literature, the rich practice martial arts."

But for wealthy merchants like the Tang family from Jiangnan, it's more than a drop in the ocean.

The strength of the two stages achieved through this technique is comparable to that of a body-tempering martial artist supported by the Great Qian Dynasty.

Tang Zhongyu stepped onto the platform, his footsteps making a dull thud on the bluestone surface.

He stood less than two zhang away from Fang Yuan, stretched his shoulders and neck, his bones cracking softly, then raised his fists, assuming an attack stance.

His stance was perfectly upright, shoulders relaxed, elbows dropped, his demeanor calm and composed.

The younger brothers from Qianjin Pavilion shouted especially enthusiastically,

Tang Zhongyu's name was well-known among his peers; beating a sixteen-year-old was a piece of cake.

"Senior Brother Tang, show him what real skill is!"

"Uphold our sect's prestige! Senior Brother Tang!"

Before the shouts had even faded, Tang Zhongyu moved.

His movement was all-out. There was no underestimation; even a lion uses its full strength to hunt a rabbit.

His internal energy, at the Five Viscera Realm level, surged into his legs, his feet slamming against the bluestone platform, propelling him forward like an arrow released from a bow.

His right fist, whistling through the air, aimed straight for Fang Yuan's face, while his left fist was drawn back to his ribs, poised to strike at any moment. This was his most proficient technique, the "Monument-Breaking Fist," a single punch capable of shattering a three-inch stone monument; almost none of his peers in the sect dared to take it head-on.

Fang Yuan moved.

No one saw how he moved.

Tang Zhongyu only felt a blur before his eyes—the dark blue figure vanished from his sight, not with the graceful disappearance of light footwork, but like a drop of water exploding in boiling oil.

The next instant, an overwhelming force slammed into his abdomen. The feeling wasn't like a fist hitting him, but rather like being head-on rammed by a charging rhinoceros.

His two layers of hardened skin offered no cushioning; the internal energy supporting his body was easily torn apart like a thin sheet of paper. The force pierced through flesh, fascia, and internal organs, penetrating straight to his spine.

Tang Zhongyu was sent flying.

His feet left the ground, his body contorted in mid-air like a shrimp, flying over half the ring before crashing heavily to the edge.

A mouthful of acid gushed from Tang Zhongyu's throat. He clutched his stomach, struggling to get up, but the excruciating pain in his abdomen rendered his limbs completely unresponsive.

Kneeling on the ring, veins bulging on his forehead, he gasped for breath, his mind blank.

One move.

He hadn't even seen how his opponent had made the move.

Dead silence fell over the audience.

Tang Zhongyu rushed forward, and the next second he was sent flying—the interval was so short it made one wonder if their eyes were playing tricks on them.

Someone gasped first, followed by a buzzing murmur like a sieve exploding.

"What...what was that just now?"

"Too fast, I didn't even see it clearly."

"Tang Zhongyu is at the Five Visceral Realm, right? And he's practiced Iron Shirt, yet..."

The words trailed off, because everyone witnessed the same fact—Tang Zhongyu's Iron Shirt technique was utterly useless against that young man.

Fang Yuan remained standing in the center of the arena, his posture almost unchanged, except his right fist had been retracted at some point. He hadn't even adjusted his breathing; his aura was as steady as when he first stepped onto the stage.

His gaze remained calm, devoid of the joy of defeating his opponent, only an expression of utter indifference.

“Next.”

He said.

Tang Zhongyu finally got up, clutching his stomach, his back hunched, and slowly moved off the stage. His face alternated between pale and flushed, whether from pain or something else, it was unclear. As he reached the bottom of the stage, several junior disciples from Qianjin Pavilion helped him up, and one of them whispered, “Senior brother, are you alright?”

He shook his head, sat down silently on a bench by the arena, and stared at his palms, his fingers trembling slightly.

Fang Yuan didn't wait any longer. He turned around, his gaze sweeping across the crowd below the stage. This time, his gaze was no longer calm and collected, but sharp and piercing.

Fights began simultaneously on all eight arenas, the sounds of cheers, punches, kicks, and weapons clashing rising and falling. But everyone's attention was involuntarily drawn to this particular arena, like iron filings pulled by a magnet.

The figure in dark blue robes stood on the stage, not particularly tall, even somewhat thin, yet the aura he exuded at that moment involuntarily evoked the image of a ferocious beast lurking deep in the mountains.

In the silence, another person from the Thousand Gold Pavilion rose. It wasn't Ji Mingzhao—he remained seated under the tea stall, teacup in hand, his expression unchanged. It was another junior disciple who rose, not as robust as Tang Zhongyu, but with extremely light and swift steps, clearly agile.

He walked down from the stage, removed his outer robe, revealing a tight-fitting short-sleeved shirt, and was about to step onto the steps when suddenly another person in the crowd rose simultaneously.

It was a disciple from the Qingyun Medical Pavilion, not tall, but with unusually thick arms, especially prominent knuckles, clearly indicating finger martial arts training. He and the person from the Thousand Gold Pavilion exchanged a glance, both momentarily stunned, unsure who should go first.

A soft voice came from the stage.

"No need to step aside. Come together."

Both men looked up simultaneously. Fang Yuan stood in the center of the arena, his expression obscured by the morning light, only the calm, almost cold light in his eyes was visible.

The disciple from Qianjin Pavilion gritted his teeth, while the disciple from Qingyun Medical Cottage narrowed his eyes. The next second, both leaped onto the arena, attacking Fang Yuan from the left and right.

Two muffled thuds.

Two figures flew off the arena simultaneously, one landing on the grass to the east, the other hanging on the mat to the west.

No one saw how those two punches were thrown. The speed was so fast that even the wind couldn't keep up. The sixteen flags on the arena fluttered in the wind, and on that flagpole, an unclaimed flag would eventually be planted—no, perhaps it wouldn't take that long.

Fang Yuan withdrew his fists, his sleeves fluttering slightly in the wind. He stood in the very center of the arena, like an iron stake driven into the bluestone, completely still.

The commotion in the crowd had subsided. Instead, a deeper solemnity settled in—countless eyes were fixed on the young man on stage, their gazes filled with complex emotions.

Awe? Fear? Or disbelief?

Fang Yuan glanced down at the audience for the third time; this time, he didn't even bother to say "next."

Ji Mingzhao put down his teacup. Xue Shaoyan's amusement vanished, and he slowly sat up straight. Liu Chuanping had somehow moved to the front row, arms crossed, silently gazing up at the young man on stage.

Su Wantang finally reached out and picked a dried flower, placing it on her lap. Her fingertips gently caressed the petals; the smile on her lips hadn't faded, but her eyes were much more serious than before.

The winners advanced.

The next day, facing these prodigies, she uttered those same words again.

"Come on, all at once."



Chapter 47 The Stepping Stone for the Male Protagonist of a Wuxia Story: The Holy Son 17


The next day.

The second round of the martial arts competition was held on the east side of the arena. After a day of fierce fighting, the sixteen flags had been assigned to their respective owners.

As dawn broke, the number of people in the spectator stands had increased by thirty percent compared to the previous day—the events of yesterday's arena, after a night of fermentation, had spread throughout the entire Medicine King Valley.

When Fang Yuan arrived, the other fifteen qualifiers were already standing below the stage.

He was still wearing that dark blue close-fitting outfit, a two-finger-wide leather belt around his waist, and thin-soled boots that made a light, steady sound on the bluestone ground.

As he walked through the crowd, the murmurs on both sides seemed to be cut off by a knife, all falling short by half.

Fang Yuan walked to the center of the arena, turned around, and calmly swept his gaze over the fifteen top disciples from various sects below.

Then he uttered those words again.

“Come at me all at once.”

Three words, the exact same tone as yesterday.

There was no uproar from below the stage.

A heavy silence descended. The fifteen chosen ones all looked grim, but no one uttered a word of protest, nor did any of them rush forward like Tang Zhongyu had the day before.

Ji Mingzhao slightly turned his head, withdrawing his gaze from Fang Yuan, then subtly sweeping it over the surrounding disciples.

Xue Shaoyan of Qingyun Medical Clinic stood with his arms crossed, a faint smile playing on his lips, but the smile didn't reach his eyes.

Liu Chuanping of Shennong Sect stood with his hands behind his back, his fingers clenching and unclenching.

Several junior sisters from Hundred Flowers Valley were stealing glances at Su Wantang, who simply kept her eyes lowered, lost in thought.

As Ji Mingzhao withdrew his gaze, he looked at the calm Fang Yuan before him, and only two words flashed through his mind.

Arrogance.

But what was most terrifying was that what they saw as arrogance, he himself appeared to Fang Yuan as—terrifyingly calm.

Su Wantang's thoughts were exactly the same as his.

She placed the dried flowers back into the handkerchief on her lap and looked up at the young man on the stage. His smart, tailored outfit accentuated his handsome features, and many of her junior sisters almost drooled with envy at the sight of such a dashing young man.

"With looks like that, what kind of doctor could he be?"

"He could marry a princess in Tai'an City with looks like that."

Although she wasn't like some of her junior sisters, it was inevitable to feel some admiration for someone with such outstanding appearance. But given the current situation, admiration aside, a fight was still necessary.

Over at Qingyun Medical Clinic, Xue Shaoyan suddenly chuckled, a laugh that wasn't too loud or too soft, just loud enough for everyone present to hear clearly.

"Senior Brother Fang," he spoke slowly, his tone carrying a hint of sarcasm,

"I truly admire your courage, and I truly admire your talent. You finished him off in just a few moves yesterday." He paused, his smile deepening,

"But one person against fifteen of us? Senior Brother Fang, you really don't consider us human."

Someone from the Thousand Gold Pavilion also wanted to speak, a disciple named Yan Zhuo, always quick-tongued, was about to speak—

"Enough."

A deep voice descended from the audience.

Everyone turned to see Han Baiqing, the Second Elder of Medicine King Valley, rise from the high platform and slowly walk down.

Han Baiqing was over sixty, his hair and beard half-white, but his back was as straight as a pine tree, his steps measured. He stopped at the edge of the arena, his gaze sweeping over the faces of the fifteen disciples, finally settling on Fang Yuan, pausing for a moment.

"The second round of the martial arts competition is a one-on-one duel by drawing lots," Han Baiqing began, his voice not loud, but full of energy, each word clearly reaching everyone present. "If you want to fight, wait until the third round."

Several disciples below the stage breathed a sigh of relief.

But Han Baiqing didn't finish. His tone shifted, and his slightly cloudy eyes suddenly brightened: "However—if you want to fight earlier, it's not impossible."

He glanced at the various geniuses present, his meaning clear:

The final winner will be decided among these dozen or so of you. You can fight earlier, but you must give the order yourselves.

As long as you can agree on a plan, we old guys can back down gracefully.

Those present were all top disciples carefully cultivated by their respective sects; their ability to read the room was unparalleled. Before Han Baiqing finished speaking, everyone's eyes understood the second half of his sentence.

Silence lasted for a few moments.

It's unclear who started it—perhaps Ji Mingzhao, perhaps Liu Chuanping—but the fifteen people began sizing each other up. Their gazes darted and intersected through the crowd, like the placement of pieces in a silent game of chess.

The people from Qianjin Pavilion looked at the people from Qingyun Medical Hall, the people from Qingyun Medical Hall looked at the people from Shennong Sect, the people from Shennong Sect looked at Baihua Valley, and the girls from Baihua Valley looked at Su Wantang. Su Wantang finally raised her eyes, her gaze meeting Ji Mingzhao's in mid-air.

It must be admitted.

Fang Yuan's strength is unfathomable.

They had clearly seen yesterday's matches from below the stage. Tang Zhongyu's Five Visceral Realm Iron Shirt technique was blasted two zhang away with a single punch; the two disciples who went up later were simultaneously knocked back—the speed was so fast that no one present dared to claim they could keep up.

If it were a one-on-one fight, in the second round of the draw, whoever drew Fang Yuan would be going home.

But no matter how strong Fang Yuan was, he was still alone.

The fifteen people exchanged glances, subtle nods circulating silently within the crowd. Defeating Fang Yuan, then deciding the victor—this was the most rational choice at the moment.

“We agree,” Ji Mingzhao spoke first.

“Agreed,” Liu Chuanping followed closely.

“Agreed,” Xue Shaoyan said seriously, his smile fading.

Su Wantang nodded slightly, and several junior sisters from Hundred Flowers Valley echoed her.

The fifteen people spoke in unison.

Fang Yuan stood still, not moving an inch from beginning to end. He slightly turned his head when Han Baiqing spoke—in that instant, he felt several pairs of eyes scrutinizing him.

But there was no malice.

Never mind, let's face the challenge before us first.

This is a crucial step in the plan.

Fang Yuan regained his composure, looked at Han Baiqing, nodded, and said nothing.

Han Baiqing glanced at him, a complex emotion flashing in his eyes—a mixture of admiration, regret, or perhaps neither. He turned and gestured towards the spectator stands.

"Move to another area."

On the north side of the martial arts arena was a separate area, enclosed by a low stone wall, forming a circle twenty zhang in diameter. The ground was paved with thicker granite than the arena itself, and it was said to contain embedded formations, specifically prepared for the third melee.

At this moment, the area was already packed with people—elders from various sects, disciples who hadn't been eliminated, and independent cultivators who had rushed to the scene, sitting in three or four dense circles.

As Ji Mingzhao entered the arena, his gaze swept around the perimeter. He saw the leader of the Thousand Gold Pavilion sitting in the northeast corner, conversing quietly with an elder from the Shennong Sect while holding a teacup. His uncle from the Qingyun Medical Lodge sat on the other side, looking up, his expression suggesting he had been waiting for someone.

Su Wantang saw him too.

His uncle from the Hundred Flowers Valley sat in the second row of the spectator stands, with writing brush, ink, and a stack of paper in front of him.

"Just as I thought."

The two words flashed through Ji Mingzhao and Su Wantang's minds almost simultaneously.

The elders had already discussed it. Otherwise, how could a mere second elder have such authority to arbitrarily change the rules of the martial arts competition?

This was clearly the result of prior communication between the leaders of the various sects and the Valley Master of Medicine King Valley. The only question was, who initiated this proposal? Was it pressure from the various sects, or was it Medicine King Valley's own scheme? Or perhaps—

Ji Mingzhao looked up at Fang Yuan.

The young man walked alone to the center of the arena, his dark blue robes fluttering slightly in the morning breeze.

He walked at a steady pace, just as he had yesterday when he stepped onto the stage, step by step, lacking the carefree air expected of someone his age, his composure unsettling.

At the sidelines, in the Hunyuan Sect's seats, Zhao Feixing was frantically scratching his head. He wasn't tall, and standing next to Mu Chen, he had to crane his neck to see the situation on the stage. He was currently gripping Xiao Tian's sleeve and shaking it vigorously.

"Senior Brother!" Zhao Feixing's voice was low, but couldn't hide his urgency, "How could you agree to this fighting style? He's clearly going to fight 15 against 1! This isn't—"

Xiao Tian also turned to look at Mu Chen, though he didn't speak, his eyebrows furrowed into a deep frown.

Mu Chen stood at the front, hands behind his back, his gaze falling over the railing onto the dark blue figure in the center of the arena. He didn't answer immediately, but spoke slowly.

“This suggestion came from Junior Brother,” Mu Chen said. “He told me about it.”

Zhao Feixing was stunned.

Xiao Tian was also stunned.

“What?” Zhao Feixing blinked. “Junior Brother… he suggested it himself?”

Mu Chen nodded, his gaze still fixed on Fang Yuan. What he didn’t mention was the secret meeting last night. Just after midnight, Fang Yuan knocked on his door and handed him a written letter, asking him to pass it on to the Valley Master of Medicine King Valley. Fang Yuan didn’t mince words about what was written in the letter, summarizing it in one sentence—

“The second and third rounds of the martial arts competition are combined. I request that all disciples join forces to spar with me.”

At the time, Mu Chen thought this letter would be ignored. Medicine King Valley had been holding martial arts competitions for over a hundred years, and the rules had never changed. How could the Valley Master possibly make an exception for a junior, given the ironclad rules set by the founder?

The reply came faster than expected.

Just as dawn broke, a disciple came to deliver a message that the Valley Master wished to speak with Junior Brother Fang in person.

The meeting was brief, lasting less than the time it takes for an incense stick to burn.

Mu Chen didn't know what Fang Yuan and the Valley Master discussed. He only knew that Fang Yuan emerged from the room with a calm expression.

Zhao Feixing was about to speak when Mu Chen raised his hand and placed it on his shoulder. His hand was broad and warm, like a small mountain pressing firmly on him.

"Don't worry," Mu Chen said, his tone unusually confident, "Junior Brother won't lose."

As he spoke, his gaze fell upon the dark blue figure's back. Morning light bathed Fang Yuan, outlining a thin halo around him.

Mu Chen had cultivated the *Hun Yuan Yang Sheng Jing* (Primordial Chaos Nourishing Life Scripture) for many years.

His primordial energy was unified, his form heavy and his breath light.

He thought to himself, "My junior brother is truly a prodigy!"

On the platform, the fifteen disciples had already dispersed.

"Gentlemen," Xue Shaoyan of Qingyun Medical Clinic spoke first, his voice echoing across the empty martial arts arena.

"You all witnessed what happened on the stage yesterday. Senior Brother Fang Yuan's skills are well-known; I don't need to elaborate."

He spread his hands, revealing a helpless smile. "To put it bluntly, none of us individually are a match for Senior Brother Fang."

"How about—we invite Senior Brother Fang off the stage first, and then we settle our differences based on our own abilities? What do you all think?"

No one around him nodded in agreement, nor did they object.

Silence was tacit consent.

At this moment, fifteen heroes were now vying for the attention of one person.

The solitary figure in dark blue robes in the center.

Fang Yuan stood in the very center of the arena, his feet on the rough surface of the blue granite. The morning light shone from behind him, casting a long, straight shadow in front of him.

He glanced at the fifteen figures scattered around him, some facing him head-on, some flanking him, and some flanking him from behind. Their coordination wasn't particularly refined, but as top disciples from their respective sects, they possessed basic positioning and awareness, creating space for each of them to attack and preventing them from tripping each other up.

Fang Yuan's hands remained clenched, not even in a fighting stance.

It felt like he was back at the inn that night, where everything and he were boundless.

This feeling intensified after arriving at Medicine King Valley.

But it wasn't enough.

It was still a little short.

So he had to fight this battle.

Only under sufficient pressure would that veil be torn away. Moreover, his plan required this step.

This was the reason he wrote to the Valley Master of Medicine King Valley, and also the reason he stood here.

As for why the Valley Master agreed to the trip to the back mountain of Medicine King Valley, Sun Sixian stood with his hands behind his back on the cliff edge, overlooking the tiny, dark blue figure in the training ground. The wind swept up from the valley, making his robes flutter loudly.

"A formidable young man," he murmured, then turned and left.

On the field.

"Begin!" Han Baiqing shouted.

Without any hesitation.

The fifteen people moved simultaneously.

It wasn't a chaotic rush, but rather each with their own methods and strategies.

Ji Mingzhao of Qianjin Pavilion was the first to lunge forward, his feet stepping on the pavilion's secret "Thousand Gold Steps." Each step was taken at an unusual angle, his body leaving three afterimages as he moved.
