From now on, when I go out and tell people my junior brother is the champion of Medicine King Valley, let's see who dares say our Hunyuan Sect has no one!"

Mu Jingxing glared at her, but couldn't suppress the smile on his lips. "What nonsense are you spouting? When has our Hunyuan Sect ever had no one?"

Though he said this, he knew better than anyone. The Hunyuan Sect was located in the Hengyi Mountains, with few disciples, and could only be described as mediocre. For years, they had relied entirely on disciples of Mu Chen's generation to maintain their reputation.

Just when things were starting to improve, they faced a talent shortage. But now, Fang Yuan had won the championship, and this glory was enough to make the Hunyuan Sect's name resound throughout half the martial world.

The Hunyuan Sect's revival was in sight!

...

As is customary, after the conference, participants would present their latest discoveries and achievements, exchanging ideas and insights. This was one of the most valuable parts of the Medicine King Valley Conference, a golden opportunity for countless medical disciples to learn from each other.

Fang Yuan stepped down from the stage, the seat Xiao Tian had reserved for him beside him.

He and Zhao Feixing were arguably the representatives of the Hunyuan Sect in this round.

Aside from the anesthesia, his surgery on Han Tieshan alone was enough to impress his peers.

After Zhao Feixing finished his presentation, it was time for the Hunyuan Sect's regularly maintained research project: an analysis of witchcraft and sorcery.

"Fellow practitioners," spoke the eldest disciple, Mu Chen, who had been involved in the project from the beginning and had gradually joined the research in recent years, traveling with his fellow disciples to collect samples.

"In recent years, our sect discovered a fragment of a scroll at the ruins of an ancient village deep in the Hengyi Mountains. It records some of the primitive aspects of Miao Gu techniques. After years of research and verification, we have discovered that the essence of Gu techniques shares a remarkably similar underlying logic with the 'nerve response' mechanism proposed in the *Neishen Lun* (Treatise on the Inner Spirit) from the eighteenth year of the Tai'an era."

This statement immediately sparked a low murmur of discussion from the audience.

The *Neishen Lun* from the eighteenth year of the Tai'an era is a classic of medicine, and its discussions on human bodily responses are still considered fundamental principles. However, linking it to Gu techniques was an unprecedentedly bold idea.

"Next, Junior Sister Hu will demonstrate the specific method of control."

Hu Ling then took a bamboo tube from her waist, opened the seal, and a gray-furred mouse crawled out, landing motionless in her palm.

She used a thin needle to prick several joints and the mouse's brain, transmitting internal energy through the needle, then pulled it out and placed it on a prepared seat. She took out a flute and played it, and the mouse began to move, following a specific rhythm.

The people from Medicine King Valley noticed that Hu Ling's actions resembled the snake-controlling techniques of some foreigners, but upon closer examination, the two were fundamentally different. They had already studied it; so-called snake control was merely using specific sounds to elicit a snake's reaction—the dance was simply a snake's pre-attack reaction, not true snake control.

What was being shown on stage, however, was genuine control, albeit somewhat crude, but fundamentally different.

The audience was silent, then the Medicine King Valley members led the way, erupting in thunderous applause.

Next, the people from Thousand Gold Pavilion went on stage to present.

Watching from below the stage, Fang Yuan couldn't help but sigh in his heart, "Different paths, but the same destination."

On the stage, Senior Brother Mu Chen took over, "We have compiled this method into two volumes and twelve chapters. If any fellow practitioners are interested, they are welcome to come to our sect for discussion and exchange."

For several days, the conference proceeded, with each sect presenting their discoveries and exchanging ideas.

…………

The night after the conference was exceptionally quiet.

Fang Yuan packed his belongings; he would return to the Hengyi Mountains with his sect early the next morning. He lit an oil lamp in his room and began to peruse the book *Inner God Theory*, contemplating further research.

Suddenly, he sensed an unfamiliar presence.

Fang Yuan's ears twitched. He put down the book, got up, and opened the door.

Standing outside was an elderly man with white hair, a slender figure, and a kind face. His plain robe gleamed faintly with a silvery sheen in the moonlight.

It was none other than Sun Sichuan, the Valley Master of Medicine King Valley.

"This junior greets Valley Master Sun," Fang Yuan quickly bowed.

The Valley Master of Medicine King Valley, usually so shrewd and unassuming, had suddenly come to visit. Was it because of what happened that day?

Sun Sixian waved his hand and smiled, "No need for formalities. The night is long, and I can't sleep. I'd like to ask young friend Fang to accompany me for a walk. Do you have the time?"

Fang Yuan naturally had no reason to refuse.

Sun Sixian led him through the stone paths of Medicine King Valley, winding and turning, finally arriving at a secluded medicinal garden outside the valley. The garden wasn't large, but it was filled with many rare medicinal herbs that Fang Yuan had only seen in books. Under the moonlight, the fragrance of the herbs wafted through the air, refreshing and invigorating.

"Young friend Fang," Sun Sixian stopped in front of a century-old He Shou Wu (Polygonum multiflorum), turning to look at Fang Yuan, "I won't beat around the bush. I already sensed the change in your aura during the competition."

Fang Yuan's heart stirred.

"You're only one step away from achieving innate enlightenment," Sun Sixian said, his gaze gentle yet penetrating. "That's why I agreed to your proposal to merge the civil and military examinations. Because I know that what you need isn't a competition, but an opportunity."

Fang Yuan remained silent for a moment, then bowed deeply: "Thank you for your kindness, Senior."

Sun Sixian smiled, not declining. His eyes held an indescribable appreciation for Fang Yuan, like an old craftsman seeing a rough, unpolished gem.

"I've sat in this Medicine King Valley for sixty years, and I've seen countless geniuses," Sun Sixian said slowly, "but a prodigy like you is truly rare."

Fang Yuan remained silent, standing with his hands at his sides, his expression calm and composed.

Sun Sixian, observing his reaction, grew increasingly satisfied, yet his expression remained even more casual: "Young friend Fang, I have a question for you."

"Please speak, senior."

"Have you ever considered coming to my Medicine King Valley?" Sun Sixian's tone was as casual as if he were chatting about family matters, but his words were enough to make countless people tremble.

"If you're willing to come, I'll give you the position of honorary elder. Who knows, a hundred years from now, you might even be able to sit in that position yourself."

The position of Valley Master of Medicine King Valley.

That was the pinnacle of medicine, the head of the main lineage revered by all physicians in the world. Whether in the Great Qian Dynasty court or overseas, anyone who met the Valley Master of Medicine King Valley had to respectfully invite him as an honored guest.

Regardless of status, the valley's rare and precious medicinal herbs, superior martial arts, and centuries-old renowned lineage—any one of these would be enough to drive everyone in the world mad.

Status, wealth, martial prowess, knowledge—each is something the world covets.

Now, someone has laid all of these before Fang Yuan.

Fang Yuan remained silent for a moment.

Thinking of his goals, of Mu Chen and Xiao Tian, ​​of Mu Ling's vivaciousness and cheerfulness.

A night breeze blew through the herb garden, carrying a bitter, medicinal fragrance. Moonlight shone on his face, the young man's expression calm and serene, revealing no emotion.

Finally, he shook his head.

Even without going to Medicine King Valley, I can still become a Holy Son.

"This junior thanks you for your kindness, senior," Fang Yuan's voice was not loud, but exceptionally firm, "but the Hunyuan Sect is very good. My master and fellow disciples treat me like family, and I cannot be ungrateful and turn elsewhere."

Sun Sixian looked at him, his eyes not filled with anger, but with regret, reluctance, and an indescribable sense of emotion.

“What kind of incredible luck did that kid Mu Jingxing have?” Sun Sixian shook his head, muttering to himself, “Is that wretched place, the Hengyi Mountains, some kind of feng shui treasure land? Picking up one genius is luck, but picking up two in a row, that’s not luck, that’s fate.”

When Fang Yuan heard him say “two,” he knew the other one referred to his senior brother, Mu Chen, and couldn’t help but smile slightly.

Sun Sixian sighed and patted Fang Yuan’s shoulder: “Fine. Forced things won’t be sweet, and I won’t force you.”

“By the way, there’s something I wanted to ask you, senior.”

“Speak.”

“My senior brother, Xiao Tian, ​​once said that those who break through to the Innate Realm before the age of twenty-four will be trained as the next generation of medical successors.”

Hearing this, Sun Sixian looked at Fang Yuan, meeting his eyes directly.

"You have an idea?"

Fang Yuan looked directly at Sun Sixian and nodded frankly: "Yes!"

Sun Sixian was taken aback, then burst into laughter. His laughter carried far through the quiet herb garden, startling several night birds perched in the treetops.

"Good lad!" He patted Fang Yuan's shoulder. "You're usually so quiet, I never expected you to harbor such great ambition. Good! I admire you!"

After laughing, Sun Sixian's expression gradually became serious.

"To achieve that, cultivation alone is not enough."

His voice deepened. "Each sect and school has similar rules and legends, but do you know why no one has been able to do it in the last hundred years?"

Fang Yuan shook his head slightly.

According to each sect, there are many talented disciples. If they wanted, they could pile up all sorts of rare treasures and secret techniques.

“Because each school has its own expertise and pursuits, they are all different,” Sun Sixian said, standing with his hands behind his back, the moonlight casting a long shadow. “But there is one thing they all share—the pursuit of the ‘Tao.’”

“Taoists seek immortality, Confucians seek to govern the world, Legalists seek unification, and Mohists seek universal love, non-aggression, and the virtuous.”

“But what my medical school seeks is nothing more than four words—the great physician's sincerity and skill!”

Sun Sixian turned around, his gaze fixed intently on Fang Yuan: “Your ‘talent’ has been seen by all of us, by everyone at the Medicine King Valley Assembly. But your ‘virtue,’ while present, is not enough. At least, to sit in the position of a successor of the medical school, you still have a long way to go.”

Fang Yuan remained silent for a moment, then bowed deeply: “Thank you for your understanding, elder.”

Sun Sixian looked at the young man's straight back in the moonlight, stroked his beard, and a complex emotion flashed in his eyes.

He had lived for sixty years and witnessed countless geniuses. A sixteen-year-old with innate talent, already accomplished in medicine, and unmoved by the temptation of becoming the Valley Master of Medicine King Valley—this talent, this character, was indeed the kind of successor countless sects dreamed of.

But precisely because he was too good, too good to be true.

"Extreme intelligence is bound to cause harm, and deep affection is short-lived." These eight words lingered in Sun Sixian's mind for a long time, but he ultimately didn't utter them.

If he could, wouldn't he also want the medical school, under Fang Yuan's guidance, to reach another peak, just like in the era of his ancestors? But now, handing this burden to this young man so early would be precisely what harmed him.

The world ultimately belongs to the young. What would the future hold when the baton was passed to him?

"The young phoenix's cry is clearer than the old phoenix's; the younger generation is truly formidable!"



Chapter 51 The Stepping Stone for the Male Protagonist of a Wuxia Story: The Holy Son 21


The following day, Medicine King Valley hosted a farewell banquet for the various families.

As Fang Yuan was saying goodbye to the young talents from several families, a young boy suddenly ran over and handed him a package.

"Young Master Fang, this is from the Valley Master, sent by his disciple."

Fang Yuan took the package, opened it, and found a letter and two handwritten notes inside.

The letter was written in Sun Sixian's own handwriting, the characters vigorous and powerful.

"Young friend Fang: I greatly admire your talent and character. However, the position of successor to the medical lineage has remained unheld for a century; this is not something that can be achieved overnight. You are excellent, but this path still requires further exploration."

"Two books are attached. One contains my insights into cultivation after reaching the Innate Realm, and the other contains my pharmacological understanding gleaned from decades of medical practice. Healing and saving lives is never something one person can accomplish alone. If these books can save a few more lives, it will be a small token of my appreciation."

"If you have any doubts, you are welcome to come to Medicine King Valley to explore them together. The gates of Medicine King Valley are always open to you. I hope to see you again at the upcoming conference."

While this world's cultivation path after reaching the Innate Realm is described to some extent, it is mostly vague and ambiguous. The handbook of insights passed down by Sun Si is an invaluable gift.

The other handbook is also priceless. As the current master of Medicine King Valley, his medical skills are at least among the top ten in the world, making its value immeasurable.

Especially the last sentence, which clearly showed how much he valued Fang Yuan. It was a reminder that Fang Yuan absolutely had to attend the Medicine King Valley Gathering.

Fang Yuan, holding two handbooks, bowed solemnly towards the depths of Medicine King Valley.

As dawn broke, the mountain mist gradually dissipated, revealing the layered medicinal fields and pavilions of Medicine King Valley. Fang Yuan carefully packed his bundle and turned to walk towards his senior brothers and sisters who were already waiting for him.

Xiao Tian waved to him from afar: "Junior Brother! Hurry up! Let's go home!"

Fang Yuan smiled and strode after him.

Behind him, the bells of Medicine King Valley rang out melodiously, echoing among the mountains.

At the tender age of twenty, he embarked on his cultivation journey, his fame spreading far and wide.

While resting along the way, Fang Yuan held the yellowed booklet in his hands, studying it carefully.

Sun Sixian's notes.

Xiao Tian peeked in: "Junior Brother, what are you looking at? You seem so engrossed."

"A pharmacology manual given to me by Senior Sun," Fang Yuan looked up. "It contains some of his medical theories."

"Senior Sun? The Valley Master of Medicine King Valley, Sun the Saintly!"

"Yes."

Xiao Tian advised, "Junior Brother, if you want to read Senior Sun's books, study them carefully. Senior Sun has always been fond of mentoring younger generations; don't disappoint him."

Xiao Tian wasn't surprised that Fang Yuan had obtained Sun Sichuan's books. This senior was known for his mentorship, and Fang Yuan was a genius rarely seen in decades; there was no reason he wouldn't offer assistance.

No, he probably already did.

"Hmm."

Fang Yuan didn't explain further. He turned to the next page and continued reading.

Fang Yuan hadn't finished reading the books after the Innate Realm; he had only skimmed through them.

After getting a general understanding of the later sections, he stopped studying them.

Sun Sixian wrote in his notes that the Innate Realm involves the inner circulation of Qi to perceive the outer circulation, a process of mutual understanding between man and heaven and earth.

However, people are diverse; even with the same cultivation method, the "intention" comprehended will differ from person to person.

As for the realms beyond the Innate Realm…

According to Fang Yuan's own understanding, if Qi and meridians represent enlightenment, it's like planting a seed, initially obtaining nutrients from the outside world, and beginning to grow.

The Innate Realm is like the seed developing, breaking through the soil, and further absorbing nutrients from the outside world.

Later realms require the user to develop roots, absorb nutrients, and gradually begin to grow.

According to Sun Sixian's manual, the realm after the Innate Realm is called the Grandmaster Realm, and it requires the longest accumulation time of all realms.

In Fang Yuan's understanding, at this realm, the practitioner not only needs to deeply root themselves and absorb nutrients, but also resist the storms from the outside world; if doubt arises, their realm will collapse.

Sun Sixian's original words were: "Before the Innate Realm, cultivation is about seeking inward, tempering muscles and bones, refining meridians, and condensing true Qi. After the Innate Realm, cultivation is about verifying outward, aligning the true Qi within the body with the Great Dao of Heaven and Earth. Therefore, the cultivation of physicians after the Innate Realm is often related to their own 'Spirit'."

This is the so-called "Dao," which differs from school to school, but what each school's founders pursued has already pointed out.

"The Great Physician's Sincerity, huh..."

Fang Yuan murmured to himself, his hands tracing the book in his hands.

A true teaching is contained in a single sentence, while false scriptures fill countless volumes.

After Fang Yuan finished reading the two manuals Sun Si had given him and recording them in the system data,

the auxiliary system also revealed his current predicament:

[According to the cultivation deduction of this world: The host's foundation, comprehension, and mental accumulation are all complete. What is currently lacking is not cultivation depth, but an opportunity to enter the world in accordance with one's own Dao heart and practice the true meaning of the Great Physician's Sincerity.

This opportunity is the final layer of paper to break through the barrier of realm. A single, spontaneous act, revealing one's true nature, is all it takes to complete the breakthrough.

If no external opportunity triggers it, with the host's current accumulation, simply waiting patiently and letting nature take its course will allow the advancement of realm to proceed naturally over time.]

Fang Yuan listened to the solution provided by the system in his mind.

An opportunity?

Shaking his head, he figured that while waiting for the right opportunity was possible, he might as well continue studying medicine to prepare for the future.

The word "refined" referred to mastering medical skills and diligently studying their origins.

But was simply studying medicine enough?

"Junior Brother?" Xiao Tian called out again, seeing him lost in thought.

"Senior Brother, you said…" Fang Yuan carefully chose his words, "If someone has very high medical skills but has never actually saved many people, can they be considered a 'great physician'?"

Xiao Tian hesitated. "That's a strange question. Who studies medicine without saving lives?"

"But what if… he's always studying and practicing, but has never encountered a crisis requiring his intervention?"

"What kind of great physician is that?" Xiao Tian shook his head. "At most, he's just a bookworm who's gone mad from studying."

Hearing Xiao Tian's words, Fang Yuan thought to himself that merely studying medical principles and diligently practicing medical skills was not enough.

The fundamental purpose of medical practice is to help and save lives. It requires engaging in worldly medicine, personally treating patients, and putting knowledge into practice, thereby cultivating a pure and compassionate heart and perfecting one's true nature through healing and helping others overcome suffering.

Three days later.

The group passed through Qing Shi Town.

This was an inconspicuous little town, nestled between two mountains, with only one main street running east to west.

Several disciples of the Hunyuan Sect stood at the town entrance, tasked with scouting ahead.

Seeing the convoy arrive, one of the disciples stepped forward to report, "Sect Leader, something's happened in the town ahead."

"What is it?" Mu Chen lifted the carriage curtain.

"It's...it's a plague!"

Everyone was stunned.

The word "plague" was a nightmare anywhere.

"Plague!" Xiao Tian poked his head out from behind. "How serious is it? How many people have been injured or killed?"

"I don't know." The disciple shook his head. "More than a dozen people have already died in the town, and dozens more are bedridden. Some doctors came to this village before, but they haven't made any progress in the past few days."

Mu Chen said with a grim face, "Tell me in detail."

"Yes," the disciple wiped his sweat. "We went ahead to scout the way, and when we arrived at Qing Shi Town, we found a checkpoint at the entrance, guarded by government officials, prohibiting entry and exit.

We inquired and learned that there's a plague in the town; over a dozen people have died, and dozens more are bedridden. A few itinerant doctors came a few days ago, prescribing some medicine, but it hasn't been effective."

Mu Chen frowned, turning to look at the group behind him.

The group of over seventy Hunyuan Sect disciples were mostly young men around seventeen or eighteen years old, many of them skilled in medicine. They had just returned from the Medicine King Valley Conference, full of vigor, intending to celebrate their return to the sect, but they encountered this situation on the way.

Detour?

Qing Shi Town was a necessary stop on the official road; detouring would add at least three days to the journey. But that wasn't the most important reason.

The most important reason was that they were healers.

Mu Chen looked at Fang Yuan, but before he could speak, Fang Yuan interjected, "It is not the duty of a physician to witness death, Senior Brother!"

Fang Yuan looked at Mu Chen with resolute eyes. Behind him came the voices of Zhao Feixing and the others:

"That's right. As healers, how can we stand by and watch patients die?"

Their voices weren't loud, but every word carried clearly to everyone present.

Mu Chen felt a warmth flow through his heart upon hearing this.

Mu Chen looked at his disciples, remained silent for a moment, and then spoke loudly: "Fellow disciples."

More than seventy pairs of eyes turned to him.

"You've all heard about the situation in Qing Shi Town," Mu Chen's voice wasn't loud, but it drowned out the wind in the mountains. "I was the guide on this journey, bringing you out here, and I should have brought you back safely. But now there's a plague ahead; we can avoid it by taking a three-day detour."

He paused, his gaze sweeping over the young faces.

"We are all healers. Since our sect's founding, we have used medicine to heal the world and martial arts to protect our principles."

"Today, who among you is willing to come with me to the town to save lives?"

Before the words were finished, more than seventy disciples responded in unison, "We are willing to follow our senior brother!"

The brothers were full of vigor and enthusiasm for this journey.

Mu turned and called to Fang Yuan, "Junior brother, you and I will go to the town first to scout out the situation. Junior brothers Xiao and Zhao, stay here to count the medicinal herbs and organize the number of people. We will enter the town after we have scouted the situation."

Fang Yuan nodded, exchanged a glance with his senior brother Mu Chen, and the two walked side by side towards the town.

…………

Qingshi Town was not large, with a main street running east to west. The houses on both sides were mostly made of mud walls and thatched roofs, indicating that it was not a wealthy town.

A makeshift checkpoint stood at the town entrance, with several men resembling yamen runners guarding behind the fence. Upon seeing Fang Yuan and Mu Chen approach, they immediately raised their wooden sticks in alarm.

"Who goes there? Don't come any closer!" the lead runner shouted. "There's an epidemic in the town; the government has sealed it off. Outsiders are not allowed in!"

Mu Chen stepped forward, cupping his hands in greeting, "I am Mu Chen of the Hunyuan Sect, and this is my junior brother, Fang Yuan. We passed through this area on our way back from the Medicine King Valley Conference and heard of the epidemic in your town, so we came to offer our assistance."

The runner sized them up, his expression skeptical. "Hunyuan Sect? Never heard of it. You know medicine?"

The other runner, more knowledgeable, asked, "Are you perhaps from the Hunyuan Sect, a lineage of physicians?"

"Indeed," Mu Chen replied politely. "Please inform them if there is anyone in charge in the town?"

Just as the runner was about to go inside to report, a slightly hoarse voice came from behind the checkpoint.

"Old Liu, let them in. I know them."

Fang Yuan looked in the direction of the voice and saw a man in white robes walking briskly from the town. His face was haggard, and his eyes were sunken, clearly from days of hard work. He reached the checkpoint and bowed respectfully to Fang Yuan.

"Junior Brother Fang, Senior Brother Mu, I didn't expect to run into you here."

Fang Yuan recognized the man—Xue Shaoyan from Qingyun Medicine House, the talented physician he had competed against at the Medicine King Valley Tournament. Xue Shaoyan had ranked fifth in the written exam, and his acupuncture skills were quite exquisite, leaving a good impression on Fang Yuan.

"Brother Xue?" Fang Yuan was taken aback. "What are you doing here?"

Xue Shaoyan gave a wry smile and gestured for the constables to open the gate and let the two in. "It's a long story. We had some business to attend to and returned early, arriving two days before you.

Just outside the town, we encountered several townspeople seeking medical help by the roadside. My junior brother examined them and discovered they were suffering from a strange plague. I took a few of my junior brothers into the town to investigate, only to find that seven or eight people had already died."

He led Fang Yuan and Mu Chen into the town, saying as they walked, "I immediately contacted the local government and sealed off the town to prevent the plague from spreading. But after two days of research, we still couldn't concoct a suitable medicine."

"What about your elders?" Mu Chen asked.

Xue Shaoyan sighed and said, "We left early because of some matters within our sect. Our elders are still in Medicine King Valley. As for the common people..."

"Those who could be cured have been cured." Xue Shaoyan stopped and pointed to an area on the west side of the town. "That's the isolation area for early-stage patients. I've controlled their conditions with medication. But for the middle and late-stage patients..."

He shook his head. "I'm truly helpless. If you hadn't come soon, I was going to send someone to fetch the elders from Medicine King Valley."

Fang Yuan followed his gaze. From several large houses on the west side of the town, faint, low groans could be heard, along with a strange, indescribable odor permeating the air.

"Take me to see them," Fang Yuan said.

Xue Shaoyan led the two to a makeshift clinic. The clinic was small, with five or six patients lying side-by-side, all in the middle and late stages of their illness.

Although Fang Yuan had changed into medical attire and wore a white face covering to prevent infection, he frowned as soon as he entered.

The patients all had their eyes closed, seemingly in a deep sleep. But their lips moved incessantly, emitting muffled "ooh-ooh" sounds, like something stuck in their throats, or some meaningless murmur.

"This is the most difficult part," Xue Shaoyan said in a low voice.

"All patients in the middle to late stages fall into this drowsy state. They're alright during the day, but around midnight, they start moving around erratically, as if trying to say something.

If you forcibly wake them at this time, they go berserk, extremely aggressive, and three or four people can't hold them down. But if you don't wake them, they eat voraciously, consuming the equivalent of three or four people's meals in one sitting, yet they become increasingly thin."

Fang Yuan's gaze fell on the nearest patient. He was a man in his forties, with a sallow complexion, high cheekbones, and arms that were barely visible outside the blankets, reduced to skin and bones. But his stomach was slightly swollen, as if he had eaten a lot and hadn't had time to digest.

Mu Chen reached out and took his pulse.

His pulse was erratic, sometimes fast, sometimes slow, as if something was interfering with his internal energy circulation. Even stranger, Mu Chen sensed a faint, rhythmic fluctuation within his meridians.

Mu Chen frowned and stood up, gesturing for Fang Yuan to try as well.

Fang Yuan also sensed the strange fluctuation and frowned.

Fang Yuan withdrew his hand and turned to Xue Shaoyan: “Brother Xue said the sounds they make are clearer at night?”

“Yes,” Xue Shaoyan nodded, “They start precisely around midnight and last for about an hour. I’ve been listening for two nights now, and the sound…” He paused, seemingly trying to find the right words, “is a bit like chanting scriptures, a bit like reciting incantations, indistinct, but with a very regular rhythm.”

Fang Yuan and Mu Chen exchanged a glance.

“We’ll stay here tonight,” Mu Chen said. “I want to see what exactly is causing this.”



Chapter 52 The Stepping Stone for the Male Protagonist of a Wuxia Story: The Holy Son 22


That afternoon, all seventy-odd disciples of the Hunyuan Sect entered Qing Shi Town and set up a temporary medical camp in an open area.

Mu Chen personally oversaw the operation, Zhao Feixing was responsible for allocating manpower and supplies, and Xiao Tian inventoried the medicines.

Fang Yuan, Mu Chen, and Xue Shaoyan remained in the isolation ward for terminally ill patients, awaiting the arrival of night.

After sunset, Qing Shi Town fell into an eerie silence. There were no roosters crowing, no dogs barking, no children crying; only the occasional cough and groan made the sealed-off town seem deathly still.

Fang Yuan sat cross-legged in the medical ward, closing his eyes to regulate his breathing, silently processing all the information he had gathered during the day.

Drowsiness, strange noises, madness, bulimia, weight loss, inability to distinguish between hot and cold…

Miasma? No, although the south is humid and hot, it's almost December, and there's no stagnant water nearby.

Typhoid fever doesn't seem right either. If it were typhoid, the number of patients shouldn't be so low. While there are coughs, they're mild, mostly due to fear and anxiety.

The group consisted of exceptionally skilled physicians. Xue Shaoyan was quite pleased to hear of Fang Yuan's arrival; Fang Yuan's medical skills were unparalleled among his peers. However, after examining the patients, they were still clueless.

With the symptoms incomplete, they couldn't make a decision.

Fang Yuan and the others also only had a superficial understanding of the disease. For now, they could only continue observing the patients, hoping to glean some insights from their midnight symptoms.

Night deepened.

Only an oil lamp burned in the clinic, its dim light casting flickering shadows on the walls. Mu Chen, sword in hand, leaned against the doorframe, half-asleep. Xue Shaoyan sat beside Fang Yuan, holding a medical book, clearly distracted, occasionally glancing at the water clock in the corner.

"Soon," he whispered.

As the clock struck midnight,

the patients lying in the clinic sat up simultaneously.

Not fully awake, but in a chilling, half-open state, their eyes rolled back, only the black edges of their pupils visible, gleaming eerily in the dim light.

Then their lips began to move.

At first, it was meaningless murmurs, indistinct guttural sounds, like whispers in a dream. But soon, the sounds became synchronized, as if some unseen force was directing them, causing five or six different vocal cords to emit the exact same frequency.

"Woo—woo—"

The sound wasn't loud, but it was like a sharp needle piercing deep into the eardrum. Fang Yuan felt his heart leap, involuntarily beating twice in sync with the rhythm.

He immediately circulated his inner energy to steady himself, while simultaneously pressing on the pulse of the patient next to him to check.

With Fang Yuan's extraordinary perception, in the dead of night, he faintly sensed a foreign object moving through the patient's meridians, extremely weak.

However, the reaction traveled along the meridians to the throat, causing the vocal cords to produce sound.

Fang Yuan realized something was wrong, grabbed the other patient's hand, and examined both simultaneously.

He discovered something alarming.

As the other person's voice traveled, he clearly sensed that the frequency of the vibration was attempting to resonate with his own internal energy.

Sound wave resonance?

A thought flashed through Fang Yuan's mind.

He swiftly drew silver needles from his robes and inserted them into several acupoints on the patients' throats. As the needles entered, the strange internal energy seemed to be cut off, and the patients' voices immediately weakened.

However, the other patients, as if summoned by some unseen force, simultaneously raised their voices, and the strange resonance frequency abruptly intensified.

“Senior Brother Mu Chen! Seal the vocal cords!” Fang Yuan shouted.

Hearing Fang Yuan's words, Mu Chen stepped forward, his five fingers lightly pressing against the throat of another patient. A surge of powerful internal energy flowed into the patient's body, directly sealing the meridians in their throat.

The patient trembled and fell silent.

Xue Shaoyan, hearing this, did the same, simultaneously inserting three silver needles, precisely piercing the acupoints on the throats of the remaining three patients.

The clinic was silent for a moment.

But then, an unexpected event occurred.

The patients' lips stopped moving, but their chests began to heave violently, their abdomens bulging visibly. One patient suddenly opened his eyes, which were no longer half-closed but had turned an inhuman blood red.

"Roar—"

The patient sprang from the bed, his emaciated arms unleashing disproportionate strength, tearing through the cloth binding his body and lunging at Xue Shaoyan, who was closest to him.

Xue Shaoyan reacted swiftly, dodging to the side and simultaneously striking the man on the back of the neck. The force of this strike was considerable; it should have been enough to knock a strong man unconscious on the spot.

The patient staggered a step, turned his head, and his bloodshot eyes held no human emotion, only a primal, frenzied hunger.

"Damn it..." Xue Shaoyan cursed under his breath.

Mu Chen drew his sword, slashing horizontally with the spine, striking the patient on the back of the head. The blow precisely hit the pressure point for unconsciousness, and the patient finally went limp, collapsing back onto the bed.

Fang Yuan had already pulled out paper and pen from his pocket, rapidly recording every detail he had observed—the changes in resonance frequency, the flow of true energy during the frenzy, the correspondence between the increased appetite and the swollen abdomen.

"These symptoms aren't independent," he said as he wrote, "a chain reaction."

"What?" Xue Shaoyan leaned closer.

“The excessive sleepiness is due to a foreign object inside the body. The sounds emitted at night are the foreign object influencing another person through resonance. If the transmission is forcibly blocked, the patient's internal energy will be affected, stimulating the dantian and stomach meridian, leading to madness and bulimia.” Fang Yuan raised his head, his gaze sharp and cold. “This is not an ordinary plague.”

He looked at the resonance frequency values ​​recorded on the paper in his hand, the system in his mind continuously providing analytical data.

“This is a disease that spreads through internal energy frequency. Ordinary medicine can only treat the symptoms, not the root cause. To cure it completely, we must find a way to disrupt that resonance frequency.”

Xue Shaoyan was stunned: “You mean… this disease spreads through sound?”

“Yes and no.” Fang Yuan shook his head. “The patients do indeed produce that abnormal true energy within their bodies, but they themselves are also victims. The true energy resonance is not emitted by them, but rather ‘drawn’ out. It’s like…”

He thought for a moment and gave an example: “Like…”

Mu Chen sheathed his sword and looked at Fang Yuan: “Gu!”

"You mean you're thinking about Gu magic, right?"

Fang Yuan noticed something, and Mu Chen, the senior brother who was gradually taking over the research on Gu magic, couldn't possibly miss it.

Just now, when Fang Yuan was examining the patients, Mu Chen had also used his inner energy to probe. Although Mu Chen's talent in spiritual perception wasn't as good as Fang Yuan's, his cultivation level could compensate.

Therefore, Mu Chen also sensed the abnormality in these people.

Fang Yuan didn't answer, turning to look out the window.

The night was thick and inky, the outline of Qing Shi Town faintly visible in the moonlight. Although the murmurs that rose and fell were temporarily suppressed, Fang Yuan knew that at the same time, dozens of patients in the middle to late stages of the disease were making the same sounds in the town.

And the source of the resonance was hidden in this darkness.

This pattern did indeed resemble the legendary Gu magic, but the records of the Hunyuan Sect, which had the deepest research on Gu magic, did not mention this kind of Gu.

“We can’t be certain yet,” Fang Yuan blew on the still-wet ink on the paper. “Let’s compile tonight’s data first.”

On the system panel beside him, lines of analysis results scrolled rapidly. Those complex frequency data were like guiding lights in his eyes, illuminating the path to solving this puzzle.

But that wasn’t enough.

He needed more observation, more data…

But before that,

Fang Yuan looked at Mu Chen and said formally, “Senior Brother, we can’t be certain whether this is related to Gu magic. We need to conduct further tests.”

“But, Senior Brother, you must promise me you won’t act rashly.”

If any other junior brother said this to his senior brother, the other brother would at least slap him; this guy had a deep sense of self-control.

However, Mu Chen's expression remained unchanged; he nodded, indicating he understood.

Meanwhile, Fang Yuan looked at Xue Shaoyan,

"These people..."

"They're beyond saving, aren't they?"

Fang Yuan nodded, and Mu Chen sighed. Xue Shaoyan wore an expression that said, "I knew it."

These patients, in their late stages, were already in a delirious state. Later, they couldn't even understand human speech, only knowing how to eat, behaving like animals. Although the winter temperatures here weren't freezing enough to kill someone, the rugged terrain meant that the annual harvest was mediocre, and every household was not well-off.

If Xue Shaoyan and his group hadn't wanted to keep them as samples, hoping to discover something from these late-stage patients, these patients would have long been thrown into the fire by the terrified villagers.

"Junior Brother Xue, have you checked the village's water source?"

Mu Chen spoke first, asking Xue Shaoyan if they had checked the water source in Qing Shi Village.

Many plagues are spread through contaminated water sources.

Xue Shaoyan shook his head:

"As soon as I arrived in the village, I went to look for its water source. Most villagers in Qing Shi Village rely on a single well for their livelihood, and we've checked that well; there's nothing wrong with it."

Fang Yuan shook his head, indicating that it wasn't time to jump to conclusions.

He stepped forward, took Xue Shaoyan's hand, and whispered something in his ear. Upon hearing this, Xue Shaoyan's face flashed with surprise and shock, then changed to an expression of certainty. He looked at Fang Yuan and asked, "What are the odds?"

Fang Yuan spread his index finger and thumb, forming a right angle.

"Seventy percent…"

Xue Shaoyan wasn't one to procrastinate. Finding a breakthrough now meant that every day of delay could lead to more unforeseen problems.

He nodded in agreement, indicating he would negotiate with the residents. He pointed to a patient unconscious in the corner, saying that if an autopsy was needed, they could use him first. This guy was a local thug who had been a bandit in the mountains for three years. Even after returning to the village, he wasn't quiet; a few weeks ago, he tried to kidnap a child. They had initially imprisoned him, but then a plague broke out in the village, and he was infected.

Fang Yuan nodded, and Xue Shaoyan went to negotiate with the villagers.

Mu Chen looked at Fang Yuan and asked, "Junior Brother..."

But Fang Yuan raised his hand to interrupt him, turning to him and saying, "Senior Brother, I need your help. This isn't something I can handle alone."

…………………

Hu Ning squatted by a campfire at the edge of the camp, holding a half-burnt stick of firewood, listlessly poking at the ashes in the fire.

From the moment she arrived in this village, she felt an inexplicable unease.

This feeling was hard to describe; it wasn't fear, nor tension, but rather a feeling

etched into her very being, like...like facing a venomous snake!

The survival instincts inherited from evolution made her particularly sensitive to objects that made her uncomfortable, such as long, thin creatures with exposed fangs, or food of different colors.

Thinking of this, Hu Ning seemed to realize something. Ignoring her surroundings, she sat cross-legged, her palms facing upwards. After a short while, she opened her eyes, her left hand pressed against her chest.

Just now, Hu Ning had tried to circulate their village's secret technique, the "Five Poisons Returning to Origin Technique." This technique was their village's development of Gu (poison) magic, which, under certain conditions, could accelerate cultivation.

Just now, Hu Ning had tried to circulate it. Logically, without special circumstances, this secret technique would function like an ordinary cultivation method. However, just now, when she tried to circulate it, Hu Ning felt her internal energy protesting, as if it were afraid.

It was like eating on a precipice; the slightest disturbance would mean certain death.

She endured for several hours, finally standing up as dawn approached. She brushed the dust off her skirt and headed straight for Zhao Feixing's medicine tent.

Zhao Feixing was frowning at the prescriptions spread out on the table. Hearing footsteps, he looked up, saw Hu Ning's expression, and frowned slightly: "What's wrong?"

"Senior Brother Zhao, this illness isn't right," Hu Ning said bluntly, lowering her voice. "I spent some time with several patients who had experienced the symptoms today, and it felt very much like…like a Gu poison!"

Zhao Feixing's pen paused. He remained silent for a moment, neither refuting nor immediately pressing for answers, but simply placed the pen beside the inkstone and slowly sat up straight.

"Are you sure?" His voice was deep.

“Eighty percent.” Hu Ning bit her lower lip. “I’ve never planted Gu myself, but our village’s secret techniques are closely related to Gu.”

Afraid Zhao Feixing wouldn’t believe her, Hu Ning truthfully recounted what she had just learned about the technique.

Zhao Feixing’s brows furrowed even more. It wasn’t that he didn’t believe Hu Ning’s assessment; quite the opposite, it was precisely because he knew Hu Ning’s background and her talent in Gu witchcraft that he valued this statement even more.

But the problem is, if it really is a Gu poison, then the nature of the matter completely changes.

A plague is a natural disaster. A Gu poison is a man-made calamity.

“Don’t make a fuss yet,” Zhao Feixing finally said. “Our senior brothers are still observing him; we’ll draw a conclusion after he comes out. If you speak now, it will only make our junior brothers and sisters panic.”

As dawn broke, Mu Chen and Fang Yuan walked out of the late-stage isolation zone one after the other. Both their steps were heavy. Fang Yuan clutched a stack of papers covered in writing, while Mu Chen held his sword. Their expressions were unreadable, but both were weary.



Chapter 53 The Stepping Stone of the Martial Arts World: The Holy Son 23


Several people gathered in the medicine tent, and Hu Ning recounted her observations again.

No one interrupted her; they listened quietly until Hu Ning finished, then he unfolded the stack of papers in his hand.

“Hu Ning is right,” Fang Yuan said, pointing to the densely packed records on the papers. “These patients do indeed have an abnormal fluctuation within their bodies. This fluctuation peaks at 11:45 AM, driving the vocal cords to produce a specific frequency of sound through the throat meridians. This frequency resonates with the internal energy of others around them. In other words, it’s ‘infecting’ normal people.”

He paused, then looked up at Zhao Feixing and Hu Ning: “This is no longer a simple plague.

Last night we tried to stop it, but the abnormal internal energy within their bodies wasn’t released; instead, it flowed back into their dantian and stomach meridians, directly triggering madness and gluttony. This shows that the strange energy within the patients is ‘alive’—it consciously resists external intervention.”

“A Gu worm,” Hu Ning added confidently.

Fang Yuan didn't deny it. Mu Chen, however, placed his sword on the table and spoke, "My feeling is the same as Junior Brother Fang's. Although that strange energy was weak, its movement through the meridians wasn't random; it seemed to follow a fixed, cyclical path. This highly matches the characteristics of Gu worms circulating with the blood and qi in witchcraft."

Zhao Feixing listened in silence for a long time. As the person in charge of coordinating the overall situation, he had to consider not only the illness itself but also the subsequent chain reaction—if it was Gu, who cast it? What was their purpose? Were there any other potential threats to Qing Shi Town?

But no one could answer these questions now.

Mu Chen didn't give him much time to think. He directly stated his plan: "The current situation is beyond our control. This isn't a problem we can solve; we need an elder with in-depth knowledge of witchcraft to intervene. I will immediately use my magic to go to Medicine King Valley and seek assistance from the seniors."

Fang Yuan continued, "Xue Shaoyan and I have discussed it; we'll stabilize the situation here for now. As for the late-stage patients..." He paused, his voice lowering, "We've done what we could. We'll decide on the rest when the seniors arrive."

The words "late-stage patients" caused a moment of silence in the tent. Everyone understood the meaning behind those words—those patients who had completely lost their minds, like walking corpses.

If it was witchcraft, even if the seniors from Medicine King Valley arrived, they would likely be powerless to save those patients.

Hu Ning clenched her fists and looked away.

Coming from a Miao village, she hated nothing more than people using Gu magic to cause trouble.

Zhao Feixing took a deep breath and nodded: "Alright. Senior Brother, you go to Medicine King Valley. I'll arrange the supplies and manpower here. You all rest for a day and set off early tomorrow morning."

That night, he changed into a dark-colored outfit, carrying only a sword and a few healing pills, and quietly left Qing Shi Town. The night was thick, the moonlight completely obscured by thick clouds, and the bare branches of the trees on both sides of the mountain path rustled in the night wind.

Mu Chen's feet never stopped, his figure like a flowing shadow sweeping across the mountain path, the Hunyuan Sect's movement techniques displayed to their fullest extent.

He concentrated his true energy, moving with the speed of a feather.

Fang Yuan's earlier warning still echoed in his ears.

But the current situation left him no room for complacency.

With Mu Chen's stamina, a full-speed trip to Medicine King Valley to find the people and back would take about half a day. Normally, when traveling, he had to take care of his junior brothers and sisters, and on some rugged terrain, he also had to prevent the medicines they were carrying from colliding, which was why their progress was so slow.

Hopefully, nothing unexpected would happen…

Mu Chen thought to himself, recalling his conversation with Fang Yuan.

About twenty miles from the town, the mountain road rounded a bend, leading to a dense forest. Just as Mu Chen was about to speed up and pass through, suddenly, an extremely faint fluctuation of energy emanated from the treetops on his left.

The fluctuation was so faint it was almost an illusion, but Mu Chen possessed exceptional perception, and years of chivalrous deeds had ingrained his ability to sense killing intent into his instincts.

His body moved faster than his mind. He parried with his sword sheath, his figure shifting three feet to the right. A streak of dark light grazed his ear and embedded itself in a pine tree behind him—a poisoned hidden arrow.

“Who!”

A tall figure in black robes emerged from the treetop.

…………

Meanwhile, outside the camp in Qing Shi Town, a cluster of flames flickered in the night wind.

“Wandering souls, wandering souls, listen closely, go east to Penglai Island, south to Zhuling Palace, west to the Vajra Land, north to escape the bitter cold, hear the sutra in the Northern Palace, hear the repentance in the Southern Palace. Relying on the power of the Dao, for the best cause, sincerely recite, and you will be reborn in the Heavenly Venerable, with inconceivable merit.”

Fang Yuan stood before the ashes, his hands forming a mudra, and softly recited the *Scripture of Salvation*.

The terminally ill patients in the town, who had completely lost their minds, were beyond saving; further delay would only increase the risk of infection for others.

They were already dead. After being informed of the risks, many chose to let the dead give way to the living.

Living meant enduring, enduring the happiness and suffering that reality presented.

Fang Yuan personally took action.

He used an extremely gentle method—inserting silver needles into the patients' acupoints to induce sleep, allowing them to pass away peacefully in their slumber. There was no pain, no struggle; those faces, emaciated by illness, finally regained their peace at the last moment.

This was the last thing Fang Yuan could do for them.

“…Relying on the power of the Dao, for the best cause, with sincere devotion, may you be reborn in the Heavenly Venerable, with inconceivable merit.”

Just like Mu Jingxing back then.

After reciting the last sentence, Fang Yuan turned and walked towards the village.

He was going to verify something…

When he reached the old locust tree at the village entrance, Fang Yuan suddenly stopped.

The night was too quiet. So quiet that his instincts immediately went off. Without making a sound, he shifted his weight to his back foot, his right hand discreetly pressing against the silver needle hidden in his sleeve. Then he whirled around, shouting sharply, "Who's there!"

A person emerged from behind the tree.

Xue Shaoyan carried a lantern in one hand and a tray in the other, a slightly embarrassed smile on his face. "It's me, it's me. Don't be nervous."

Fang Yuan recognized him and relaxed his stance. "What are you doing here so late at night?"

"I was asked by the villagers to come and see you." Xue Shaoyan stepped forward and placed the tray on the stone table under the old locust tree.

On the tray lay a roast chicken, two flatbreads, and a small bottle of wine. The bottle was made of rough earthenware, its mouth sealed with red cloth, clearly homemade rice wine from a local farmer. Next to it sat an exquisite celadon wine pot, engraved with the emblem of the Hunyuan Sect.

“This chicken is from Aunt Wang’s house at the east end of the village, and the flatbreads were made by Aunt Li. This wine—” Xue Shaoyan patted the celadon wine pot, “is my own treasured brew, a medicinal wine made according to our sect’s recipe.”

“These foods are from the village to thank you for your help, and also gifts for them.”

As he spoke, Xue Shaoyan looked towards the place where Shuangyun had taken away the critically ill patients.

Because although the exact nature of the disease was still unclear, its contagiousness was certain. The families could only come to see the patients briefly when they were taken away; the cremation and final rites still required Fang Yuan's intervention.

"It's normal for people to give gifts at funerals; they even host a meal and give two copper coins. They've been busy helping out, so everyone just chips in and gives a small gift."

"This wine is a gift from me. Your arrival has relieved us of what we've been struggling with all day, and I apologize for my rudeness earlier."

Fang Yuan looked at the tray, then at Xue Shaoyan. The other man's face was full of sincerity, even a little reserved, as if afraid Fang Yuan wouldn't accept it.

"Thanks." Fang Yuan sat down at the stone table, picked up a flatbread, and took a bite.

He was indeed hungry; he finished half a flatbread in a few bites and then tore off a chicken leg.

Fang Yuan ate with considerable gusto, but he didn't touch the medicinal wine at all.

Xue Shaoyan didn't mind either, pouring himself a cup and downing it in one gulp. Then he poured himself another cup and drank that too. After a few cups, he started talking non-stop.

"Junior Brother Fang, you know, sometimes I really envy you." Xue Shaoyan held his wine cup, his eyes slightly unfocused.

"Among our generation, in terms of talent and cultivation, you're number one. You single-handedly took on 15 people, suppressing your peers—I admire that! In terms of pharmacology, you're even more amazing. As for me? I barely squeezed into fifth."

He took a sip of wine and continued, "This time with the plague in Qing Shi Town, I stayed here for four or five days, scouring medical books and asking all my fellow disciples, but I still couldn't find a breakthrough. You arrived on the second day and figured out the cause and the transmission pattern. Tell me, how can the difference between people be so vast?"

Fang Yuan chewed on his flatbread, remaining silent. He could tell that Xue Shaoyan's words weren't just polite formalities or sarcasm, but rather genuine emotions revealed after drinking.

He, being a blockhead, truly didn't know how to comfort him.

"Senior brother, you're too modest," Fang Yuan swallowed the last bite of his flatbread. "The diagnosis of this disease wasn't achieved by one person alone. You sealed off the town's distribution beforehand, preserved samples from late-stage patients, and investigated the water source—these were the crucial foundations. Without them, I would have been completely lost."

Xue Shaoyan looked at Fang Yuan, picked up his wine glass, poured himself a drink, then took a sip, gesturing to Fang Yuan with the bottle.

Seeing this, Fang Yuan reluctantly picked up his glass and took a small sip as well.

At this, Xue Shaoyan chuckled and drank another glass.

The pot of medicinal wine was more than half empty. His cheeks flushed, and his speech became slurred: "You, you always know how to talk. It's clearly your skill that's impressive, but you insist on claiming it's everyone's achievement. The more you do that, the more envious I become."

"Senior Brother Xue, you're a little drunk," Fang Yuan reminded Xue Shaoyan.

The other seemed oblivious, continuing to mutter to himself:

"Envy turns to jealousy."

He stood up, swaying as he walked to Fang Yuan's side, placing a hand on Fang Yuan's shoulder. The mingled scents of alcohol and medicine wafted from his breath, warmly brushing against the back of Fang Yuan's neck.

Fang Yuan's body tensed instantly.

Not because of the content of the words, but because his senses caught an extremely subtle detail—the five fingers of Xue Shaoyan's hand on his shoulder were trembling slightly.

Not the trembling of someone drunk, but a rhythmic, regular contraction.

This frequency…

It's the resonance frequency of the abnormal internal energy backlash experienced by the terminally ill patients in the clinic after their throat meridians were severed.

Fang Yuan: !!!

Fang Yuan abruptly turned his head to look at Xue Shaoyan's face. The other man's head was lowered, his lips moving slightly, as if in prayer, or perhaps mechanically.

Xue Shaoyan slowly raised his head.

His eyes were unfocused, empty voids, pupils rolled back, the whites of his eyes occupying most of their sockets, revealing only a small, dark edge.

In the dim lantern light, those eyes didn't reflect Fang Yuan's face, but rather a hollow, inhuman glow.

"Junior Brother Fang, is the wine good?"

Fang Yuan took a small sip of the wine Xue Shaoyan offered him.

His pupils suddenly contracted. He tried to get up, but found his limbs felt as if their bones had been removed. A violent weakness surged from deep within his dantian, instantly spreading throughout his body.

Fang Yuan's body slid off the stone bench, kneeling on one knee, one hand desperately supporting himself to keep from falling. His vision began to blur, but his hearing became unusually sharp. He heard a faint hissing sound coming from the withered tree to his right.

A jet-black snake emerged from a hole at the base of a withered tree. Its body snaked upwards along the trunk, its triangular head revealing two dark red eyes fixed intently on Fang Yuan. Its forked tongue flickered rapidly, emitting a sickening hiss.

No—this wasn't a wild snake.

Fang Yuan and his disciples carried special insect repellent powder; ordinary snakes wouldn't even come within ten paces of them.

The black snake suddenly sprang from the tree trunk like a black arrow, aimed straight for Fang Yuan's throat. Its fangs reflected two eerie green points in the dim lantern light, its speed too fast for anyone to react.

Watching this, Xue Shaoyan's originally handsome face twisted into a sinister smile. His lips moved faster and faster, a muffled, high-pitched sound emanating from deep within his throat, like someone scraping glass with fingernails.

“Stay, Junior Brother Fang… You’re so powerful, stay and keep me company.”

At the critical moment, a white figure swooped down from the night sky.

Its speed was so great that only a blur remained.

It was a bird—pure white, plump like a round cotton ball, looking utterly endearing and bearing no resemblance to the word "fierce." Yet this excessively plump white bird, with unbelievable precision, grabbed a withered branch with one claw, hung from it, and swung, its round body arcing gracefully, perfectly positioned in front of Fang Yuan.

The black snake's venomous fangs bit down hard on the white bird's fluffy breast.

A crisp "crack" rang out.

Beneath the bird's fluffy feathers lay solid flesh; the instant the snake's fangs bit in, the white bird lowered its head and pecked at the snake's head. The peck was lightning fast, precise as if measured with a ruler—hitting the snake's vital spot.

The black snake shuddered, its body loosening its coils on the withered branch, falling to the ground with a thud like a broken rope, twitching twice before becoming still.

The white bird shook the feathers on its chest, completely unharmed. It tilted its head and looked at Fang Yuan with its tiny black eyes.

A clear voice rang in Fang Yuan's mind.

"System 120, mission complete!"



Chapter 54 The Stepping Stone of the Martial Arts World: The Holy Son 24


During the autopsy of the critically ill patient that day, both Fang Yuan and Mu Chen sensed something was amiss.

Anyone who had tried it would know this wasn't something one or two disciples could handle.

Something was wrong, very wrong!

Just as Fang Yuan was considering whether to rush to find the senior from Medicine King Valley that very night,

System 120 returned from its part-time job!

After learning of Fang Yuan's current predicament, System 120 proposed a plan to turn the tables.

The two went along with it, aiming to uncover the mastermind.

However, Fang Yuan said that while the plan was good, the risk was too high.

This person was only three days' journey from Qing Shi Village to Medicine King Valley. A Qi Meridian expert could arrive in half a day at full speed. Anyone who dared to cause trouble here was no ordinary person.

Even if Fang Yuan broke through to the Innate Realm, he couldn't claim he could easily capture the mastermind. Fang Yuan didn't want to gamble with the lives of his fellow disciples.

System 120 was, of course, aware of the danger involved; he wasn't just talking without understanding the risks.

Don't forget why System 120 entered the main space in the first place!

Safety, safety, and above all, safety!

"Host, I understand your concerns..."

System 120's chubby body turned slightly, continuing, "But do you think I would so recklessly propose this method?"

Indeed, System 120 wasn't the kind of system to propose something so impulsive, disregarding their opinions.

He definitely had some trump card that Fang Yuan didn't know about.

"Hmph, not bad, Host, the reason I came back so late this time is because of this!"

As soon as he finished speaking, the small circle of System 120 in Fang Yuan's consciousness space suddenly glowed, and the surface broke open,

revealing...!

A chubby, white—bird!?

System 120 displayed its form, saying, "How about it? Isn't it beautiful, host? This is a divine beast I carefully selected."

System 120 then explained to Fang Yuan that his friend's part-time job had run into some problems, causing a significant delay. As compensation, he had increased the pay.

Furthermore, in their world, as Fang Yuan's cultivation level continued to rise, the system also began to improve, resulting in more replenished essence.

In other words, System 120 and Fang Yuan could be said to have initially escaped the poverty of their early entrepreneurial days!

Congratulations!

Fang Yuan: (◦˙▽˙◦)

What does this have to do with this fat bird?

System 120 explained that although they were just emerging from poverty, their status was already quite high. Now that they had the resources, they could better assist their host.

And this materialized divine beast was a manifestation of its evolution.

System 120 explained that ordinary systems can assist their hosts in various mission worlds, but often through special means of influence; the world's rules forbid them from direct intervention.

Therefore, in many missions, the vast majority of the tasks still rely on the host's own abilities to complete.

However!

Due to their rank, System 120's role has been elevated, granting them greater authority and scope of activity.

System 120 projected its consciousness, directly influencing the world.

Hearing this, Fang Yuan was also surprised.

So amazing?!

"Then, 120, what can you do for me now?"

Upon hearing this, System 120's white bird showed a proud expression.

Fang Yuan looked at him expectantly.

"Anything is fine."

"Oh!"

"Hmph, he can do anything he says he can do!"

"What exactly is it?"

System 120 gave a wicked smile (though it's unclear why a bird's face would show such an expression, that's the feeling └｜゜ε゜｜┐)

"Including running errands, helping in fights, scouting, killing time, and providing emotional value through cuteness."

Fang Yuan: "(￣(エ)￣)ゞ

Seems quite useful, but also seems not very useful.

Back to the main point, System 120 stated that although his combat strength is currently low, his mobility is extremely high.

The host believes that they alone cannot defeat the mastermind, so he can help as a messenger.

In short, he can help the Yao people.
